Then the bear laugh beneath the table and mutter to itself .
And the prince continue : ' I be tire to death .
Order some soup to be make for me , but I do n't want that bear to meddle with it .
Every time I speak of my love the brute mutter and laugh , and seem to mock at me .
I hate the sight of the creature ! '
When the soup be ready , the bear bring it to the prince ; but before hand it to him , she drop into the plate the ring the prince have give her the night before at the ball .
The prince begin to eat his soup very slowly and languidly , for he be sad at heart , and all his thought be busy , wonder how and where he could see the lovely stranger again .
Suddenly he notice the ring at the bottom of the plate .
In a moment he recognise it , and be dumb with surprise .
Then he saw the bear standing beside him , look at him with gentle , beseech eye , and something in the eye of the bear make him say : ` Take off that skin , some mystery be hidden beneath it . '
And the bear 's skin drop off , and the beautiful girl stand before him , in the dress weave out of the starlight , and he saw that she be the stranger with whom he have fall so deeply in love .
And now she appear to him a thousand times more beautiful than ever , and he lead her to his mother .
And the princess tell them her story , and how she have be keep shut up by her father in his palace , and how she have weary of her imprisonment .
And the prince 's mother love her , and rejoice that her son should have so good and beautiful a wife .
So they be marry , and live happily for many year , and reign wisely over their kingdom .
THE SUNCHILD Once there be a woman who have no child , and this make her very unhappy .
So she speak one day to the Sunball , say : ` Dear Sunball , send me only a little girl now , and when she be twelve year old you may take her back again . '
So soon after this the Sunball send her a little girl , whom the woman call Letiko , and watch over with great care till she be twelve year old .
Soon after that , while Letiko be away one day gather herb , the Sunball come to her , and say : ` Letiko , when you go home , tell your mother that she must bethink herself of what she promise me . '
Then Letiko go straight home , and say to her mother : ` While I be gather herb a fine tall gentleman come to me and charge me to tell you that you should remember what you promise him . '
When the woman hear that she be sore afraid , and immediately shut all the door and window of the house , stop up all the chink and hole , and keep Letiko hide away , that the Sunball should not come and take her away .
But she forget to close up the keyhole , and through it the Sunball send a ray into the house , which take hold of the little girl and carry her away to him .
One day , the Sunball have send her to the straw shed to fetch straw , the girl sit down on the pile of straw and bemoan herself , save : ` As sigh this straw under my foot so sighs my heart after my mother . '
And this cause her to be so long away that the Sunball ask her , when she come back : ` Eh , Letiko , where have you be so long ? '
She answer : ` My slipper be too big , and I could not go faster . '
Then the Sunball make the slipper shorter .
Another time he send her to fetch water , and when she come to the spring , she sit down and lamented , say : ` As flow the water even so flows my heart with longing for my mother . '
Thus she again remain so long away that the Sunball ask her : ` Eh , Letiko , why have you remain so long away ? '
And she answer : ` My petticoat be too long and hinders me in walk . '
Then the Sunball cut her petticoat to make it short .
Another time the Sunball send her to bring him a pair of sandal , and a the girl carry these in her hand she begin to lament , say : ` As creak the leather so creaks my heart after my little mother . '
When she come home the Sunball ask her again : ` Eh , Letiko , why do you come home so late ? '
` My red hood be too wide , and fall over my eye , therefore I could not go fast . '
Then he make the hood narrower .
At last , however , the Sunball become aware how sad Letiko be .
He send her a second time to bring straw , and , slip in after her , he hear how she lament for her mother .
Then he go home , call two fox to him , and say : ` Will you take Letiko home ? '
` Yes , why not ? '
` But what will you eat and drink if you should become hungry and thirsty by the way ? '
` We will eat her flesh and drink her blood . '
When the Sunball heard that , he say : ` You be not suit for this affair . '
Then he send them away , and call two hare to him , and say : ` Will you take Letiko home to her mother ? '
` Yes , why not ? '
` What will you eat and drink if you should become hungry and thirsty by the way ? '
` We will eat grass and drink from streamlet . '
` Then take her , and bring her home . '
Then the hare set out , take Letiko with them , and because it be a long way to her home they become hungry by the way .
Then they say to the little girl : ` Climb this tree , dear Letiko , and remain there till we have finish eating . '
So Letiko climb the tree , and the hare go graze .
It be not very long , however , before a lamia come under the tree and call out : ` Letiko , Letiko , come down and see what beautiful shoe I have on . '
` Oh !
my shoe be much fine than yours . '
` Come down .
I be in a hurry , for my house be not yet sweep . '
` Go home and sweep it then , and come back when you be ready . '
Then the lamia go away and sweep her house , and when she be ready she come back and call out : ` Letiko , Letiko , come down and see what a beautiful apron I have . '

thou bird of ill-omen !

THE DAUGHTER OF BUK ETTEMSUCH Once upon a time there live a man who have seven daughter .
For a long time they dwell quite happily at home together , then one morning the father call them all before him and say : ` Your mother and I be go on a journey , and a we do not know how long we may be away , you will find enough provision in the house to last you three year .
But see you do not open the door to any one till we come home again . '
` Very well , dear father , ' reply the girl .
For two year they never leave the house or unlock the door ; but one day , when they have wash their clothes , and be spread them out on the roof to dry , the girl look down into the street where people be walk to and fro , and across to the market , with it stall of fresh meat , vegetable , and other nice thing .
` Come here , ' cry one .
` It make me quite hungry !
Why should not we have our share ?
Let one of u go to the market , and buy meat and vegetable . '
` Oh , we must n't do that ! '
say the young .
` You know our father forbid u to open the door till he come home again . '
Then the eldest sister sprang at her and strike her , the second spit at her , the third abuse her , the fourth push her , the fifth fling her to the ground , and the sixth tore her clothes .
Then they leave her lie on the floor , and go out with a basket .
In about an hour they come back with the basket full of meat and vegetable , which they put in a pot , and set on the fire , quite forget that the house door stand wide open .
The young sister , however , take no part in all this , and when dinner be ready and the table laid , she steal softly out to the entrance hall , and hide herself behind a great cask which stand in one corner .
Now , while the other sister be enjoy their feast , a witch pass by , and catch sight of the open door , she walk in .
She go up to the eldest girl , and say : ` Where shall I begin on you , you fat bolster ? '
` You must begin , ' answer she ` with the hand which strike my little sister . '
So the witch gobble her up , and when the last scrap have disappear , she come to the second and ask : ` Where shall I begin on you , my fat bolster ? '
And the second answered , ` You must begin on my mouth , which spat on my sister . '
And so on to the rest ; and very soon the whole six have disappear .
And a the witch be eat the last mouthful of the last sister , the young , who have be crouch , frozen with horror , behind the barrel , run out through the open door into the street .
Without look behind her , she hasten on and on , a fast a her foot would carry her , till she saw an ogre 's castle standing in front of her .
In a corner near the door she spy a large pot , and she creep softly up to it and pull the cover over it , and go to sleep .
By-and-by the ogre come home .
` Fee , Fo , Fum , ' cry he , ' I smell the smell of a man .
What ill fate have bring him here ? '
And he look through all the room , and find nobody .
` Where be you ? '
he call .
` Do not be afraid , I will do you no harm . '
But the girl be still silent .
` Come out , I tell you , ' repeat the ogre .
` Your life be quite safe .
If you be an old man , you shall be my father .
If you be a boy , you shall be my son .
If your year be as many a mine , you shall be my brother .
If you be an old woman , you shall be my mother .
If you be a young one , you shall be my daughter .
If you be middle-aged , you shall be my wife .
So come out , and fear nothing . '
Then the maiden come out of her hiding-place , and stand before him .
-LSB- Illustration : The Maiden creep out of the Pot . -RSB-
` Fear nothing , ' say the ogre again ; and when he go away to hunt he leave her to look after the house .
In the evening he return , bring with him hare , partridge , and gazelle , for the girl 's supper ; for himself he only care for the flesh of men , which she cook for him .
He also give into her charge the key of six room , but the key of the seventh he keep himself .
And time pass on , and the girl and the ogre still live together .
She call him ` Father , ' and he call her ` Daughter , ' and never once do he speak roughly to her .
One day the maiden say to him , ` Father , give me the key of the upper chamber . '
` No , my daughter , ' reply the ogre .
` There be nothing there that be any use to you . '
` But I want the key , ' she repeat again .
However the ogre take no notice , and pretend not to hear .
The girl begin to cry , and say to herself : ` To-night , when he think I be asleep , I will watch and see where he hide it ' ; and after she and the ogre have sup , she bid him good-night , and leave the room .
In a few minute she steal quietly back , and watch from behind a curtain .
In a little while she saw the ogre take the key from his pocket , and hide it in a hole in the ground before he go to bed .
And when all be still she take out the key , and go back to the house .
The next morning the ogre awoke with the first ray of light , and the first thing he do be to look for the key .
It be go , and he guess at once what have become of it .
But instead of get into a great rage , a most ogre would have do , he say to himself , ` If I wake the maiden up I shall only frighten her .
For to-day she shall keep the key , and when I return to-night it will be time enough to take it from her . '
So he go off to hunt .
The moment he be safe out of the way , the girl run upstairs and open the door of the room , which be quite bare .
The one window be close , and she throw back the lattice and look out .
Beneath lay a garden which belong to the Prince , and in the garden be an ox , who be draw up water from the well all by himself -- for there be nobody to be see anywhere .
The ox raise his head at the noise the girl make in open the lattice , and say to her , ` Good morning , O daughter of Buk Ettemsuch !
Your father be feed you up till you be nice and fat , and then he will put you on a spit and cook you . '
These word so frighten the maiden that she burst into tear and run out of the room .
All day she weep , and when the ogre come home at night , no supper be ready for him .
` What be you cry for ? '
say he .
` Where be my supper , and be it you who have open the upper chamber ? '
` Yes , I open it , ' answer she .
` And what do the ox say to you ? '
` He say , `` Good morning , O daughter of Buk Ettemsuch .
Your father be feed you up till you be nice and fat , and then he will put you on a spit and cook you . '' '
` Well , to-morrow you can go to the window and say , `` My father be feed me up till I be nice and fat , but he do not mean to eat me .
If I have one of your eye I would use it for a mirror , and look at myself before and behind ; and your girth should be loosen , and you should be blind -- seven day and seven night . '' '
` All right , ' reply the girl , and the next morning , when the ox speak to her , she answer him a she have be tell , and he fell down straight upon the ground , and lay there seven day and seven night .
But the flower in the garden wither , for there be no one to water them .
When the prince come into his garden he find nothing but yellow stalk ; in the midst of them the ox be lie .
With a blow from his sword he kill the animal , and , turn to his attendant , he say , ` Go and fetch another ox ! '
And they bring in a great beast , and he draw the water out of the well , and the flower revive , and the grass grow green again .
Then the prince call his attendant and go away .
The next morning the girl hear the noise of the water-wheel , and she open the lattice and look out of the window .
` Good morning , O daughter of Buk Ettemsuch ! '
say the new ox .

And the maiden answer : ` My father be feed me up till I be nice and fat , but he do not mean to eat me .
If I have one of your eye I would use it for a mirror , and look at myself before and behind ; and your girth should be loosen , and you should be blind -- seven day and seven night . '
Directly she utter these word the ox fell to the ground and lay there , seven day and seven night .
Then he arise and begin to draw the water from the well .
He have only turn the wheel once or twice , when the prince take it into his head to visit his garden and see how the new ox be get on .
When he enter the ox be work busily ; but in spite of that the flower and grass be dry up .
And the prince draw his sword , and rush at the ox to slay him , a he have do the other .
But the ox fell on his knee and say : ` My lord , only spare my life , and let me tell you how it happen . '
` How what happen ? '
ask the prince .
` My lord , a girl look out of that window and speak a few word to me , and I fell to the ground .
For seven day and seven night I lay there , unable to move .
But , O my lord , it be not give to u twice to behold beauty such a hers . '

And the prince , from his hiding-place , hear her word , and he jump up and run to her and say , ` By the head of Buk Ettemsuch , speak to me . '
So she speak to him , and they live happily to the end of their day , because the girl keep the promise she have make to the ogre .

LAUGHING EYE AND WEEPING EYE , OR THE LIMPING FOX -LRB- SERVIAN STORY -RRB- Once upon a time there live a man whose right eye always smile , and whose leave eye always cry ; and this man have three son , two of them very clever , and the third very stupid .
Now these three son be very curious about the peculiarity of their father 's eye , and a they could not puzzle out the reason for themselves , they determine to ask their father why he do not have eye like other people .
So the eldest of the three go one day into his father 's room and put the question straight out ; but , instead of answer , the man fly into a fearful rage , and sprang at him with a knife .
The young fellow run away in a terrible fright , and take refuge with his brother , who be await anxiously the result of the interview .
` You have good go yourselves , ' be all the reply they get , ` and see if you will fare any good . '
Upon hear this , the second son enter his father 's room , only to be treat in the same manner a his brother ; and back he come tell the young , the fool of the family , that it be his turn to try his luck .
Then the young son march boldly up to his father and say to him , ` My brother would not let me know what answer you have give to their question .
But now , do tell me why your right eye always laugh and your left eye always weeps . '
As before , the father grow purple with fury , and rush forward with his knife .
But the simpleton do not stir a step ; he know that he have really nothing to fear from his father .
` Ah , now I see who be my true son , ' exclaim the old man ; ` the others be mere coward .
And a you have show me that you be brave , I will satisfy your curiosity .
My right eye laugh because I be glad to have a son like you ; my leave eye weeps because a precious treasure have be steal from me .
I have in my garden a vine that yield a tun of wine every hour -- someone have manage to steal it , so I weep it loss . '
The simpleton return to his brother and tell them of their father 's loss , and they all make up their mind to set out at once in search of the vine .
They travel together till they come to some cross road , and there they part , the two elder one take one road , and the simpleton the other .
` Thank goodness we have get rid of that idiot , ' exclaim the two elder .
` Now let u have some breakfast . '
And they sit down by the roadside and begin to eat .
They have only half finish , when a lame fox come out of a wood and beg them to give him something to eat .
But they jump up and chase him off with their stick , and the poor fox limp away on his three pad .
As he run he reach the spot where the young son be get out the food he have bring with him , and the fox ask him for a crust of bread .
The simpleton have not very much for himself , but he gladly give half of his meal to the hungry fox .
` Where be you go , brother ? '
say the fox , when he have finish his share of the bread ; and the young man tell him the story of his father and the wonderful vine .
` Dear me , how lucky ! '
say the fox . '
I know what have become of it .
Follow me ! '
So they go on till they come to the gate of a large garden .
` You will find here the vine that you be seek , but it will not be at all easy to get it .
You must listen carefully to what I be go to say .
Before you reach the vine you will have to pass twelve outpost , each consist of two guard .
If you see these guard look straight at you , go on without fear , for they be asleep .
But if their eye be shut then beware , for they be wide awake .
If you once get to the vine , you will find two shovel , one of wood and the other of iron .
Be sure not to take the iron one ; it will make a noise and rouse the guard , and then you be lose . '
The young man get safely through the garden without any adventure till he come to the vine which yield a tun of wine an hour .
But he think he should find it impossible to dig the hard earth with only a wooden shovel , so pick up the iron one instead .
The noise it make soon awaken the guard .
They seize the poor simpleton and carry him to their master .
` Why do you try to steal my vine ? '
demand he ; ` and how do you manage to get past the guard ? '
` The vine be not yours ; it belong to my father , and if you will not give it to me now , I will return and get it somehow . '
` You shall have the vine if you will bring me in exchange an apple off the golden apple-tree that flower every twenty-four hour , and bear fruit of gold . '
So say , he give order that the simpleton should be release , and this do , the youth hurry off to consult the fox .
` Now you see , ' observe the fox , ` this come of not follow my advice .
However , I will help you to get the golden apple .
It grow in a garden that you will easily recognise from my description .
Near the apple-tree be two pole , one of gold , the other of wood .
Take the wooden pole , and you will be able to reach the apple . '
Master Simpleton listen carefully to all that be tell him , and after cross the garden , and escape a before from the men who be watch it , soon arrive at the apple-tree .
But he be so dazzle by the sight of the beautiful golden fruit , that he quite forget all that the fox have say .
He seize the golden pole , and strike the branch a sounding blow .
The guard at once awoke , and conduct him to their master .
Then the simpleton have to tell his story . '
I will give you the golden apple , ' say the owner of the garden , ` if you will bring me in exchange a horse which can go round the world in four-and-twenty hour . '
And the young man depart , and go to find the fox .
This time the fox be really angry , and no wonder .
` If you have listen to me , you would have be home with your father by this time .
However I be willing to help you once more .
Go into the forest , and you will find the horse with two halter round his neck .
One be of gold , the other of hemp .
Lead him by the hempen halter , or else the horse will begin to neigh , and will waken the guard .
Then all be over with you . '
So Master Simpleton search till he find the horse , and be strike dumb at it beauty .
` What ! '
he say to himself , ` put the hempen halter on an animal like that ?
Not I , indeed ! '
Then the horse neigh loudly ; the guard seize our young friend and conduct him before their master . '
I will give you the golden horse , ' say he , ` if you will bring me in exchange a golden maiden who have never yet see either sun or moon . '
` But if I be to bring you the golden maiden you must lend me first the golden steed with which to seek for her . '
` Ah , ' reply the owner of the golden horse , ` but who will undertake that you will ever come back ? ' '
I swear on the head of my father , ' answer the young man , ` that I will bring back either the maiden or the horse . '
And he go away to consult the fox .
Now , the fox who be always patient and charitable to other people 's fault , lead him to the entrance of a deep grotto , where stand a maiden all of gold , and beautiful a the day .
He place her on his horse and prepared to mount .

THE UNLOOKED-FOR PRINCE -LRB- POLISH STORY -RRB- A long time ago there live a king and queen who have no child , although they both wish very much for a little son .
They try not to let each other see how unhappy they be , and pretend to take pleasure in hunt and hawk and all sort of other sport ; but at length the king could bear it no longer , and declare that he must go and visit the furthest corner of his kingdom , and that it would be many month before he should return to his capital .
By that time he hop he would have so many thing to think about that he would have forget to trouble about the little son who never come .
The country the king reign over be very large , and full of high , stony mountain and sandy desert , so that it be not at all easy to go from one place to another .
One day the king have wander out alone , mean to go only a little distance , but everything look so alike he could not make out the path by which he have come .
He walk on and on for hour , the sun beat hotly on his head , and his legs tremble under him , and he might have die of thirst if he have not suddenly stumble on a little well , which look a if it have be newly dig .
On the surface float a silver cup with a golden handle , but a it bob about whenever the king try to seize it , he be too thirsty to wait any long and kneel down and drink his fill .
When he have finish he begin to rise from his knee , but somehow his beard seem to have stick fast in the water , and with all his effort he could not pull it out .
After two or three jerk to his head , which only hurt him without do any good , he call out angrily , ` Let go at once !
Who be hold me ? '
` It be I , the King Kostieï , ' say a voice from the well , and look up through the water be a little man with green eye and a big head .
` You have drink from my spring , and I shall not let you go until you promise to give me the most precious thing your palace contains , which be not there when you leave it . '
Now the only thing that the king much care for in his palace be the queen herself , and a she be weep bitterly on a pile of cushion in the great hall when he have ride away , he know that Kostieï 's word could not apply to her .
So he cheerfully give the promise ask for by the ugly little man , and in the twinkling of an eye , man , spring , and cup have disappear , and the king be leave kneel on the dry sand , wonder if it be all a dream .
But a he felt much strong and well he make up his mind that this strange adventure must really have happen , and he spring on his horse and ride off with a light heart to look for his companion .
In a few week they begin to set out on their return home , which they reach one hot day , eight month after they have all leave .
The king be greatly beloved by his people , and crowd line the road , shout and wave their hat a the procession pass along .
On the step of the palace stand the queen , with a splendid golden cushion in her arm , and on the cushion the most beautiful boy that ever be see , wrap about in a cloud of lace .
In a moment Kostieï 's word rush into the king 's mind , and he begin to weep bitterly , to the surprise of everybody , who have expect him nearly to die of joy at the sight of his son .
But try a he would and work as hard a he might he could never forget his promise , and every time he let the baby out of his sight he think that he have see it for the last time .
However , year pass on and the prince grow first into a big boy , and then into a fine young man .
Kostieï make no sign , and gradually even the anxious king thought less and less about him , and in the end forget him altogether .
There be no family in the whole kingdom happy than the king and queen and prince , until one day when the youth meet a little old man a he be hunt in a lonely part of the wood .

So say the old man disappear , and the prince return to the palace and tell his father what have happen .
The king turn pale and explain to his son the terrible story .
` Do not grieve over it , father , ' answer the prince .
` It be nothing so dreadful after all !
I will find some way to force Kostieï to give up his right over me .

Then the prince begin to prepare for his journey .

So , kiss him tenderly , with many tear they let him go .
He ride steadily on for three day , and at sunset on the fourth day he find himself on the seashore .

In a few minute a flock of geese which have be paddle about in the sea approach the shore , and put on the dress , strike the sand with their foot and be transform in the twinkling of an eye into eleven beautiful young girl , who fly away as fast a they could .

THE SIMPLETON There live , once upon a time , a man who be as rich a he could be ; but a no happiness in this world be ever quite complete , he have an only son who be such a simpleton that he could barely add two and two together .
At last his father determine to put up with his stupidity no longer , and give him a purse full of gold , he send him off to seek his fortune in foreign land , mindful of the adage : How much a fool that 's send to roam Excels a fool that stay at home .
Moscione , for this be the youth 's name , mount a horse , and set out for Venice , hop to find a ship there that would take him to Cairo .
After he have ride for some time he saw a man stand at the foot of a poplar tree , and say to him : ` What 's your name , my friend ; where do you come from , and what can you do ? '
The man reply , ` My name be Quick-as-Thought , I come from Fleet-town , and I can run like lightning . ' '
I should like to see you , ' return Moscione .
` Just wait a minute , then , ' say Quick-as-Thought , ` and I will soon show you that I be speak the truth . '
The word be hardly out of his mouth when a young doe run right across the field they be stand in .
Quick-as-Thought let her run on a short distance , in order to give her a start , and then pursue her so quickly and so lightly that you could not have track his footstep if the field have be strew with flour .
In a very few spring he have overtake the doe , and have so impressed Moscione with his fleetness of foot that he beg Quick-as-Thought to go with him , promise at the same time to reward him handsomely .
Quick-as-Thought agree to his proposal , and they continue on their journey together .
They have hardly go a mile when they meet a young man , and Moscione stop and ask him : ` What 's your name , my friend ; where do you come from , and what can you do ? '
The man thus address answer promptly , ' I be call Hare 's - ear , I come from Curiosity Valley , and if I lay my ear on the ground , without move from the spot , I can hear everything that go on in the world , the plot and intrigue of court and cottage , and all the plan of mouse and men . '
` If that 's the case , ' reply Moscione , ` Just tell me what 's go on in my own home at present . '
The youth lay his ear to the ground and at once report : ` An old man be say to his wife , `` Heaven be praise that we have get rid of Moscione , for perhaps , when he have be out in the world a little , he may gain some common sense , and return home less of a fool than when he set out . '' '
` Enough , enough , ' cry Moscione .
` You speak the truth , and I believe you .
Come with u , and your fortune 's make . '
The young man consent ; and after they have go about ten mile , they meet a third man , to whom Moscione say : ` What 's your name , my brave fellow ; where be you bear , and what can you do ? '
The man reply , ' I be call Hit-the-Point , I come from the city of Perfect-aim , and I draw my bow so exactly that I can shoot a pea off a stone . ' '
I should like to see you do it , if you 've no objection , ' say Moscione .
The man at once place a pea on a stone , and , draw his bow , he shoot it in the middle with the great possible ease .
When Moscione saw that he have speak the truth , he immediately ask Hit-the-Point to join his party .
After they have all travel together for some day , they come upon a number of people who be dig a trench in the blazing sun .
Moscione felt so sorry for them , that he say : ` My dear friend , how can you endure work so hard in heat that would cook an egg in a minute ? '
But one of the workman answer : ` We be as fresh a daisy , for we have a young man among u who blow on our back like the west wind . '
` Let me see him , ' say Moscione .
The youth be call , and Moscione ask him : ` What 's your name ; where do you come from , and what can you do ? '
He answer : ' I be call Blow-Blast , I come from Wind-town , and with my mouth I can make any wind you please .
If you wish a west wind I can raise it for you in a second , but if you prefer a north wind I can blow these house down before your eye . '
` Seeing be believe , ' return the cautious Moscione .
Blow-Blast at once begin to convince him of the truth of his assertion .
First he blow so softly that it seem like the gentle breeze at evening , and then he turn round and raise such a mighty storm , that he blow down a whole row of oak tree .
When Moscione saw this he be delight , and beg Blow-Blast to join his company .
And a they go on their way they meet another man , whom Moscione address a usual : ` What 's your name ; where do you come from , and what can you do ? ' '
I be call Strong-Back ; I come from Power-borough , and I possess such strength that I can take a mountain on my back , and it seem a feather to me . '
` If that 's the case , ' say Moscione , ` you be a clever fellow ; but I should like some proof of your strength . '
Then Strong-Back load himself with great boulder of rock and trunk of tree , so that a hundred waggon could not have take away all that he carry on his back .
When Moscione saw this he prevail on Strong-Back to join his troop , and they all continue their journey till they come to a country call Flower Vale .
Here there reign a king whose only daughter run as quickly a the wind , and so lightly that she could run over a field of young oat without bend a single blade .
The king have give out a proclamation that anyone who could beat the princess in a race should have her for a wife , but that all who fail in the competition should lose their head .
As soon a Moscione heard of the Royal Proclamation , he hasten to the king and challenge the princess to race with him .
But on the morning appoint for the trial he send word to the king that he be not feel well , and that a he could not run himself he would supply someone to take his place .
` It 's just the same to me , ' say Canetella , the princess ; ` let anyone come forward that like , I be quite prepared to meet him . '
At the time appoint for the race the whole place be crowd with people anxious to see the contest , and , punctual to the moment , Quick-as-Thought , and Canetella dress in a short skirt and very lightly shod , appear at the starting-point .
Then a silver trumpet sound , and the two rival start on their race , look for all the world like a greyhound chase a hare .
But Quick-as-Thought , true to his name , outrun the princess , and when the goal be reach the people all clap their hand and shout , ` Long live the stranger ! '

Accordingly she go home and send Quick-as-Thought a magic ring , which prevent the person who wear it , not only from run , but even from walk , and beg that he would wear it for her sake .
Early next morning the crowd assemble on the race-course , and Canetella and Quick-as-Thought begin their trial afresh .
The princess run as quickly a ever , but poor Quick-as-Thought be like an overloaded donkey , and could not go a step .

In a moment the youth 's leg become free again , and in five bound he have overtake Canetella and win the race .
The king be much disgust when he saw that he must acknowledge Moscione a his future son-in-law , and summon the wise men of his court to ask if there be no way out of the difficulty .
The council at once decide that Canetella be far too dainty a morsel for the mouth of such a travelling tinker , and advise the king to offer Moscione a present of gold , which no doubt a beggar like him would prefer to all the wife in the world .
The king be delight at this suggestion , and call Moscione before him , he ask him what sum of money he would take instead of his promised bride .
Moscione first consult with his friend , and then answer : ' I demand as much gold and precious stone a my follower can carry away . '
The king think he be be let off very easily , and produce coffer of gold , sack of silver , and chest of precious stone ; but the more Strong-Back be load with the treasure the straighter he stand .
At last the treasury be quite exhaust , and the king have to send his courtier to his subject to collect all the gold and silver they possess .
But nothing be of any avail , and Strong-Back only ask for more .
When the king 's counsellor saw the unexpected result of their advice , they say it would be more than foolish to let some stroll thief take so much treasure out of the country , and urge the king to send a troop of soldier after them , to recover the gold and precious stone .
So the king send a body of arm men on foot and horse , to take back the treasure Strong-Back be carry away with him .
But Hare 's - ear , who have hear what the counsellor have advise the king , tell his companion just a the dust of their pursuer be visible on the horizon .
No sooner have Blow-Blast take in their danger than he raise such a mighty wind that all the king 's army be blow down like so many nine-pins , and a they be quite unable to get up again , Moscione and his companion proceed on their way without further let or hindrance .
As soon a they reach his home , Moscione divide his spoil with his companion , at which they be much delight .
He , himself , stay with his father , who be oblige at last to acknowledge that his son be not quite such a fool a he look .

THE STREET MUSICIANS A man once possess a donkey which have serve him faithfully for many year , but at last the poor beast grow old and feeble , and every day his work become more of a burden .
As he be no long of any use , his master make up his mind to shoot him ; but when the donkey learn the fate that be in store for him , he determine not to die , but to run away to the near town and there to become a street musician .
When he have trot along for some distance he come upon a greyhound lie on the road , and pant for dear life .
` Well , brother , ' say the donkey , ` what 's the matter with you ?
You look rather tire . '
` So I be , ' reply the dog , ` but because I be get old and be grow weak every day , and can not go out hunt any longer , my master want to poison me ; and , a life be still sweet , I have take leave of him .
But how I be to earn my own livelihood I have n't a notion . '
` Well , ' say the donkey , ' I be on my way to the near big town , where I mean to become a street musician .
Why do n't you take up music a a profession and come along with me ?
I 'll play the flute and you can play the kettle-drum . '
The greyhound be quite pleased at the idea , and the two set off together .
When they have go a short distance they meet a cat with a face as long a three rainy day .
` Now , what have happen to upset your happiness , friend pus ? '
inquire the donkey .
` It 's impossible to look cheerful when one feel depress , ' answer the cat . '
I be well up in year now , and have lose most of my teeth ; consequently I prefer sit in front of the fire to catch mouse , and so my old mistress want to drown me .
I have no wish to die yet , so I run away from her ; but good advice be expensive , and I do n't know where I be to go to , or what I be to do . '
` Come to the near big town with u , ' say the donkey , ` and try your fortune a a street musician .
I know what sweet music you make at night , so you be sure to be a success . '
The cat be delight with the donkey 's proposal , and they all continue their journey together .
In a short time they come to the courtyard of an inn , where they find a cock crow lustily .
` What in the world be the matter with you ? '
ask the donkey .
` The noise you be make be enough to break the drum of our ear . ' '
I be only prophesy good weather , ' say the cock ; ` for to-morrow be a feast day , and just because it be a holiday and a number of people be expect at the inn , the landlady have give order for my neck to be wrung to-night , so that I may be make into soup for to-morrow 's dinner . '
` I 'll tell you what , redcap , ' say the donkey ; ` you have much well come with u to the near town .
You have get a good voice , and could join a street band we be get up . '
The cock be much please with the idea , and the party proceed on their way .
But the near big town be a long way off , and it take them more than a day to reach it .
In the evening they come to a wood , and they make up their mind to go no far , but to spend the night there .
The donkey and the greyhound lay down under a big tree , and the cat and the cock get up into the branch , the cock fly right up to the topmost twig , where he think he would be safe from all danger .
Before he go to sleep he look round the four point of the compass , and saw a little spark burning in the distance .
He call out to his companion that he be sure there must be a house not far off , for he could see a light shining .
When he hear this , the donkey say at once : ` Then we must get up , and go and look for the house , for this be very poor shelter . '
And the greyhound add : ` Yes ; I feel I 'd be all the good for a few bone and a scrap or two of meat . '
So they set out for the spot where the light be to be see shin faintly in the distance , but the nearer they approach it the brighter it grow , till at last they come to a brilliantly light house .
The donkey be the big of the party , go to the window and look in .
` Well , greyhead , what do you see ? '
ask the cock . '
I see a well-covered table , ' reply the donkey , ` with excellent food and drink , and several robber be sit round it , enjoy themselves highly . ' '
I wish we be do the same , ' say the cock .
` So do I , ' answer the donkey .
` Ca n't we think of some plan for turn out the robber , and take possession of the house ourselves ? '
So they consult together what they be to do , and at last they arrange that the donkey should stand at the window with his fore-feet on the sill , that the greyhound should get on his back , the cat on the dog 's shoulder , and the cock on the cat 's head .
When they have group themselves in this way , at a give signal , they all begin their different form of music .
The donkey bray , the greyhound bark , the cat miawed , and the cock crew .
Then they all scramble through the window into the room , break the glass into a thousand piece a they do so .
The robber be all startle by the dreadful noise , and think that some evil spirit at the least be enter the house , they rush out into the wood , their hair stand on end with terror .
The four companion , delight with the success of their trick , sit down at the table , and ate and drink all the food and wine that the robber have leave behind them .
When they have finish their meal they put out the light , and each animal choose a suitable sleeping-place .
The donkey lay down in the courtyard outside the house , the dog behind the door , the cat in front of the fire , and the cock fly up on to a high shelf , and , a they be all tire after their long day , they soon go to sleep .
Shortly after midnight , when the robber saw that no light be burn in the house and that all seem quiet , the captain of the band say : ` We be fool to let ourselves be so easily frighten away ; ' and , turn to one of his men , he order him to go and see if all be safe .
The man find everything in silence and darkness , and go into the kitchen he think he have well strike a light .
He take a match , and mistake the fiery eye of the cat for two glowing coal , he try to light his match with them .
But the cat do n't see the joke , and sprang at his face , spit and scratch him in the most vigorous manner .
The man be terrify out of his life , and try to run out by the back door ; but he stumble over the greyhound , which bite him in the leg .
Yelling with pain he run across the courtyard only to receive a kick from the donkey 's hind leg a he pass him .
In the meantime the cock have be rouse from his slumber , and feel very cheerful he call out , from the shelf where he be perch , ` Kikeriki ! '
Then the robber hasten back to his captain and say : ` Sir , there be a dreadful witch in the house , who spat at me and scratch my face with her long finger ; and before the door there stand a man with a long knife , who cut my leg severely .
In the courtyard outside lie a black monster , who fell upon me with a huge wooden club ; and that be not all , for , sit on the roof , be a judge , who call out : `` Bring the rascal to me . ''
So I flee for dear life . '
After this the robber dare not venture into the house again , and they abandon it for ever .
But the four street musician be so delighted with their lodging that they determine to take up their abode in the robber ' house , and , for all I know to the contrary , they may be live there to this day .

THE TWIN BROTHERS Once there be a fisherman who have plenty of money but no child .
One day an old woman come to his wife and say : ` What use be all your prosperity to you when you have no child ? '
` It be God 's will , ' answer the fisherman 's wife .
` Nay , my child , it be not God 's will , but the fault of your husband ; for if he would but catch the little gold-fish you would surely have child .
To-night , when he come home , tell him he must go back and catch the little fish .
He must then cut it in six piece -- one of these you must eat , and your husband the second , and soon after you will have two child .
The third piece you must give to the dog , and she will have two puppy .
The fourth piece give to the mare , and she will have two foal .
The fifth piece bury on the right of the house door , and the sixth on the left , and two cypress tree will spring up there . '
When the fisherman come home at even his wife tell him all that the old woman have advise , and he promise to bring home the little gold-fish .
Next morning , therefore , he go very early to the water , and catch the little fish .
Then they do a the old woman have order , and in due time the fisherman 's wife have two son , so like each other that no one could tell the difference .
The dog have two puppy exactly alike , the mare have two foal , and on each side of the front door there spring up two cypress tree precisely similar .
When the two boy be grow up , they be not content to remain at home , though they have wealth in plenty ; but they wish to go out into the world , and make a name for themselves .
Their father would not allow them both to go at once , a they be the only child he have .
He say : ` First one shall travel , and when he be come back then the other may go . '
So the one take his horse and his dog , and go , say to his brother : ` So long a the cypress tree be green , that be a sign that I be alive and well ; but if one begin to wither , then make haste and come to me . '
So he go forth into the world .
One day he stop at the house of an old woman , and a at even he sit before the door , he perceive in front of him a castle stand on a hill .
He ask the old woman to whom it belong , and her answer be : ` My son , it be the castle of the Fairest in the Land ! '
` And I be come here to woo her ! '
` That , my son , many have seek to do , and have lose their life in the attempt ; for she have cut off their head and stick them on the post you see stand there . '
` And the same will she do to me , or else I shall be victor , for to-morrow I go there to court her . '
Then he take his zither and play upon it so beautifully that no one in all that land have ever hear the like , and the princess herself come to the window to listen .
The next morning the Fairest in the Land send for the old woman and ask her , ` Who be it that live with you , and play the zither so well ? '
` It be a stranger , princess , who arrive yesterday evening , ' answer the old woman .
And the princess then command that the stranger should be bring to her .
When he appear before the princess she question him about his home and his family , and about this and that ; and confess at length that his zither-playing give her great pleasure , and that she would take him for her husband .
The stranger reply that it be with that intent he have come .
The princess then say : ` You must now go to my father , and tell him you desire to have me to wife , and when he have put the three problem before you , then come back and tell me . '
The stranger then go straight to the king , and tell him that he wish to wed his daughter .
And the king answer : ' I shall be well pleased , provide you can do what I impose upon you ; if not you will lose your head .
Now , listen ; out there on the ground , there lie a thick log , which measure more than two fathom ; if you can cleave it in two with one stroke of your sword , I will give you my daughter to wife .
If you fail , then it will cost you your head . '
Then the stranger withdraw , and return to the house of the old woman sore distress , for he could believe nothing but that next day he must atone to the king with his head .
And so full be he of the idea of how to set about cleave the log that he forget even his zither .
In the evening come the princess to the window to listen to his playing , and behold all be still .
Then she call to him : ` Why be you so cast down this evening , that you do not play on your zither ? '
And he tell her his trouble .
But she laugh at it , and call to him : ` And you grieve over that ?
Bring quickly your zither , and play something for my amusement , and early to-morrow come to me . '
Then the stranger take his zither and play the whole evening for the amusement of the princess .
Next morning she take a hair from her lock and give it to him , say : ` Take this hair , and wind it round your sword , then you will be able to cleave the log in two . '
Then the stranger go forth , and with one blow cleave the log in two .
But the king say : ' I will impose another task upon you , before you can wed my daughter . '
` Speak on , ' say the stranger .
` Listen , then , ' answer the king ; ` you must mount a horse and ride three mile at full gallop , hold in each hand a goblet full of water .
If you spill no drop then I shall give you my daughter to wife , but should you not succeed then I will take your life . '
Then the stranger return to the house of the old woman , and again he be so troubled a to forget his zither .
In the even the princess come to the window a before to listen to the music , but again all be still ; and she call to him : ` What be the matter that you do not play on your zither ? '
Then he relate all that the king have order him to do , and the princess answer : ` Do not let yourself be disturb , only play now , and come to me to-morrow morning . '
Then next morning he go to her , and she give him her ring , say : ` Throw this ring into the water and it will immediately freeze , so that you will not spill any . '
The stranger do a the princess bid him , and carry the water all the way .
Then the king say : ` Now I will give you a third task , and this shall be the last .
I have a negro who will fight with you to-morrow , and if you be the conqueror you shall wed my daughter . '
The stranger return , full of joy , to the house of the old woman , and that evening be so merry that the princess call to him : ` You seem very cheerful this evening ; what have my father tell you that make you so glad ? '
He answer : ` Your father have tell me that to-morrow I must fight with his negro .
He be only another man like myself , and I hope to subdue him , and to gain the contest . '
But the princess answer : ` This be the hard of all .
I myself be the black man , for I swallow a drink that change me into a negro of unconquerable strength .
Go to-morrow morning to the market , buy twelve buffalo hide and wrap them round your horse ; fasten this cloth round you , and when I be let loose upon you to-morrow show it to me , that I may hold myself back and may not kill you .
Then when you fight me you must try to hit my horse between the eye , for when you have kill it you have conquer me . '
Next morning , therefore , he go to the market and buy the twelve buffalo hide which he wrap round his horse .
Then he begin to fight with the black man , and when the combat have already last a long time , and eleven hide be tear , then the stranger hit the negro 's horse between the eye , so that it fell dead , and the black man be defeat .
Then say the king : ` Because you have solve the three problem I take you for my son-in-law . '
But the stranger answer : ' I have some business to conclude first ; in fourteen day I will return and bring the bride home . '
So he arise and go into another country , where he come to a great town , and alight at the house of an old woman .
When he have have supper he beg of her some water to drink , but she answer : ` My son , I have no water ; a giant have take possession of the spring , and only let u draw from it once a year , when we bring him a maiden .
He eat her up , and then he let u draw water ; just now it be the lot of the king 's daughter , and to-morrow she will be lead forth . '
The next day accordingly the princess be lead forth to the spring , and bound there with a golden chain .
After that all the people go away and she be leave alone .
When they have go the stranger go to the maiden and ask her what ail her that she lament so much , and she answer that the reason be because the giant would come and eat her up .
And the stranger promise that he would set her free if she would take him for her husband , and the princess joyfully consent .
When the giant appear the stranger set his dog at him , and it take him by the throat and throttle him till he die ; so the princess be set free .
Now when the king heard of it he gladly consent to the marriage , and the wedding take place with great rejoicing .
The young bridegroom abode in the palace one hundred and one week .
Then he begin to find it too dull , and he desire to go out hunting .
The king would fain have prevent it , but in this he could not succeed .
Then he beg his son-in-law at least to take sufficient escort with him , but this , too , the young man evade , and take only his horse and his dog .
He have ride already a long way , when he saw in the distance a hut , and ride straight towards it in order to get some water to drink .
There he find an old woman from whom he beg the water .
She answer that first he should allow her to beat his dog with her little wand , that it might not bite her while she fetch the water .
The hunter consent ; and as soon a she have touch the dog with her wand it immediately turn to stone .
Thereupon she touch the hunter and also his horse , and both turn to stone .
As soon a that have happen , the cypress tree in front of his father 's house begin to wither .
And when the other brother saw this , he immediately set out in search of his twin .
He come first to the town where his brother have slay the giant , and there fate lead him to the same old woman where his brother have lodge .
When she saw him she take him for his twin brother , and say to him : ` Do not take it amiss of me , my son , that I do not come to wish you joy on your marriage with the king 's daughter . '
The stranger perceive what mistake she have make , but only say : ` That do not matter , old woman , ' and ride on , without further speech , to the king 's palace , where the king and the princess both take him for his twin brother , and call out : ` Why have you tarry so long away ?
We think something evil have befall you . '
When night come and he sleep with the princess , who still believe him to be her husband , he lay his sword between them , and when morning come he rise early and go out to hunt .
Fate lead him by the same way which his brother have take , and from a distance he saw him and know that he be turn to stone .
Then he enter the hut and order the old woman to disenchant his brother .
But she answer : ` Let me first touch your dog with my wand , and then I will free your brother . '
He order the dog , however , to take hold of her , and bite her up to the knee , till she cry out : ` Tell your dog to let me go and I will set your brother free ! '
But he only answer : ` Tell me the magic word that I may disenchant him myself ; ' and a she would not he order his dog to bite her up to the hip .
Then the old woman cry out : ' I have two wand , with the green one I turn to stone , and with the red one I bring to life again . '
So the hunter take the red wand and disenchant his brother , also his brother 's horse , and his dog , and order his own dog to eat the old woman up altogether .
While the brother go on their way back to the castle of the king , the one brother relate to the other how the cypress tree have all at once dry up and wither , how he have immediately set out in search of his twin , and how he have come to the castle of his father-in-law , and have claim the princess a his wife .
But the other brother become furious on hear this , and smite him over the forehead till he die , and return alone to the house of his father-in-law .
-LSB- Illustration : THE TWIN BROTHERS THE BROTHER COMES TO THE RESCUE -RSB- When night come and he be in bed the princess ask him : ` What be the matter with you last night , that you never speak a word to me ? '
Then he cry out : ` That be not me , but my brother , and I have slay him , because he tell me by the way that he have claim you for his wife ! '
` Do you know the place where you slew him ? '
ask the princess , ` and can you find the body ? ' '
I know the place exactly . '
` Then to-morrow we shall ride thither , ' say the princess .
Next morning accordingly they set out together , and when they have come to the place , the princess draw forth a small bottle that she have bring with her , and sprinkle the body with some drop of the water so that immediately he become alive again .
When he stand up , his brother say to him : ` Forgive me , dear brother , that I slew you in my anger . '
Then they embrace and go together to the Fairest in the Land , whom the unmarried brother take to wife .
Then the brother bring their parent to live with them , and all dwell together in joy and happiness .
CANNETELLA There be once upon a time a king who reign over a country call ` Bello Puojo . '
He be very rich and powerful , and have everything in the world he could desire except a child .
But at last , after he have be marry for many year , and be quite an old man , his wife Renzolla present him with a fine daughter , whom they call Cannetella .
She grow up into a beautiful girl , and be a tall and straight a a young fir-tree .
When she be eighteen year old her father call her to him and say : ` You be of an age now , my daughter , to marry and settle down ; but a I love you more than anything else in the world , and desire nothing but your happiness , I be determine to leave the choice of a husband to yourself .
Choose a man after your own heart , and you be sure to satisfy me . '
Cannetella thank her father very much for his kindness and consideration , but tell him that she have not the slight wish to marry , and be quite determine to remain single .
The king , who felt himself grow old and feeble , and long to see an heir to the throne before he die , be very unhappy at her word , and beg her earnestly not to disappoint him .
When Cannetella saw that the king have set his heart on her marriage , she say : ` Very well , dear father , I will marry to please you , for I do not wish to appear ungrateful for all your love and kindness ; but you must find me a husband handsomer , cleverer , and more charming than anyone else in the world . '
The king be overjoy by her word , and from early in the morning till late at night he sit at the window and look carefully at all the passer-by , in the hope of find a son-in-law among them .
One day , see a very good-looking man cross the street , the king call his daughter and say : ` Come quickly , dear Cannetella , and look at this man , for I think he might suit you a a husband . '
They call the young man into the palace , and set a sumptuous feast before him , with every sort of delicacy you can imagine .
In the middle of the meal the youth let an almond fall out of his mouth , which , however , he pick up again very quickly and hide under the table-cloth .
When the feast be over the stranger go away ' , and the king ask Cannetella : ` Well , what do you think of the youth ? ' '
I think he be a clumsy wretch , ' reply Cannetella .
` Fancy a-man of his age let an almond fall out of his mouth ! '
When the king hear her answer he return to his watch at the window , and shortly afterwards a very handsome young man pass by .
The king instantly call his daughter to come and see what she think of the new comer .
` Call him in , ' say Cannetella , ` that we may see him close . '
Another splendid feast be prepare , and when the stranger have eat and drink as much a he be able , and have take his departure , the king ask Cannetella how she like him .
` Not at all , ' reply his daughter ; ` what could you do with a man who require at least two servant to help him on with his cloak , because he be too awkward to put it on properly himself ? '
` If that 's all you have against him , ' say the king , ' I see how the land lie .
You be determine not to have a husband at all ; but marry someone you shall , for I do not mean my name and house to die out . '
` Well , then , my dear parent , ' say Cannetella , ' I must tell you at once that you have good not count upon me , for I never mean to marry unless I can find a man with a gold head and gold teeth . '
The king be very angry at find his daughter so obstinate ; but a he always give the girl her own way in everything , he issue a proclamation to the effect that any man with a gold head and gold teeth might come forward and claim the princess a his bride , and the kingdom of Bello Puojo a a wedding gift .
Now the king have a deadly enemy call Scioravante , who be a very powerful magician .
No sooner have this man heard of the proclamation than he summon his attendant spirit and command them to gild his head and teeth .
The spirit say , at first , that the task be beyond their power , and suggest that a pair of golden horn attach to his forehead would both be easy to make and more comfortable to wear ; but Scioravante would allow no compromise , and insist on have a head and teeth make of the fine gold .
When it be fix on his shoulder he go for a stroll in front of the palace .
And the king , see the very man he be in search of , call his daughter , and say : ` Just look out of the window , and you will find exactly what you want . '
Then , a Scioravante be hurry past , the king shout out to him : ` Just stop a minute , brother , and do n't be in such desperate haste .
If you will step in here you shall have my daughter for a wife , and I will send attendant with her , and a many horse and servant a you wish . ' '
A thousand thanks , ' return Scioravante ; ' I shall be delight to marry your daughter , but it be quite unnecessary to send anyone to accompany her .
Give me a horse and I will carry off the princess in front of my saddle , and will bring her to my own kingdom , where there be no lack of courtier or servant , or , indeed , of anything your daughter can desire . '
At first the king be very much against Cannetella 's departing in this fashion ; but finally Scioravante get his way , and place the princess before him on his horse , he set out for his own country .
Towards even he dismount , and enter a stable he place Cannetella in the same stall a his horse , and say to her : ` Now listen to what I have to say .
I be go to my home now , and that be a seven year ' journey from here ; you must wait for me in this stable , and never move from the spot , or let yourself be see by a living soul .
If you disobey my command , it will be the bad for you . '
-LSB- Illustration : SCIORAVANTE LEAVES CANNETELLA IN THE STABLE -RSB- The princess answer meekly : ` Sir I be your servant , and will do exactly a you bid me ; but I should like to know what I be to live on till you come back ? '
` You can take what the horse leave , ' be Scioravante 's reply .
When the magician have leave her Cannetella felt very miserable , and bitterly curse the day she be bear .
She spend all her time weeping and bemoan the cruel fate that have drive her from a palace into a stable , from soft , down cushion to a bed of straw , and from the dainty of her father 's table to the food that the horse leave .
She lead this wretched life for a few month , and during that time she never saw who feed and water the horse , for it be all do by invisible hand .
One day , when she be more than usually unhappy , she perceive a little crack in the wall , through which she could see a beautiful garden , with all manner of delicious fruit and flower grow in it .
The sight and smell of such delicacy be too much for poor Cannetella , and she say to herself , ' I will slip quietly out , and pick a few orange and grape , and I do n't care what happen .
Who be there to tell my husband what I do ?
and even if he should hear of my disobedience , he can not make my life more miserable than it be already . '
So she slip out and refresh her poor , starve body with the fruit she pluck in the garden .
But a short time afterwards her husband return unexpectedly , and one of the horse instantly tell him that Cannetella have go into the garden , in his absence , and have steal some orange and grape .
Scioravante be furious when he hear this , and seize a huge knife from his pocket he threaten to kill his wife for her disobedience .
But Cannetella throw herself at his foot and implore him to spare her life , say that hunger drive even the wolf from the wood .
At last she succeed in so far soften her husband 's heart that he say , ' I will forgive you this time , and spare your life ; but if you disobey me again , and I hear , on my return , that you have as much a move out of the stall , I will certainly kill you .
So , beware ; for I be go away once more , and shall be absent for seven year . '
With these word he take his departure , and Cannetella burst into a flood of tear , and , wring her hand , she moan : ` Why be I ever bear to such a hard fate ?
Oh !
father , how miserable you have make your poor daughter !
But , why should I blame my father ?
for I have only myself to thank for all my suffering .
I get the cursed head of gold , and it have bring all this misery on me .
I be indeed punish for not do a my father wish ! '
When a year have go by , it chance , one day , that the king 's cooper pass the stable where Cannetella be keep prisoner .
She recognise the man , and call him to come in .
At first he do not know the poor princess , and could not make out who it be that call him by name .
But when he hear Cannetella 's tale of woe , he hide her in a big empty barrel he have with him , partly because he be sorry for the poor girl , and , even more , because he wish to gain the king 's favour .
Then he sling the barrel on the mule 's back , and in this way the princess be carry to her own home .
They arrive at the palace about four o'clock in the morning , and the cooper knock loudly at the door .
When the servant come in haste and saw only the cooper standing at the gate , they be very indignant , and scold him soundly for come at such an hour and wake them all out of their sleep .
The king hear the noise and the cause of it , send for the cooper , for he felt certain the man must have some important business , to have come and disturb the whole palace at such an early hour .
The cooper ask permission to unload his mule , and Cannetella creep out of the barrel .
At first the king refuse to believe that it be really his daughter , for she have change so terribly in a few year , and have grow so thin and pale , that it be pitiful to see her .
At last the princess show her father a mole she have on her right arm , and then he saw that the poor girl be indeed his long-lost Cannetella .
He kiss her a thousand time , and instantly have the choice food and drink set before her .
-LSB- Illustration : CANNETELLA COMES OUT OF THE CASK -RSB- After she have satisfy her hunger , the king say to her : ` Who would have think , my dear daughter , to have find you in such a state ?
What , may I ask , have bring you to this pas ? '
Cannetella reply : ` That wicked man with the gold head and teeth treat me bad than a dog , and many a time , since I leave you , have I long to die .
But I could n't tell you all that I have suffer , for you would never believe me .
It be enough that I be once more with you , and I shall never leave you again , for I would rather be a slave in your house than queen in any other . '
In the meantime Scioravante have return to the stable , and one of the horse tell him that Cannetella have be take away by a cooper in a barrel .
When the wicked magician heard this he be beside himself with rage , and , hasten to the kingdom of Bello Puojo , he go straight to an old woman who live exactly opposite the royal palace , and say to her : ` If you will let me see the king 's daughter ' , I will give you whatever reward you like to ask for . '
The woman demand a hundred ducat of gold , and Scioravante count them out of his purse and give them to her without a murmur .
Then the old woman lead him to the roof of the house , where he could see Cannetella comb out her long hair in a room in the top story of the palace .
The princess happen to look out of the window , and when she saw her husband gaze at her , she get such a fright that she fly downstairs to the king , and say : ` My lord and father , unless you shut me up instantly in a room with seven iron door , I be lose . '
` If that 's all ' say the king , ` it shall be do at once . '
And he give order for the door to be close on the spot .
When Scioravante saw this he return to the old woman , and say : ' I will give you whatever you like if you will go into the palace , hide under the princess 's bed , and slip this little piece of paper beneath her pillow , say , a you do so : `` May everyone in the palace , except the princess , fall into a sound sleep . '' '
The old woman demand another hundred golden ducat , and then proceed to carry out the magician 's wish .
No sooner have she slip the piece of paper under Cannetella 's pillow , than all the people in the palace fell fast asleep , and only the princess remain awake .
Then Scioravante hurry to the seven door and open them one after the other .
Cannetella scream with terror when she saw her husband , but no one come to her help , for all in the palace lay a if they be dead .
The magician seize her in the bed on which she lay , and be go to carry her off with him , when the little piece of paper which the old woman have place under her pillow fell on the floor .
In an instant all the people in the palace wake up , and a Cannetella be still scream for help , they rush to her rescue .
They seize Scioravante and put him to death ; so he be catch in the trap which he have lay for the princess -- and , a be so often the case in this world , the biter himself be bit .

THE OGRE There live , once upon a time , in the land of Marigliano , a poor woman call Masella , who have six pretty daughter , all as upright a young fir-trees , and an only son call Antonio , who be so simple a to be almost an idiot .
Hardly a day pass without his mother say to him ; ` What be you do , you useless creature ?
If you be n't too stupid to look after yourself , I would order you to leave the house and never to let me see your face again . '
Every day the youth commit some fresh piece of folly , till at last Masella , lose all patience , give him a good beating , which so startle Antonio that he take to his heel and never stop run till it be dark and the star be shin in the heaven .
He wander on for some time , not know where to go , and at last he come to a cave , at the mouth of which sit an ogre , ugly than anything you can conceive .
He have a huge head and wrinkled brow -- eyebrows that meet , squint eye , a flat broad nose , and a great gash of a mouth from which two huge tusk stick out .
His skin be hairy , his arm enormous , his leg like sword blade , and his foot as flat a duck ' .
In short , he be the most hideous and laughable object in the world .
But Antonio , who , with all his fault , be no coward , and be moreover a very civil-spoken lad , take off his hat , and say : ` Good-day , sir ; I hope you be pretty well .
Could you kindly tell me how far it be from here to the place where I wish to go ? '
