` What wag do you give ? '
reply Antonio .
` If you serve me faithfully , ' return the ogre , ` I 'll be bind you 'll get enough wage to satisfy you . '
So the bargain be strike , and Antonio agree to become the ogre 's servant .
He be very well treat , in every way , and he have little or no work to do , with the result that in a few day he become as fat a a quail , as round a a barrel , as red a a lobster , and as impudent a a bantam-cock .
But , after two year , the lad get weary of this idle life , and long desperately to visit his home again .
The ogre , who could see into his heart and know how unhappy he be , say to him one day : ` My dear Antonio , I know how much you long to see your mother and sister again , and because I love you a the apple of my eye , I be willing to allow you to go home for a visit .
Therefore , take this donkey , so that you may not have to go on foot ; but see that you never say `` Bricklebrit '' to him , for if you do you 'll be sure to regret it . '
Antonio take the beast without as much a say thank you , and jump on it back he ride away in great haste ; but he have n't go two hundred yard when he dismount and call out ` Bricklebrit . '
No sooner have he pronounce the word than the donkey open it mouth and pour forth ruby , emerald , diamond and pearl , as big a walnut .
Antonio gaze in amazement at the sight of such wealth , and joyfully fill a huge sack with the precious stone , he mount the donkey again and ride on till he come to an inn .
Here he get down , and go straight to the landlord , he say to him : ` My good man , I must ask you to stable this donkey for me .
Be sure you give the poor beast plenty of oat and hay , but beware of say the word `` Bricklebrit '' to him , for if you do I can promise you will regret it .
Take this heavy sack , too , and put it carefully away for me . '
The landlord , who be no fool , on receive this strange warning , and see the precious stone sparkle through the canvas of the sack , be most anxious to see what would happen if he use the forbidden word .
So he give Antonio an excellent dinner , with a bottle of fine old wine , and prepare a comfortable bed for him .
As soon a he saw the poor simpleton close his eye and have hear his lusty snore , he hurry to the stable and say to the donkey ` Bricklebrit , ' and the animal a usual pour out any number of precious stone .
When the landlord saw all these treasure he long to get possession of so valuable an animal , and determine to steal the donkey from his foolish guest .
As soon a it be light next morning Antonio awoke , and have rub his eye and stretch himself about a hundred time he call the landlord and say to him : ` Come here , my friend , and produce your bill , for short reckoning make long friend . '
When Antonio have pay his account he go to the stable and take out his donkey , a he think , and fasten a sack of gravel , which the landlord have substitute for his precious stone , on the creature 's back , he set out for his home .
No sooner have he arrive there than he call out : ` Mother , come quickly , and bring table-cloths and sheet with you , and spread them out on the ground , and you will soon see what wonderful treasure I have bring you . '
His mother hurry into the house , and open the linen-chest where she keep her daughter ' wed outfit , she take out table-cloths and sheet make of the fine linen , and spread them flat and smooth on the ground .
Antonio place the donkey on them , and call out ` Bricklebrit . '
But this time he meet with no success , for the donkey take no more notice of the magic word than he would have do if a lyre have be twang in his ear .
Two , three , and four time do Antonio pronounce ` Bricklebrit , ' but all in vain , and he might as well have speak to the wind .
Disgusted and furious with the poor creature , he seize a thick stick and begin to beat it so hard that he nearly break every bone in it body .
The miserable donkey be so distract at such treatment that , far from pour out precious stone , it only tear and dirty all the fine linen .
When poor Masella saw her table-cloths and sheet be destroy , and that instead of become rich she have only be make a fool of , she seize another stick and belabour Antonio so unmercifully with it , that he flee before her , and never stop till he reach the ogre 's cave .
When his master saw the lad return in such a sorry plight , he understand at once what have happen to him , and make no bone about the matter , he tell Antonio what a fool he have be to allow himself to be so impose upon by the landlord , and to let a worthless animal be palm off on him instead of his magic donkey .
Antonio listen humbly to the ogre 's word , and vow solemnly that he would never act so foolishly again .
And so a year pass , and once more Antonio be overcome by a fit of home-sickness , and felt a great longing to see his own people again .
Now the ogre , although he be so hideous to look upon , have a very kind heart , and when he saw how restless and unhappy Antonio be , he at once give him leave to go home on a visit .
At part he give him a beautiful table-cloth , and say : ` Give this to your mother ; but see that you do n't lose it a you lose the donkey , and till you be safely in your own house beware of say `` Table-cloth , open , '' and `` Table-cloth , shut . ''
If you do , the misfortune be on your own head , for I have give you fair warn . '
Antonio set out on his journey , but hardly have he get out of sight of the cave than he lay the table-cloth on the ground and say , ` Table-cloth , open . '
In an instant the table-cloth unfold itself and disclose a whole mass of precious stone and other treasure .
When Antonio perceive this he say , ` Table-cloth , shut , ' and continue his journey .
He come to the same inn again , and call the landlord to him , he tell him to put the table-cloth carefully away , and whatever he do not to say ` Table-cloth , open , ' or ` Table-cloth , shut , ' to it .
The landlord , who be a regular rogue , answer , ` Just leave it to me , I will look after it a if it be my own . '
After he have give Antonio plenty to eat and drink , and have provide him with a comfortable bed , he go straight to the table-cloth and say , ` Table-cloth , open . '
It open at once , and display such costly treasure that the landlord make up his mind on the spot to steal it .
When Antonio awake next morning , the host hand him over a table-cloth exactly like his own , and carry it carefully over his arm , the foolish youth go straight to his mother 's house , and say : ` Now we shall be rich beyond the dream of avarice , and need never go about in rag again , or lack the best of food . '
With these word he spread the table-cloth on the ground and say , ` Table-cloth , open . '
But he might repeat the injunction as often a he please , it be only waste of breath , for nothing happen .
When Antonio saw this he turn to his mother and say : ` That old scoundrel of a landlord have do me once more ; but he will live to repent it , for if I ever enter his inn again , I will make him suffer for the loss of my donkey and the other treasure he have rob me of . '
Masella be in such a rage over her fresh disappointment that she could not restrain her impatience , and , turn on Antonio , she abuse him soundly , and tell him to get out of her sight at once , for she would never acknowledge him a a son of hers again .
The poor boy be very depressed by her word , and slink back to his master like a dog with his tail between his leg .
When the ogre saw him , he guess at once what have happen .
He give Antonio a good scolding , and say , ' I do n't know what prevent me smash your head in , you useless ne'er - do-well !
You blurt everything out , and your long tongue never cease wag for a moment .
If you have remain silent in the inn this misfortune would never have overtake you , so you have only yourself to blame for your present suffering . '
Antonio listen to his master 's word in silence , look for all the world like a whipped dog .
When he have be three more year in the ogre 's service he have another bad fit of home-sickness , and long very much to see his mother and sister again .
So he ask for permission to go home on a visit , and it be at once grant to him .
Before he set out on his journey the ogre present him with a beautifully carve stick and say , ` Take this stick a a remembrance of me ; but beware of say , `` Rise up , Stick , '' and `` Lie down , Stick , '' for if you do , I can only say I would n't be in your shoe for something . '
Antonio take the stick and say , ` Do n't be in the least alarmed , I 'm not such a fool a you think , and know good than most people what two and two make . '
` I 'm glad to hear it , ' reply the ogre , ` but word be woman , deed be men .
You have hear what I say , and forewarn be forearm . '
This time Antonio thank his master warmly for all his kindness , and start on his homeward journey in great spirit ; but he have not go half a mile when he say ` Rise up , Stick . '
The word be hardly out of his mouth when the stick rise and begin to rain down blow on poor Antonio 's back with such lightning-like rapidity that he have hardly strength to call out , ` Lie down , Stick ' ; but as soon a he utter the word the stick lay down , and cease beat his back black and blue .
Although he have learnt a lesson at some cost to himself , Antonio be full of joy , for he saw a way now of revenge himself on the wicked landlord .
Once more he arrive at the inn , and be receive in the most friendly and hospitable manner by his host .
Antonio greet him cordially , and say : ` My friend , will you kindly take care of this stick for me ?
But , whatever you do , do n't say `` Rise up , Stick . ''
If you do , you will be sorry for it , and you need n't expect any sympathy from me . '
The landlord , think he be come in for a third piece of good fortune , give Antonio an excellent supper ; and after he have see him comfortably to bed , he run to the stick , and call to his wife to come and see the fun , he lose no time in pronounce the word ` Rise up , Stick . '
The moment he speak the stick jump up and beat the landlord so unmercifully that he and his wife run scream to Antonio , and , wake him up , plead for mercy .
When Antonio saw how successful his trick have be he say : ' I refuse to help you , unless you give me all that you have steal from me , otherwise you will be beat to death . '
The landlord , who felt himself at death 's door already , cry out : ` Take back your property , only release me from this terrible stick ; ' and with these word he order the donkey , the table-cloth , and other treasure to be restore to their rightful owner .
As soon a Antonio have recover his belonging he say ` Stick , lie down , ' and it stop beat the landlord at once .
Then he take his donkey and table-cloth and arrive safely at his home with them .
This time the magic word have the desired effect , and the donkey and table-cloth provide the family with treasure untold .
Antonio very soon marry off his sister , make his mother rich for life , and they all live happily for ever after .

A FAIRY 'S BLUNDER Once upon a time there live a fairy whose name be Dindonette .
She be the best creature in the world , with the kind heart ; but she have not much sense , and be always do thing , to benefit people , which generally end in cause pain and distress to everybody concern .
No one know this good than the inhabitant of an island far off in the midst of the sea , which , accord to the law of fairyland , she have take under her special protection , think day and night of what she could do to make the isle the pleasant place in the whole world , a it be the most beautiful .
Now what happen be this : As the fairy go about , unseen , from house to house , she hear everywhere child long for the time when they would be ` grown-up , ' and able , they think , to do a they like ; and old people talk about the past , and sigh to be young again .
` Is there no way of satisfy these poor thing ? '
she think .
And then one night an idea occur to her .
` Oh , yes , of course !
It have be try before ; but I will manage good than the rest , with their old Fountain of Youth , which , after all , only make people young again .
I will enchant the spring that bubble up in the middle of the orchard , and the child that drink of it shall at once become grown men and woman , and the old people return to the day of their childhood . '
And without stop to consult one single other fairy , who might have give her good advice , off rush Dindonette , to cast her spell over the fountain .
It be the only spring of fresh water in the island , and at dawn be crowd with people of all age , come to drink at it source .
Delighted at her plan for make them all happy , the fairy hid herself behind a thicket of rose , and peep out whenever footstep come that way .
It be not long before she have ample proof of the success of her enchantment .
Almost before her eye the child put on the size and strength of adult , while the old men and woman instantly become helpless , tiny baby .
Indeed , so pleased be she with the result of her work , that she could no longer remain hidden , and go about tell everybody what she have do , and enjoy their gratitude and thanks .
But after the first outburst of delight at their wish be grant , people begin to be a little frighten at the rapid effect of the magic water .
It be delicious to feel yourself at the height of your power and beauty , but you would wish to keep so always !
Now this be exactly what the fairy have be in too much of a hurry to arrange , and no sooner have the child become grow up , and the men and woman become baby , than they all rush on to old age at an appal rate !
The fairy only find out her mistake when it be too late to set it right .
When the inhabitant of the island saw what have befall them , they be fill with despair , and do everything they could think of to escape from such a dreadful fate .
They dig well in their place , so that they should no longer need to drink from the magic spring ; but the sandy soil yield no water , and the rainy season be already past .
They store up the dew that fell , and the juice of fruit and of herb , but all this be a a drop in the ocean of their want .
Some throw themselves into the sea , trust that the current might carry them to other shore -- they have no boat -- and a few , still more impatient , put themselves to death on the spot .
The rest submit blindly to their destiny .
Perhaps the bad part of the enchantment be , that the change from one age to another be so rapid that the person have no time to prepare himself for it .
It would not have matter so much if the man who stand up in the assembly of the nation , to give his advice a to peace or war , have look like a baby , as long a he speak with the knowledge and sense of a full-grown man .
But , ala !
with the outward form of an infant , he have take on it helplessness and foolishness , and there be no one who could train him to good thing .
The end of it all be , that before a month have pass the population have die out , and the fairy Dindonette , ashamed and grieve at the effect of her folly , have leave the island for ever .
Many century after , the fairy Selnozoura , who have fall into bad health , be order by her doctor to make the tour of the world twice a week for change of air , and in one of these journey she find herself at Fountain Island .
Selnozoura never make these trip alone , but always take with her two child , of whom she be very fond -- Cornichon , a boy of fourteen , buy in his childhood at a slave-market , and Toupette , a few month younger , who have be entrust to the care of the fairy by her guardian , the genius Kristopo .
Cornichon and Toupette be intend by Selnozoura to become husband and wife , as soon a they be old enough .
Meanwhile , they travel with her in a little vessel , whose speed through the air be just a thousand nine hundred and fifty time great than that of the swift of our ship .
Struck with the beauty of the island , Selnozoura run the vessel to ground , and leave it in the care of the dragon which live in the hold during the voyage , step on shore with her two companion .
Surprised at the sight of a large town whose street and house be absolutely desolate , the fairy resolve to put her magic art in practice to find out the cause .
While she be thus engage , Cornichon and Toupette wander away by themselves , and by-and-by arrive at the fountain , whose bubble water look cool and delicious on such a hot day .
Scarcely have they each drink a deep draught , when the fairy , who by this time have discover all she wish to know , hasten to the spot .
` Oh , beware !
beware ! '
she cry , the moment she saw them .
` If you drink that deadly poison you will be ruin for ever ! '
` Poison ? '
answer Toupette .
` It be the most refreshing water I have ever taste , and Cornichon will say so too ! '
` Unhappy child , then I be too late !
Why do you leave me ?
Listen , and I will tell you what have befall the wretched inhabitant of this island , and what will befall you too .
The power of fairy be great , ' she add , when she have finish her story , ` but they can not destroy the work of another fairy .
Very shortly you will pass into the weakness and silliness of extreme old age , and all I can do for you be to make it a easy to you a possible , and to preserve you from the death that others have suffer , from have no one to look after them .
But the charm be work already !
Cornichon be tall and more manly than he be an hour ago , and Toupette no longer look like a little girl . '
It be true ; but this fact do not seem to render the young people as miserable a it do Selnozoura .
` Do not pity u , ' say Cornichon .
` If we be fat to grow old so soon , let u no longer delay our marriage .
What matter if we anticipate our decay , if we only anticipate our happiness too ? '
The fairy felt that Cornichon have reason on his side , and see by a glance at Toupette 's face that there be no opposition to be fear from her , she answer , ` Let it be so , then .
But not in this dreadful place .
We will return at once to Bagota , and the festivity shall be the most brilliant ever see . '
They all return to the vessel , and in a few hour the four thousand five hundred mile that lay between the island and Bagota be pass .
Everyone be surprise to see the change which the short absence have make in the young people , but a the fairy have promise absolute silence about the adventure , they be none the wiser , and busy themselves in prepare their dress for the marriage , which be fix for the next night .
Early on the following morning the genius Kristopo arrive at the Court , on one of the visit he be in the habit of pay his ward from time to time .
Like the rest , he be astonish at the sudden improvement in the child .
He have always be fond of her , and in a moment he fell violently in love .
Hastily demand an audience of the fairy , he lay his proposal before her , never doubt that she would give her consent to so brilliant a match .
But Selnozoura refuse to listen , and even hint that in his own interest Kristopo have well turn his thought elsewhere .
The genius pretend to agree , but , instead , he go straight to Toupette 's room , and fly away with her through the window , at the very instant that the bridegroom be await her below .
When the fairy discover what have happen , she be furious , and send messenger after messenger to the genius in his palace at Ratibouf , command him to restore Toupette without delay , and threaten to make war in case of refusal .
Kristopo give no direct answer to the fairy 's envoy , but keep Toupette closely guard in a tower , where the poor girl use all her power of persuasion to induce him to put off their marriage .
All would , however , have be quite in vain if , in the course of a few day , sorrow , join to the spell of the magic water , have not alter her appearance so completely that Kristopo be quite alarmed , and declare that she need amusement and fresh air , and that , a his presence seem to distress her , she should be leave her own mistress .
But one thing he decline to do , and that be to send her back to Bagota .
In the meantime both side have be busily collect army , and Kristopo have give the command of his to a famous general , while Selnozoura have place Cornichon at the head of her force .
But before war be actually declare , Toupette 's parent , who have be summon by the genius , arrive at Ratibouf .
They have never see their daughter since they part from her a a baby , but from time to time traveller to Bagota have bring back account of her beauty .
What be their amazement , therefore , at find , instead of a lovely girl , a middle-aged woman , handsome indeed , but quite fade -- look , in fact , old than themselves .
Kristopo , hardly less astonish than they be at the sudden change , think that it be a joke on the part of one of his courtier , who have hide Toupette away , and put this elderly lady in her place .
Bursting with rage , he send instantly for all the servant and guard of the town , and inquire who have the insolence to play him such a trick , and what have become of their prisoner .
They reply that since Toupette have be in their charge she have never leave her room unveil , and that during her walk in the surrounding garden , her food have be bring in and place on her table ; a she prefer to eat alone no one have ever see her face , or know what she be like .
The servant be clearly speak the truth , and Kristopo be oblige to believe them .
` But , ' think he , ` if they have not have a hand in this , it must be the work of the fairy , ' and in his anger he order the army to be ready to march .
On her side , Selnozoura of course know what the genius have to expect , but be deeply offend when she hear of the base trick which she be believe to have invent .
Her first desire be to give battle to Kristopo at once , but with great difficulty her minister induce her to pause , and to send an ambassador to Kristopo to try to arrange matter .
So the Prince Zeprady depart for the court of Ratibouf , and on his way he meet Cornichon , who be encamp with his army just outside the gate of Bagota .
The Prince show him the fairy 's write order that for the present peace must still be keep , and Cornichon , fill with longing to see Toupette once more , beg to be allow to accompany Zeprady on his mission to Ratibouf .
By this time the genius 's passion for Toupette , which have cause all these trouble , have die out , and he willingly accept the term of peace offer by Zeprady , though he inform the prince that he still believe the fairy to be guilty of the dreadful change in the girl .
To this the prince only reply that on that point he have a witness who could prove , good than anyone else , if it be Toupette or not , and desire that Cornichon should be send for .
When Toupette be tell that she be to see her old lover again , her heart leapt with joy ; but soon the recollection come to her of all that have happen , and she remember that Cornichon would be change as well a she .
The moment of their meeting be not all happiness , especially on the part of Toupette , who could not forget her lose beauty , and the genius , who be present , be at last convince that he have not be deceive , and go out to sign the treaty of peace , follow by his attendant .
` Ah , Toupette : my dear Toupette ! '
cry Cornichon , as soon a they be leave alone ; ` now that we be once more united , let our past trouble be forget . '
` Our past trouble ! '
answer she , ` and what do you call our lose beauty and the dreadful future before u ?
You be look fifty year old than when I saw you last , and I know too well that fate have treat me no good ! '
` Ah , do not say that , ' reply Cornichon , clasp her hand , ` You be different , it be true ; but every age have it grace , and surely no woman of sixty be ever handsome than you !
If your eye have be as bright a of yore they would have match badly with your faded skin .
The wrinkle which I notice on your forehead explain the increased fulness of your cheek , and your throat in withering be elegant in decay .
Thus the harmony show by your feature , even a they grow old , be the best proof of their former beauty .
` Oh , monster , ' cry Toupette , burst into tear , ` be that all the comfort you can give me ? '
` But , Toupette , ' answered Cornichon ; ` you use to declare that you do not care for beauty , as long a you have my heart . '
` Yes , I know , ' say she , ` but how can you go on care for a person who be a old and plain a I ? '
` Toupette , Toupette , ' reply Cornichon , ` you be only talk nonsense .
My heart be as much yours a ever it be , and nothing in the world can make any difference . '
At this point of the conversation the Prince Zeprady enter the room , with the news that the genius , full of regret for his behaviour , have give Cornichon full permission to depart for Bagota as soon a he like , and to take Toupette with him ; add that , though he beg they would excuse his take leave of them before they go , he hop , before long , to visit them at Bagota .
Neither of the lover sleep that night -- Cornichon from joy at return home , Toupette from dread of the blow to her vanity which await her at Bagota .
It be hopeless for Cornichon to try to console her during the journey with the reason he have give the day before .
She only grow bad and bad , and when they reach the palace go straight to her old apartment , entreat the fairy to allow both herself and Cornichon to remain concealed , and to see no one .
For some time after their arrival the fairy be take up with the preparation for the rejoicing which be to celebrate the peace , and with the reception of the genius , who be determine to do all in his power to regain Selnozoura 's lose friendship .
Cornichon and Toupette be therefore left entirely to themselves , and though this be only what they want , still , they begin to feel a little neglected .
At length , one morning , they saw from the window that the fairy and the genius be approach , in state , with all their courtier in attendance .
Toupette instantly hide herself in the dark corner of the room , but Cornichon , forget that he be now no longer a boy of fourteen , run to meet them .
In so do he trip and fell , bruise one of his eye severely .
At the sight of her lover lie helpless on the floor , Toupette hasten to his side ; but her feeble leg give way under her , and she fell almost on top of him , knock out three of her loosened teeth against his forehead .
The fairy , who enter the room at this moment , burst into tear , and listen in silence to the genius , who hint that by-and-by everything would be put right .
` At the last assembly of the fairy , ' he say , ` when the doings of each fairy be examine and discuss , a proposal be make to lessen , as far a possible , the mischief cause by Dindonette by enchant the fountain .
And it be decide that , a she have mean nothing but kindness , she should have the power of undo one half of the spell .
Of course she might always have destroy the fatal fountain , which would have be best of all ; but this she never think of .
Yet , in spite of this , her heart be so good , that I be sure that the moment she hear that she be want she will fly to help .
Only , before she come , it be for you , Madam , to make up your mind which of the two shall regain their former strength and beauty . '
At these word the fairy 's soul sank .
Both Cornichon and Toupette be equally dear to her , and how could she favour one at the cost of the other ?
As to the courtier , none of the men be able to understand why she hesitate a second to declare for Toupette ; while the lady be equally strong on the side of Cornichon .
But , however undecided the fairy might be , it be quite different with Cornichon and Toupette .
` Ah , my love , ' exclaim Cornichon , ` at length I shall be able to give you the best proof of my devotion by show you how I value the beauty of your mind above those of your body !
While the most charming woman of the court will fall victim to my youth and strength , I shall think of nothing but how to lay them at your foot , and pay heart-felt homage to your age and wrinkle . '
` Not so fast , ' interrupted Toupette , ' I do n't see why you should have it all .
Why do you heap such humiliation upon me ?
But I will trust to the justice of the fairy , who will not treat me so . '
Then she enter her own room , and refuse to leave them , in spite of the prayer of Cornichon , who beg her to let him explain .
No one at the court think or spoke of any other subject during the few day before the arrival of Dindonette , whom everybody expect to set thing right in a moment .
But , ala !
she have no idea herself what be best to be do , and always adopt the opinion of the person she be talk to .
At length a thought struck her , which seem the only way of satisfy both party , and she ask the fairy to call together all the court and the people to hear her decision .
` Happy be he , ' she begin , ` who can repair the evil he have cause , but happy he who have never cause any . '
As nobody contradict this remark , she continue : ` To me it be only allow to undo one half of the mischief I have work .
I could restore you your youth , ' she say to Cornichon , ` or your beauty , ' turn to Toupette . '
I will do both ; and I will do neither . '
A murmur of curiosity arise from the crowd , while Cornichon and Toupette tremble with astonishment .
` No , ' go on Dindonette , ` never should I have the cruelty to leave one of you to decay , while the other enjoy the glory of youth .
And a I can not restore you both at once to what you be , one half of each of your body shall become young again , while the other half go on it way to decay .
I will leave it to you to choose which half it shall be -- if I shall draw a line round the waist , or a line straight down the middle of the body . '
She look about her proudly , expect applause for her clever idea .
But Cornichon and Toupette be shake with rage and disappointment , and everyone else break into shout of laughter .
In pity for the unhappy lover , Selnozoura come forward .
` Do you not think , ' she say , ` that instead of what you propose , it would be good to let them take it in turn to enjoy their former youth and beauty for a fixed time ?
I be sure you could easily manage that . '
` What an excellent notion ! '
cry Dindonette .
` Oh , yes , of course that be best !
Which of you shall I touch first ? '
` Touch her , ' reply Cornichon , who be always ready to give way to Toupette . '
I know her heart too well to fear any change . '
So the fairy bent forward and touch her with her magic ring , and in one instant the old woman be a girl again .
The whole court weep with joy at the sight , and Toupette run up to Cornichon , who have fall down in his surprise , promise to pay him long visit , and tell him of all her ball and water party .
The two fairy go to their own apartment , where the genius follow them to take his leave .
` Oh , dear ! '
suddenly cry Dindonette , break in to the farewell speech of the genius . '
I quite forget to fix the time when Cornichon should in his turn grow young .
How stupid of me !
And now I fear it be too late , for I ought to have declare it before I touch Toupette with the ring .
Oh , dear !
oh , dear !
why do nobody warn me ? '
` You be so quick , ' reply Selnozoura , who have long be aware of the mischief the fairy have again do , ` and we can only wait now till Cornichon shall have reach the utmost limit of his decay , when he will drink of the water , and become a baby once more , so that Toupette will have to spend her life a a nurse , a wife , and a caretaker . '
After the anxiety of mind and the weakness of body to which for so long Toupette have be a prey , it seem a if she could not amuse herself enough , and it be seldom indeed that she find time to visit poor Cornichon , though she do not cease to be fond of him , or to be kind to him .
Still , she be perfectly happy without him , and this the poor man do not fail to see , almost blind and deaf from age though he be .
But it be leave to Kristopo to undo at last the work of Dindonette , and give Cornichon back the youth he have lose , and this the genius do all the more gladly , a he discover , quite by accident , that Cornichon be in fact his son .
It be on this plea that he attend the great yearly meeting of the fairy , and pray that , in consideration of his service to so many of the member , this one boon might be grant him .
Such a request have never before be hear in fairyland , and be object to by some of the old fairy ; but both Kristopo and Selnozoura be hold in such high honour that the murmur of disgust be set aside , and the late victim to the enchant fountain be pronounce to be free of the spell .

She hear the news with astonishment , and many pang for the grief which Cornichon would certainly feel at his place be take by another ; but she do not dream of disobey the fairy , and spend the whole day wonder who the bridegroom could be .
At the appointed hour , a large crowd assemble at the fairy 's palace , which be decorate with the sweet flower , know only to fairyland .
Toupette have take her place , but where be the bridegroom ?
` Fetch Cornichon ! '
say the fairy to her chamberlain .
But Toupette interpose : ` Oh , Madam , spare him , I entreat you , this bitter pain , and let him remain hidden and in peace . '
` It be necessary that he should be here , ' answer the fairy , ` and he will not regret it . '
And , a she speak , Cornichon be lead in , smile with the foolishness of extreme old age at the sight of the gay crowd .

` May you live long , ' the genius say , ` to enjoy happiness with your wife , and to love your father . '
And that be the end of the mischief wrought by the fairy Dindonette !

LONG , BROAD , AND QUICKEYE -LRB- BOHEMIAN STORY -RRB- Once upon a time there live a king who have an only son whom he love dearly .
Now one day the king sent for his son and say to him : ` My dearest child , my hair be grey and I be old , and soon I shall feel no more the warmth of the sun , or look upon the tree and flower .
But before I die I should like to see you with a good wife ; therefore marry , my son , as speedily a possible . '
` My father , ' reply the prince , ` now and always , I ask nothing well than to do your bidding , but I know of no daughter-in-law that I could give you . '
On hear these word the old king drew from his pocket a key of gold , and give it to his son , say : ` Go up the staircase , right up to the top of the tower .
Look carefully round you , and then come and tell me which you like best of all that you see . '
So the young man go up .
He have never before be in the tower , and have no idea what it might contain .
The staircase wound round and round and round , till the prince be almost giddy , and every now and then he catch sight of a large room that open out from the side .
But he have be tell to go to the top , and to the top he go .
Then he find himself in a hall , which have an iron door at one end .
This door he unlock with his golden key , and he pass through into a vast chamber which have a roof of blue sprinkle with golden star , and a carpet of green silk soft a turf .
Twelve windows frame in gold let in the light of the sun , and on every window be paint the figure of a young girl , each more beautiful than the last .
While the prince gaze at them in surprise , not know which he like best , the girl begin to lift their eye and smile at him .
He wait , expect them to speak , but no sound come .
Suddenly he notice that one of the window be cover by a curtain of white silk .
He lift it , and saw before him the image of a maiden beautiful a the day and sad a the tomb , clothe in a white robe , have a girdle of silver and a crown of pearl .
The prince stand and gaze at her , a if he have be turn into stone , but a he look the sadness which be on her face seem to pass into his heart , and he cry out : ` This one shall be my wife .
This one and no other . '

As he say the word the young girl blush and hang her head , and all the other figure vanish .

This young girl have fall into the power of a wicked sorcerer , who live in an iron castle .

But what be do be do !

So the prince embrace his father , mount his horse , and set forth to seek his bride .

Very soon they get clear of the forest , and saw before them a wide plain end in a pile of high rock , cover here and there with tree , and very much like the fortification of a town .

PRUNELLA There be once upon a time a woman who have an only daughter .
When the child be about seven year old she use to pass every day , on her way to school , an orchard where there be a wild plum tree , with delicious ripe plum hang from the branch .
Each morning the child would pick one , and put it into her pocket to eat at school .
For this reason she be call Prunella .
Now , the orchard belong to a witch .
One day the witch notice the child gather a plum , a she pass along the road .
Prunella do it quite innocently , not know that she be do wrong in take the fruit that hang close to the roadside .
But the witch be furious , and next day hide herself behind the hedge , and when Prunella come past , and put out her hand to pluck the fruit , she jump out and seize her by the arm .
` Ah !
you little thief ! '
she exclaim . '
I have catch you at last .
Now you will have to pay for your misdeed . '
The poor child , half dead with fright , implore the old woman to forgive her , assure her that she do not know she have do wrong , and promise never to do it again .
But the witch have no pity , and she drag Prunella into her house , where she keep her till the time should come when she could have her revenge .
As the year pass Prunella grow up into a very beautiful girl .
Now her beauty and goodness , instead of soften the witch 's heart , arouse her hatred and jealousy .
One day she call Prunella to her , and say : ` Take this basket , go to the well , and bring it back to me fill with water .
If you do n't I will kill you . '
The girl take the basket , go and let it down into the well again and again .
But her work be lose labour .
Each time , a she draw up the basket , the water stream out of it .
At last , in despair , she give it up , and lean against the well she begin to cry bitterly , when suddenly she hear a voice at her side say ` Prunella , why be you cry ? '
Turning round she behold a handsome youth , who look kindly at her , a if he be sorry for her trouble .
` Who be you , ' she ask , ` and how do you know my name ? ' '
I be the son of the witch , ' he reply , ` and my name be Bensiabel .
I know that she be determine that you shall die , but I promise you that she shall not carry out her wicked plan .
Will you give me a kiss , if I fill your basket ? '
` No , ' say Prunella , ' I will not give you a kiss , because you be the son of a witch . '
` Very well , ' reply the youth sadly .
` Give me your basket and I will fill it for you . '
And he dip it into the well , and the water stay in it .
Then the girl return to the house , carry the basket fill with water .
When the witch saw it , she become white with rage , and exclaim ` Bensiabel must have help you . '
And Prunella look down , and say nothing .
` Well , we shall see who will win in the end , ' say the witch , in a great rage .
The following day she call the girl to her and say : ` Take this sack of wheat .
I be go out for a little ; by the time I return I shall expect you to have make it into bread .
If you have not do it I will kill you . '
Having say this she leave the room , close and lock the door behind her .
Poor Prunella do not know what to do .
It be impossible for her to grind the wheat , prepare the dough , and bake the bread , all in the short time that the witch would be away .
At first she set to work bravely , but when she saw how hopeless her task be , she throw herself on a chair , and begin to weep bitterly .
She be rouse from her despair by hear Bensiabel 's voice at her side say : ` Prunella , Prunella , do not weep like that .
If you will give me a kiss I will make the bread , and you will be save . ' '
I will not kiss the son of a witch , ' reply Prunella .
But Bensiabel take the wheat from her , and ground it , and make the dough , and when the witch return the bread be ready bake in the oven .
Turning to the girl , with fury in her voice , she say : ` Bensiabel must have be here and help you ; ' and Prunella look down , and say nothing .
` We shall see who will win in the end , ' say the witch , and her eye blaze with anger .
Next day she call the girl to her and say : ` Go to my sister , who live across the mountain .
She will give you a casket , which you must bring back to me . '
This she say know that her sister , who be a still more cruel and wicked witch than herself , would never allow the girl to return , but would imprison her and starve her to death .
But Prunella do not suspect anything , and set out quite cheerfully .
On the way she meet Bensiabel .
` Where be you go , Prunella ? '
he ask . '
I be go to the sister of my mistress , from whom I be to fetch a casket . '
` Oh poor , poor girl ! '
say Bensiabel .
` You be be send straight to your death .
Give me a kiss , and I will save you . '
But again Prunella answer a before , ' I will not kiss the son of a witch . '
` Nevertheless , I will save your life , ' say Bensiabel , ` for I love you good than myself .
Take this flagon of oil , this loaf of bread , this piece of rope , and this broom .
When you reach the witch 's house , oil the hinge of the door with the content of the flagon , and throw the loaf of bread to the great fierce mastiff , who will come to meet you .
When you have pass the dog , you will see in the courtyard a miserable woman try in vain to let down a bucket into the well with her plaited hair .
You must give her the rope .
In the kitchen you will find a still more miserable woman try to clean the hearth with her tongue ; to her you must give the broom .
You will see the casket on the top of a cupboard , take it as quickly a you can , and leave the house without a moment 's delay .
If you do all this exactly a I have tell you , you will not be kill . '
So Prunella , have listen carefully to his instruction , do just what he have tell her .
She reach the house , oil the hinge of the door , throw the loaf to the dog , give the poor woman at the well the rope , and the woman in the kitchen the broom , catch up the casket from the top of the cupboard , and flee with it out of the house .
But the witch hear her a she run away , and rush to the window call out to the woman in the kitchen : ` Kill that thief , I tell you ! '
But the woman reply : ' I will not kill her , for she have give me a broom , whereas you force me to clean the hearth with my tongue . '
Then the witch call out in fury to the woman at the well ; ` Take the girl , I tell you , and fling her into the water , and drown her ! '
But the woman answer ; ` No , I will not drown her , for she give me this rope , whereas you force me to use my hair to let down the bucket to draw water . '
Then the witch shout to the dog to seize the girl and hold her fast ; but the dog answer ; ` No , I will not seize her , for she give me a loaf of bread , whereas you let me starve with hunger . '
The witch be so angry that she nearly choke , a she call out ; ` Door , bang upon her , and keep her a prisoner . '
But the door answer ; ' I wo n't , for she have oil my hinge , so that they move quite easily , whereas you leave them all rough and rusty . '
And so Prunella escape , and , with the casket under her arm , reach the house of her mistress who , a you may believe , be as angry a she be surprised to see the girl stand before her , look more beautiful than ever .
Her eye flash , a in furious tone she ask her , ` Did you meet Bensiabel ? '
But Prunella look down , and say nothing .
` We shall see , ' say the witch , ` who will win in the end .
Listen , there be three cock in the hen-house ; one be yellow , one black , and the third be white .
If one of them crow during the night you must tell me which one it be .
Woe to you if you make a mistake .
I will gobble you up in one mouthful . '
Now Bensiabel be in the room next to the one where Prunella slept .
At midnight she awake hear a cock crow .
` Which one be that ? '
shout the witch .
Then , tremble , Prunella knock on the wall and whisper : ` Bensiabel , Bensiabel , tell me , which cock crow ? '
` Will you give me a kiss if I tell you ? '
he whisper back through the wall .
But she answer ` No . '
Then he whisper back to her ; ` Nevertheless , I will tell you .

And the witch stamp her foot and gnash her teeth .

And , prompt by Bensiabel , Prunella answer : ` That be the black cock . '
A few minute after the crowing be heard again , and the voice of the witch demand ` Which one be that ? '
And again Prunella implore Bensiabel to help her .
But this time he hesitate , for he hop that Prunella might forget that he be a witch 's son , and promise to give him a kiss .
And a he hesitate he hear an agonised cry from the girl : ` Bensiabel , Bensiabel , save me !
The witch be come , she be close to me , I hear the gnashing of her teeth ! '
With a bound Bensiabel open his door and flung himself against the witch .
He pull her back with such force that she stumble , and fall headlong , drop down dead at the foot of the stair .

We have an exciting time open our present .
Some of u have more than others , but we all receive enough to make u feel comfortably that we be not unduly neglect in the matter .
The content of the box which the Story Girl 's father have send her from Paris make our eye stick out .
It be full of beautiful thing , among them another red silk dress -- not the bright , flame-hued tint of her old one , but a rich , dark crimson , with the most distracting flounce and bow and ruffle ; and with it be little red satin slipper with gold buckle , and heel that make Aunt Janet hold up her hand in horror .
Felicity remark scornfully that she would have think the Story Girl would get tired wearing red so much , and even Cecily comment apart to me that she think when you get so many thing all at once you do n't appreciate them as much a when you only get a few .
`` I 'd never get tire of red , '' say the Story Girl .
`` I just love it -- it 's so rich and glowing .
When I 'm dress in red I always feel ever so much clever than in any other colour .
Thoughts just crowd into my brain one after the other .
Oh , you darling dress -- you dear , sheeny , red-rosy , glistening , silky thing ! ''
She fling it over her shoulder and dance around the kitchen .
`` Do n't be silly , Sara , '' say Aunt Janet , a little stimy .
She be a good soul , that Aunt Janet , and have a kind , love heart in her ample bosom .
But I fancy there be time when she think it rather hard that the daughter of a roving adventurer -- a she consider him -- like Blair Stanley should disport herself in silk dress , while her own daughter must go clad in gingham and muslin -- for those be the day when a feminine creature get one silk dress in her lifetime , and seldom more than one .
The Story Girl also get a present from the Awkward Man -- a little , shabby , worn volume with a great many mark on the leaf .
`` Why , it be n't new -- it 's an old book ! ''
exclaim Felicity .
`` I do n't think the Awkward Man be mean , whatever else he be . ''
`` Oh , you do n't understand , Felicity , '' say the Story Girl patiently .
`` And I do n't suppose I can make you understand .
But I 'll try .
I 'd ten time rather have this than a new book .
It 's one of his own , do n't you see -- one that he have read a hundred time and love and make a friend of .
A new book , just out of a shop , would n't be the same thing at all .
It would n't MEAN anything .
I consider it a great compliment that he have give me this book .
I 'm prouder of it than of anything else I 've get . ''
`` Well , you 're welcome to it , '' say Felicity .
`` I do n't understand and I do n't want to .
I would n't give anybody a Christmas present that be n't new , and I would n't thank anybody who give me one . ''
Peter be in the seventh heaven because Felicity have give him a present -- and , moreover , one that she have make herself .
It be a bookmark of perforated cardboard , with a gorgeous red and yellow worst goblet work on it , and below , in green letter , the solemn warning , `` Touch Not The Cup . ''
As Peter be not addict to habit of intemperance , not even to look on dandelion wine when it be pale yellow , we do not exactly see why Felicity should have select such a device .
But Peter be perfectly satisfy , so nobody cast any blight on his happiness by carp criticism .
Later on Felicity tell me she have work the bookmark for him because his father use to drink before he run away .
`` I think Peter ought to be warn in time , '' she say .
Even Pat have a ribbon of blue , which he claw off and lose half an hour after it be tie on him .
Pat do not care for vain adornment of the body .
We have a glorious Christmas dinner , fit for the hall of Lucullus , and eat far more than be good for u , none daring to make u afraid on that one day of the year .
And in the evening -- oh , rapture and delight !
-- we go to Kitty Marr 's party .
It be a fine December evening ; the sharp air of morning have mellow until it be as mild a autumn .
There have be no snow , and the long field , slop down from the homestead , be brown and mellow .
A weird , dreamy stillness have fall on the purple earth , the dark fir wood , the valley rim , the sere meadow .
Nature seem to have fold satisfied hand to rest , know that her long wintry slumber be come upon her .
At first , when the invitation to the party have come , Aunt Janet have say we could not go ; but Uncle Alec intercede in our favour , perhaps influence thereto by Cecily 's wistful eye .
If Uncle Alec have a favourite among his child it be Cecily , and he have grow even more indulgent towards her of late .
Now and then I saw him look at her intently , and , follow his eye and think , I have , somehow , see that Cecily be paler and thinner than she have be in the summer , and that her soft eye seem large , and that over her little face in moment of repose there be a certain languor and weariness that make it very sweet and pathetic .
And I hear him tell Aunt Janet that he do not like to see the child get so much the look of her Aunt Felicity .
`` Cecily be perfectly well , '' say Aunt Janet sharply .
`` She 's only grow very fast .
Do n't be foolish , Alec . ''
But after that Cecily have cup of cream where the rest of u get only milk ; and Aunt Janet be very particular to see that she have her rubber on whenever she go out .
On this merry Christmas evening , however , no fear or dim foreshadowing of any come event cloud our heart or face .
Cecily look brighter and pretty than I have ever see her , with her softly shin eye and the nut brown gloss of her hair .
Felicity be too beautiful for word ; and even the Story Girl , between excitement and the crimson silk array , blossom out with a charm and allurement more potent than any regular loveliness -- and this in spite of the fact that Aunt Olivia have taboo the red satin slipper and mercilessly decree that stout shoe should be wear .
`` I know just how you feel about it , you daughter of Eve , '' she say , with gay sympathy , `` but December road be damp , and if you be go to walk to Marrs ' you be not go to do it in those frivolous Parisian concoction , even with overboots on ; so be brave , dear heart , and show that you have a soul above little red satin shoe . ''
`` Anyhow , '' say Uncle Roger , `` that red silk dress will break the heart of all the feminine small fry at the party .
You 'd break their spirit , too , if you wear the slipper .
Do n't do it , Sara .
Leave them one wee loophole of enjoyment . ''
`` What do Uncle Roger mean ? ''
whispered Felicity .
`` He mean you girl be all die of jealousy because of the Story Girl 's dress , '' say Dan .
`` I be not of a jealous disposition , '' say Felicity loftily , `` and she 's entirely welcome to the dress -- with a complexion like that . ''
But we enjoy that party hugely , every one of u .
And we enjoy the walk home afterwards , through dim , enshadowed field where silvery star-beams lay , while Orion tread his stately march above u , and a red moon climb up the black horizon 's rim .
A brook go with u part of the way , sing to u through the dark -- a gay , irresponsible vagabond of valley and wilderness .
Felicity and Peter walk not with u .
Peter 's cup must surely have brim over that Christmas night .
When we leave the Marr house , he have boldly say to Felicity , `` May I see you home ? ''
And Felicity , much to our amazement , have take his arm and march off with him .
The primness of her be indescribable , and be not at all ruffle by Dan 's hoot of derision .
As for me , I be consume by a secret and burn desire to ask the Story Girl if I might see HER home ; but I could not screw my courage to the sticking point .
How I envy Peter his easy , insouciant manner !
I could not emulate him , so Dan and Felix and Cecily and the Story Girl and I all walk hand in hand , huddle a little close together a we go through James Frewen 's wood -- for there be strange harp in a fir grove , and who shall say what finger sweep them ?
Mighty and sonorous be the music above our head a the wind of the night stir the great bough toss athwart the starlit sky .
Perhaps it be that aeolian harmony which recall to the Story Girl a legend of elder day .
`` I read such a pretty story in one of Aunt Olivia 's book last night , '' she say .
`` It be call ` The Christmas Harp . '
Would you like to hear it ?
It seem to me it would just suit this part of the road . ''
`` There be n't anything about -- about ghost in it , be there ? ''
say Cecily timidly .
`` Oh , no , I would n't tell a ghost story here for anything .
I 'd frighten myself too much .
This story be about one of the shepherd who saw the angel on the first Christmas night .
He be just a youth , and he love music with all his heart , and he long to be able to express the melody that be in his soul .
But he could not ; he have a harp and he often try to play on it ; but his clumsy finger only make such discord that his companion laugh at him and mock him , and call him a madman because he would not give it up , but would rather sit apart by himself , with his arm about his harp , look up into the sky , while they gather around their fire and tell tale to wile away their long night vigil a they watch their sheep on the hill .
But to him the thought that come out of the great silence be far sweet than their mirth ; and he never give up the hope , which sometimes leave his lip a a prayer , that some day he might be able to express those thought in music to the tire , weary , forgetful world .
On the first Christmas night he be out with his fellow shepherd on the hill .
It be chill and dark , and all , except him , be glad to gather around the fire .
He sit , a usual , by himself , with his harp on his knee and a great longing in his heart .
And there come a marvellous light in the sky and over the hill , a if the darkness of the night have suddenly blossom into a wonderful meadow of flowery flame ; and all the shepherd saw the angel and hear them sing .
And a they sing , the harp that the young shepherd hold begin to play softly by itself , and a he listen to it he realize that it be play the same music that the angel sang and that all his secret longing and aspiration and striving be express in it .
From that night , whenever he take the harp in his hand , it play the same music ; and he wander all over the world carry it ; wherever the sound of it music be hear hate and discord flee away and peace and good-will reign .
No one who hear it could think an evil thought ; no one could feel hopeless or despair or bitter or angry .
When a man have once hear that music it enter into his soul and heart and life and become a part of him for ever .
Years go by ; the shepherd grow old and bent and feeble ; but still he roam over land and sea , that his harp might carry the message of the Christmas night and the angel song to all mankind .
At last his strength fail him and he fell by the wayside in the darkness ; but his harp play a his spirit pass ; and it seem to him that a Shining One stood by him , with wonderful starry eye , and say to him , ` Lo , the music thy harp have play for so many year have be but the echo of the love and sympathy and purity and beauty in thine own soul ; and if at any time in the wandering thou hadst open the door of that soul to evil or envy or selfishness thy harp would have cease to play .
Now thy life be end ; but what thou hast give to mankind have no end ; and as long a the world last , so long will the heavenly music of the Christmas harp ring in the ear of men . '
When the sun rise the old shepherd lay dead by the roadside , with a smile on his face ; and in his hand be a harp with all it string break . ''
We leave the fir wood a the tale be end , and on the opposite hill be home .
A dim light in the kitchen window betoken that Aunt Janet have no idea of go to bed until all her young fry be safely house for the night .
`` Ma 's wait up for u , '' say Dan .
`` I 'd laugh if she happen to go to the door just a Felicity and Peter be strut up .
I guess she 'll be cross .
It 's nearly twelve . ''
`` Christmas will soon be over , '' say Cecily , with a sigh .
`` Has n't it be a nice one ?
It 's the first we 've all spent together .
Do you suppose we 'll ever spend another together ? ''
`` Lots of 'em , '' say Dan cheerily .
`` Why not ? ''
`` Oh , I do n't know , '' answer Cecily , her footstep lag somewhat .
`` Only thing seem just a little too pleasant to last . ''
`` If Willy Fraser have have a much spunk a Peter , Miss Cecily King might n't be so low spirit , '' quoth Dan , significantly .
Cecily toss her head and disdain reply .
There be really some remark a self-respecting young lady must ignore .
CHAPTER IV .
NEW YEAR RESOLUTIONS If we do not have a white Christmas we have a white New Year .
Midway between the two come a heavy snowfall .
It be winter in our orchard of old delight then , -- so truly winter that it be hard to believe summer have ever dwell in it , or that spring would ever return to it .
There be no bird to sing the music of the moon ; and the path where the apple blossom have fall be heap with less fragrant drift .
But it be a place of wonder on a moonlight night , when the snowy arcades shine like avenue of ivory and crystal , and the bare tree cast fairy-like tracery upon them .
Over Uncle Stephen 's Walk , where the snow have fall smoothly , a spell of white magic have be weave .
Taintless and wonderful it seem , like a street of pearl in the new Jerusalem .
On New Year 's Eve we be all together in Uncle Alec 's kitchen , which be tacitly give over to our revel during the winter evening .
The Story Girl and Peter be there , of course , and Sara Ray 's mother have allow her to come up on condition that she should be home by eight sharp .
Cecily be glad to see her , but the boy never hail her arrival with over-much delight , because , since the dark begin to come down early , Aunt Janet always make one of u walk down home with her .
We hat this , because Sara Ray be always so maddeningly self-conscious of have an escort .
We know perfectly well that next day in school she would tell her chum a a `` dead '' secret that `` So-and-So King saw her home '' from the hill farm the night before .
Now , see a young lady home from choice , and be send home with her by your aunt or mother be two entirely different thing , and we think Sara Ray ought to have sense enough to know it .
Outside there be a vivid rise of sunset behind the cold hill of fir , and the long reach of snowy field glow fairily pink in the western light .
The drift along the edge of the meadow and down the lane look a if a series of break wave have , by the lifting of a magician 's wand , be suddenly transform into marble , even to their toppling curl of foam .
Slowly the splendour die , give place to the mystic beauty of a winter twilight when the moon be rise .
The hollow sky be a cup of blue .
The star come out over the white glen and the earth be cover with a kingly carpet for the foot of the young year to press .
`` I 'm so glad the snow come , '' say the Story Girl .
`` If it have n't the New Year would have seem just a dingy and wear out a the old .
There 's something very solemn about the idea of a New Year , be n't there ?
Just think of three hundred and sixty-five whole day , with not a thing happen in them yet . ''
`` I do n't suppose anything very wonderful will happen in them , '' say Felix pessimistically .
To Felix , just then , life be flat , stale and unprofitable because it be his turn to go home with Sara Ray .
`` It make me a little frightened to think of all that may happen in them , '' say Cecily .
`` Miss Marwood say it be what we put into a year , not what we get out of it , that count at last . ''
`` I 'm always glad to see a New Year , '' say the Story Girl .
`` I wish we could do a they do in Norway .
The whole family sit up until midnight , and then , just a the clock be strike twelve , the father open the door and welcome the New Year in .
Is n't it a pretty custom ? ''
`` If ma would let u stay up till twelve we might do that too , '' say Dan , `` but she never will .
I call it mean . ''
`` If I ever have child I 'll let them stay up to watch the New Year in , '' say the Story Girl decidedly .
`` So will I , '' say Peter , `` but other night they 'll have to go to bed at seven . ''
`` You ought to be ashamed , speak of such thing , '' say Felicity , with a scandalized face .
Peter shrink into the background abash , no doubt believe that he have break some Family Guide precept all to piece .
`` I do n't know it be n't proper to mention child , '' he mutter apologetically .
`` We ought to make some New Year resolution , '' suggest the Story Girl .
`` New Year 's Eve be the time to make them . ''
`` I ca n't think of any resolution I want to make , '' say Felicity , who be perfectly satisfy with herself .
`` I could suggest a few to you , '' say Dan sarcastically .
`` There be so many I would like to make , '' say Cecily , `` that I 'm afraid it would n't be any use try to keep them all . ''
`` Well , let 's all make a few , just for the fun of it , and see if we can keep them , '' I say .
`` And let 's get paper and ink and write them out .
That will make them seem more solemn and binding . ''
`` And then pin them up on our bedroom wall , where we 'll see them every day , '' suggest the Story Girl , `` and every time we break a resolution we must put a cross opposite it .
That will show u what progress we be make , as well a make u ashamed if we have too many cross . ''
`` And let 's have a Roll of Honour in Our Magazine , '' suggest Felix , `` and every month we 'll publish the name of those who keep their resolution perfect . ''
`` I think it 's all nonsense , '' say Felicity .
But she join our circle around the table , though she sit for a long time with a blank sheet before her .
`` Let 's each make a resolution in turn , '' I say .
`` I 'll lead off . ''
And , recall with shame certain unpleasant difference of opinion I have lately have with Felicity , I write down in my best hand , `` I shall try to keep my temper always . ''
`` You 'd better , '' say Felicity tactfully .
It be Dan 's turn next .
`` I ca n't think of anything to start with , '' he say , gnaw his penholder fiercely .
`` You might make a resolution not to eat poison berry , '' suggest Felicity .
`` You 'd better make one not to nag people everlastingly , '' retort Dan .
`` Oh , do n't quarrel the last night of the old year , '' implore Cecily .
`` You might resolve not to quarrel any time , '' suggest Sara Ray .
`` No , sir , '' say Dan emphatically .
`` There 's no use make a resolution you CA N'T keep .
There be people in this family you 've just GOT to quarrel with if you want to live .
But I 've think of one -- I wo n't do thing to spite people . ''
Felicity -- who really be in an unbearable mood that night -- laugh disagreeably ; but Cecily give her a fierce nudge , which probably restrain her from speaking .
`` I will not eat any apple , '' write Felix .
`` What on earth do you want to give up eat apple for ? ''
ask Peter in astonishment .
`` Never mind , '' return Felix .
`` Apples make people fat , you know , '' say Felicity sweetly .
`` It seem a funny kind of resolution , '' I say doubtfully .
`` I think our resolution ought to be give up wrong thing or do right one . ''
`` You make your resolution to suit yourself and I 'll make mine to suit myself , '' say Felix defiantly .
`` I shall never get drunk , '' write Peter painstakingly .
`` But you never do , '' say the Story Girl in astonishment .
`` Well , it will be all the easy to keep the resolution , '' argue Peter .
`` That be n't fair , '' complain Dan .
`` If we all resolve not to do the thing we never do we 'd all be on the Roll of Honour . ''
`` You let Peter alone , '' say Felicity severely .
`` It 's a very good resolution and one everybody ought to make . ''
`` I shall not be jealous , '' write the Story Girl .
`` But be you ? ''
I ask , surprise .
The Story Girl colour and nod .
`` Of one thing , '' she confess , `` but I 'm not go to tell what it be . ''
`` I 'm jealous sometimes , too , '' confess Sara Ray , `` and so my first resolution will be ' I shall try not to feel jealous when I hear the other girl in school describe all the sick spell they 've have . ' ''
`` Goodness , do you want to be sick ? ''
demand Felix in astonishment .
`` It make a person important , '' explain Sara Ray .
`` I be go to try to improve my mind by read good book and listen to old people , '' write Cecily .
`` You get that out of the Sunday School paper , '' cry Felicity .
`` It do n't matter where I get it , '' say Cecily with dignity .
`` The main thing be to keep it . ''
`` It 's your turn , Felicity , '' I say .
Felicity toss her beautiful golden head .
`` I tell you I be n't go to make any resolution .
Go on yourself . ''
`` I shall always study my grammar lesson , '' I write -- I , who loathe grammar with a deadly loathing .
`` I hate grammar too , '' sigh Sara Ray .
`` It seem so unimportant . ''
Sara be rather fond of a big word , but do not always get hold of the right one .
I rather suspect that in the above instance she really mean uninteresting .
`` I wo n't get mad at Felicity , if I can help it , '' write Dan .
`` I 'm sure I never do anything to make you mad , '' exclaim Felicity .
`` I do n't think it 's polite to make resolution about your sister , '' say Peter .
`` He ca n't keep it anyway , '' scoff Felicity .
`` He 's get such an awful temper . ''
`` It 's a family failing , '' flash Dan , break his resolution ere the ink on it be dry .
`` There you go , '' taunt Felicity .
`` I 'll work all my arithmetic problem without any help , '' scribble Felix .
`` I wish I could resolve that , too , '' sigh Sara Ray , `` but it would n't be any use .
I 'd never be able to do those compound multiplication sum the teacher give u to do at home every night if I do n't get Judy Pineau to help me .
Judy be n't a good reader and she ca n't spell AT ALL , but you ca n't stick her in arithmetic as far a she go herself .
I feel sure , '' conclude poor Sara , in a hopeless tone , `` that I 'll NEVER be able to understand compound multiplication . '' ''
` Multiplication be vexation , Division be a bad , The rule of three perplexes me , And fraction drive me mad , ' '' quote Dan .
`` I have n't get as far a fraction yet , '' sigh Sara , `` and I hope I 'll be too big to go to school before I do .
I hate arithmetic , but I be PASSIONATELY fond of geography . ''
`` I will not play tit-tat-x on the fly leave of my hymn book in church , '' write Peter .
`` Mercy , do you ever do such a thing ? ''
exclaim Felicity in horror .
Peter nod shamefacedly .
`` Yes -- that Sunday Mr. Bailey preach .
He be so long-winded , I get awful tire , and , anyway , he be talk about thing I could n't understand , so I play tit-tat-x with one of the Markdale boy .
It be the day I be sit up in the gallery . ''
`` Well , I hope if you ever do the like again you wo n't do it in OUR pew , '' say Felicity severely .
`` I ai n't go to do it at all , '' say Peter .
`` I felt sort of mean all the rest of the day . ''
`` I shall try not to be vex when people interrupt me when I 'm tell story , '' write the Story Girl .
`` but it will be hard , '' she add with a sigh .
`` I never mind be interrupt , '' say Felicity .
`` I shall try to be cheerful and smile all the time , '' write Cecily .
`` You be , anyway , '' say Sara Ray loyally .
`` I do n't believe we ought to be cheerful ALL the time , '' say the Story Girl .
`` The Bible say we ought to weep with those who weep . ''
`` But maybe it mean that we 're to weep cheerfully , '' suggest Cecily .
`` Sorter a if you be think , ` I 'm very sorry for you but I 'm mighty glad I 'm not in the scrape too , ' '' say Dan .
`` Dan , do n't be irreverent , '' rebuke Felicity .
`` I know a story about old Mr. and Mrs. Davidson of Markdale , '' say the Story Girl .
`` She be always smile and it use to aggravate her husband , so one day he say very crossly , ` Old lady , what ARE you grin at ? '
` Oh , well , Abiram , everything 's so bright and pleasant , I 've just get to smile . '
`` Not long after there come a time when everything go wrong -- the crop fail and their best cow die , and Mrs. Davidson have rheumatism ; and finally Mr. Davidson fell and break his leg .
But still Mrs. Davidson smile .
` What in the dickens be you grin about now , old lady ? '
he demand .
` Oh , well , Abiram , ' she say , ` everything be so dark and unpleasant I 've just get to smile . '
` Well , ' say the old man crossly , ' I think you might give your face a rest sometimes . ' ''
`` I shall not talk gossip , '' write Sara Ray with a satisfied air .
`` Oh , do n't you think that 's a little TOO strict ? ''
ask Cecily anxiously .
`` Of course , it 's not right to talk MEAN gossip , but the harmless kind do n't hurt .
If I say to you that Emmy MacPhail be go to get a new fur collar this winter , THAT be harmless gossip , but if I say I do n't see how Emmy MacPhail can afford a new fur collar when her father ca n't pay my father for the oat he get from him , that would be MEAN gossip .
If I be you , Sara , I 'd put MEAN gossip . ''
Sara consent to this amendment .
`` I will be polite to everybody , '' be my third resolution , which pass without comment .
`` I 'll try not to use slang since Cecily do n't like it , '' write Dan .
`` I think some slang be real cute , '' say Felicity .
`` The Family Guide say it 's very vulgar , '' grin Dan .
`` Does n't it , Sara Stanley ? ''
`` Do n't disturb me , '' say the Story Girl dreamily .
`` I 'm just think a beautiful thought . ''
`` I 've think of a resolution to make , '' cry Felicity .
`` Mr. Marwood say last Sunday we should always try to think beautiful thought and then our life would be very beautiful .
So I shall resolve to think a beautiful thought every morning before breakfast . ''
`` Can you only manage one a day ? ''
queried Dan .
`` And why before breakfast ? ''
I ask .
`` Because it 's easy to think on an empty stomach , '' say Peter , in all good faith .
But Felicity shoot a furious glance at him .
`` I select that time , '' she explain with dignity , `` because when I 'm brush my hair before my glass in the morning I 'll see my resolution and remember it . ''
`` Mr. Marwood mean that ALL our thought ought to be beautiful , '' say the Story Girl .
`` If they be , people would n't be afraid to say what they think . ''
`` They ought n't to be afraid to , anyhow , '' say Felix stoutly .
`` I 'm go to make a resolution to say just what I think always . ''
`` And do you expect to get through the year alive if you do ? ''
ask Dan .
`` It might be easy enough to say what you think if you could always be sure just what you DO think , '' say the Story Girl .
`` So often I ca n't be sure . ''
`` How would you like it if people always say just what they think to you ? ''
ask Felicity .
`` I 'm not very particular what SOME people think of me , '' rejoin Felix .
`` I notice you do n't like to be tell by anybody that you 're fat , '' retort Felicity .
`` Oh , dear me , I do wish you would n't all say such sarcastic thing to each other , '' say poor Cecily plaintively .
`` It sound so horrid the last night of the old year .
Dear know where we 'll all be this night next year .
Peter , it 's your turn . ''
`` I will try , '' write Peter , `` to say my prayer every night regular , and not twice one night because I do n't expect to have time the next , -- like I do the night before the party , '' he add .
`` I s ` pose you never say your prayer until we get you to go to church , '' say Felicity -- who have have no hand in induce Peter to go to church , but have stoutly oppose it , a record in the first volume of our family history .
`` I do , too , '' say Peter .
`` Aunt Jane teach me to say my prayer .
Ma have n't time , be a father have run away ; ma have to wash at night same a in day-time . ''
`` I shall learn to cook , '' write the Story Girl , frowning .
`` You 'd better resolve not to make pudding of -- '' begin Felicity , then stop as suddenly a if she have bite off the rest of her sentence and swallow it .
Cecily have nudge her , so she have probably remember the Story Girl 's threat that she would never tell another story if she be ever twit with the pudding she have make from sawdust .
But we all know what Felicity have start to say and the Story Girl deal her a most uncousinly glance .
`` I will not cry because mother wo n't starch my apron , '' write Sara Ray .
`` Better resolve not to cry about anything , '' say Dan kindly .
Sara Ray shake her head forlornly .
`` That would be too hard to keep .
There be time when I HAVE to cry .
It 's a relief . ''
`` Not to the folk who have to hear you , '' mutter Dan aside to Cecily .
`` Oh , hush , '' whisper Cecily back .
`` Do n't go and hurt her feeling the last night of the old year .
Is it my turn again ?
Well , I 'll resolve not to worry because my hair be not curly .
But , oh , I 'll never be able to help wish it be . ''
`` Why do n't you curl it a you use to do , then ? ''
ask Dan .
`` You know very well that I 've never put my hair up in curl paper since the time Peter be die of the measles , '' say Cecily reproachfully .
`` I resolve then I would n't because I be n't sure it be quite right . ''
`` I will keep my finger-nails neat and clean , '' I write .
`` There , that 's four resolution .
I 'm not go to make any more .
Four 's enough . ''
`` I shall always think twice before I speak , '' write Felix .
`` That 's an awful waste of time , '' comment Dan , `` but I guess you 'll need to if you 're always go to say what you think . ''
`` I 'm go to stop with three , '' say Peter .
`` I will have all the good time I can , '' write the Story Girl .
`` THAT 'S what I call sensible , '' say Dan .
`` It 's a very easy resolution to keep , anyhow , '' comment Felix .
`` I shall try to like read the Bible , '' write Sara Ray .
`` You ought to like read the Bible without try to , '' exclaim Felicity .
`` If you have to read seven chapter of it every time you be naughty I do n't believe you would like it either , '' retort Sara Ray with a flash of spirit .
`` I shall try to believe only half of what I hear , '' be Cecily 's conclude resolution .
`` But which half ? ''
scoffed Dan .
`` The best half , '' say sweet Cecily simply .
`` I 'll try to obey mother ALWAYS , '' write Sara Ray , with a tremendous sigh , a if she fully realize the difficulty of keep such a resolution .
`` And that 's all I 'm go to make . ''
`` Felicity have only make one , '' say the Story Girl .
`` I think it good to make just one and keep it than make a lot and break them , '' say Felicity loftily .
She have the last word on the subject , for it be time for Sara Ray to go , and our circle break up .
Sara and Felix depart and we watch them down the lane in the moonlight -- Sara walk demurely in one runner track , and Felix stalk grimly along in the other .
I fear the romantic beauty of that silver shin night be entirely throw away on my mischievous brother .
And it be , a I remember it , a most exquisite night -- a white poem , a frosty , starry lyric of light .
It be one of those night on which one might fall asleep and dream happy dream of garden of mirth and song , feel all the while through one 's sleep the soft splendour and radiance of the white moon-world outside , a one hear soft , far-away music sound through the thought and word that be bear of it .
As a matter of fact , however , Cecily dream that night that she saw three full moon in the sky , and waken up cry with the horror of it .
CHAPTER V .
THE FIRST NUMBER OF `` OUR MAGAZINE '' The first number of Our Magazine be ready on New Year 's Day , and we read it that even in the kitchen .
All our staff have work nobly and we be enormously proud of the result , although Dan still continue to scoff at a paper that be n't print .

It open with a short EDITORIAL With this number Our Magazine make it first bow to the public .
All the editor have do their best and the various department be full of valuable information and amusement .
The tastefully design cover be by a famous artist , Mr. Blair Stanley , who send it to u all the way from Europe at the request of his daughter .
Mr. Peter Craig , our enterprising literary editor , contribute a touching love story .
-LRB- Peter , aside , in a gratified pig 's whisper : `` I never be call ` Mr. ' before . '' -RRB-
Miss Felicity King 's essay on Shakespeare be none the worse for be an old school composition , a it be new to most of our reader .
Miss Cecily King contribute a thrilling article of adventure .
The various department be ably edit , and we feel that we have reason to be proud of Our Magazine .
But we shall not rest on our oar .
`` Excelsior '' shall ever be our motto .
We trust that each succeed issue will be good than the one that go before .
We be well aware of many defect , but it be easy to see them than to remedy them .
Any suggestion that would tend to the improvement of Our Magazine will be thankfully receive , but we trust that no criticism will be make that will hurt anyone 's feeling .
Let u all work together in harmony , and strive to make Our Magazine an influence for good and a source of innocent pleasure , and let u always remember the word of the poet .
`` The height by great men reach and kept Were not attain by sudden flight , But they , while their companion sleep , Were toil upwards in the night . ''
