ESSAY ON SHAKESPEARE Shakespeare 's full name be William Shakespeare .
He do not always spell it the same way .
He live in the reign of Queen Elizabeth and write a great many play .
His play be write in dialogue form .
Some people think they be not write by Shakespeare but by another man of the same name .
I have read some of them because our school teacher say everybody ought to read them , but I do not care much for them .
There be some thing in them I can not understand .
I like the story of Valeria H. Montague in the Family Guide ever so much good .
They be more exciting and truer to life .
Romeo and Juliet be one of the play I read .
It be very sad .
Juliet dy and I do n't like story where people die .
I like it well when they all get marry especially to duke and earl .
Shakespeare himself be marry to Anne Hatheway .
They be both dead now .
They have be dead a good while .
He be a very famous man .

THE STORY OF AN ELOPEMENT FROM CHURCH This be a true story .
It happen in Markdale to an uncle of my mother .
He want to marry Miss Jemima Parr .
Felicity say Jemima be not a romantic name for a heroin of a story but I cant help it in this case because it be a true story and her name realy be Jemima .
My mother uncle be name Thomas Taylor .
He be poor at that time and so the father of Miss Jemima Parr do not want him for a soninlaw and tell him he be not to come near the house or he would set the dog on him .
Miss Jemima Parr be very pretty and my mother uncle Thomas be just crazy about her and she want him too .
She cry almost every night after her father forbid him to come to the house except the night she have to sleep or she would have die .
And she be so frightened he might try to come for all and get tore up by the dog and it be a bull-dog too that would never let go .
But mother uncle Thomas be too cute for that .
He wait till one day there be preach in the Markdale church in the middle of the week because it be sacrament time and Miss Jemima Parr and her family all go because her father be an elder .
My mother uncle Thomas go too and set in the pew just behind Miss Jemima Parrs family .
When they all bow their head at prayer time Miss Jemima Parr didnt but set bolt uprite and my mother uncle Thomas bent over and wispered in her ear .
I dont know what he say so I cant right it but Miss Jemima Parr blush that be turn red and nod her head .
Perhaps some people may think that my mother uncle Thomas shouldent of wispered at prayer time in church but you must remember that Miss Jemima Parrs father have thretened to set the dog on him and that be hard line when he be a respektable young man though not rich .
Well when they be sing the last sam my mother uncle Thomas get up and go out very quitely and as soon a church be out Miss Jemima Parr walk out too real quick .
Her family never suspekted anything and they hang round talk to folk and shake hand while Miss Jemima Parr and my mother uncle Thomas be elope outside .
And what do you suppose they elope in .
Why in Miss Jemima Parrs father slay .
And when he go out they be go and his slay be go also his horse .
Of course my mother uncle Thomas didnt steal the horse .
He just borroed it and send it home the next day .
But before Miss Jemima Parrs father could get another rig to follow them they be so far away he couldent catch them before they get marry .
And they live happy together forever afterwards .
Mothers uncle Thomas live to be a very old man .
He die very suddent .
He felt quite well when he go to sleep and when he wake up he be dead .
PETER CRAIG .
MY MOST EXCITING ADVENTURE The editor say we must all write up our most exciting adventure for Our Magazine .
My most exciting adventure happen a year ago last November .
I be nearly frighten to death .
Dan say he would n't of be scar and Felicity say she would of know what it be but it 's easy to talk .
It happen the night I go down to see Kitty Marr .
I think when I go that Aunt Olivia be visit there and I could come home with her .
But she be n't there and I have to come home alone .
Kitty come a piece of the way but she would n't come any further than Uncle James Frewen 's gate .
She say it be because it be so windy she be afraid she would get the tooth-ache and not because she be frighten of the ghost of the dog that haunt the bridge in Uncle James ' hollow .
I do wish she have n't say anything about the dog because I might n't of think about it if she have n't .
I have to go on alone thinking of it .
I 'd hear the story often but I 'd never believe in it .
They say the dog use to appear at one end of the bridge and walk across it with people and vanish when he get to the other end .
He never try to bite anyone but one would n't want to meet the ghost of a dog even if one do n't believe in him .
I know there be no such thing a ghost and I keep say a paraphrase over to myself and the Golden Text of the next Sunday School lesson but oh , how my heart beat when I get near the hollow !
It be so dark .
You could just see thing dim-like but you could n't see what they be .
When I get to the bridge I walk along sideways with my back to the rail so I could n't think the dog be behind me .
And then just in the middle of the bridge I meet something .
It be right before me and it be big and black , just about the size of a Newfoundland dog , and I think I could see a white nose .
And it keep jump about from one side of the bridge to the other .
Oh , I hope none of my reader will ever be so frightened a I be then .
I be too frighten to run back because I be afraid it would chase me and I could n't get past it , it move so quick , and then it just make one spring right on me and I felt it claw and I scream and fell down .
It roll off to one side and laid there quite quiet but I do n't dare move and I do n't know what would have become of me if Amos Cowan have n't come along that very minute with a lantern .
And there be me sit in the middle of the bridge and that awful thing beside me .
And what do you think it be but a big umbrella with a white handle ?
Amos say it be his umbrella and it have blow away from him and he have to go back and get the lantern to look for it .
I felt like ask him what on earth he be go about with an umbrella open when it wasent rain .
But the Cowans do such queer thing .
You remember the time Jerry Cowan sell u God 's picture .
Amos take me right home and I be thankful for I do n't know what would have become of me if he have n't come along .
I could n't sleep all night and I never want to have any more adventure like that one .

CHAPTER VI .
GREAT-AUNT ELIZA 'S VISIT It be a diamond winter day in February -- clear , cold , hard , brilliant .
The sharp blue sky shone , the white field and hill glitter , the fringe of icicle around the eaves of Uncle Alec 's house sparkle .
Keen be the frost and crisp the snow over our world ; and we young fry of the King household be all agog to enjoy life -- for be it not Saturday , and be we not leave all alone to keep house ?
Aunt Janet and Aunt Olivia have have their last big `` kill '' of market poultry the day before ; and early in the morning all our grown-ups set forth to Charlottetown , to be go the whole day .
They leave u many charge a usual , some of which we remember and some of which we forget ; but with Felicity in command none of u dare stray far out of line .
The Story Girl and Peter come over , of course , and we all agree that we would haste and get the work do in the forenoon , that we might have an afternoon of uninterrupted enjoyment .
A taffy-pull after dinner and then a jolly hour of coast on the hill field before supper be on our programme .
But disappointment be our portion .
We do manage to get the taffy make but before we could sample the result satisfactorily , and just a the girl be finish with the washing of the dish , Felicity glance out of the window and exclaim in tone of dismay , `` Oh , dear me , here 's Great-aunt Eliza come up the lane !
Now , be n't that too mean ? ''
We all look out to see a tall , gray-haired lady approach the house , look about her with the slightly puzzle air of a stranger .
We have be expect Great-aunt Eliza 's advent for some week , for she be visit relative in Markdale .
We know she be liable to pounce down on u any time , be one of those delightful folk who like to `` surprise '' people , but we have never think of her come that particular day .
It must be confess that we do not look forward to her visit with any pleasure .
None of u have ever see her , but we know she be very deaf , and have very decided opinion a to the way in which child should behave .
`` Whew ! ''
whistle Dan .
`` We 're in for a jolly afternoon .
She 's deaf a a post and we 'll have to split our throat to make her hear at all .
I 've a notion to skin out . ''
`` Oh , do n't talk like that , Dan , '' say Cecily reproachfully .
`` She 's old and lonely and have have a great deal of trouble .
She have bury three husband .
We must be kind to her and do the best we can to make her visit pleasant . ''
`` She 's come to the back door , '' say Felicity , with an agitated glance around the kitchen .
`` I tell you , Dan , that you should have shovel the snow away from the front door this morning .
Cecily , set those pot in the pantry quick -- hide those boot , Felix -- shut the cupboard door , Peter -- Sara , straighten up the lounge .
She 's awfully particular and ma say her house be always as neat a wax . ''
To do Felicity justice , while she issue order to the rest of u , she be fly busily about herself , and it be amaze how much be accomplish in the way of put the kitchen in perfect order during the two minute in which Great-aunt Eliza be cross the yard .
`` Fortunately the sitting-room be tidy and there 's plenty in the pantry , '' say Felicity , who could face anything undauntedly with a well-stocked larder behind her .
Further conversation be cut short by a decided rap at the door .
Felicity open it .
`` Why , how do you do , Aunt Eliza ? ''
she say loudly .
A slightly bewilder look appear on Aunt Eliza 's face .
Felicity perceive she have not speak loudly enough .
`` How do you do , Aunt Eliza , '' she repeat at the top of her voice .
`` Come in -- we be glad to see you .
We 've be look for you for ever so long . ''
`` Are your father and mother at home ? ''
ask Aunt Eliza , slowly .
`` No , they go to town today .
But they 'll be home this evening . ''
`` I 'm sorry they 're away , '' say Aunt Eliza , come in , `` because I can stay only a few hour . ''
`` Oh , that 's too bad , '' shout poor Felicity , dart an angry glance at the rest of u , a if to demand why we do n't help her out .
`` Why , we 've be think you 'd stay a week with u anyway .
You MUST stay over Sunday . ''
`` I really ca n't .
I have to go to Charlottetown tonight , '' return Aunt Eliza .
`` Well , you 'll take off your thing and stay to tea , at least , '' urge Felicity , as hospitably a her strained vocal chord would admit .
`` Yes , I think I 'll do that .
I want to get acquaint with my -- my nephew and niece , '' say Aunt Eliza , with a rather pleasant glance around our group .
If I could have associate the thought of such a thing with my preconception of Great-aunt Eliza I could have swear there be a twinkle in her eye .
But of course it be impossible .
`` Wo n't you introduce yourselves , please ? ''
Felicity shout our name and Great-aunt Eliza shake hand all round .
She perform the duty grimly and I conclude I must have be mistake about the twinkle .
She be certainly very tall and dignified and imposing -- altogether a great-aunt to be respect .
Felicity and Cecily take her to the spare room and then leave her in the sitting-room while they return to the kitchen , to discuss the matter in family conclave .
`` Well , and what do you think of dear Aunt Eliza ? ''
ask Dan .
`` S-s-s-sh , '' warn Cecily , with a glance at the half-open hall door .
`` Pshaw , '' scoff Dan , `` she ca n't hear u .
There ought to be a law against anyone be as deaf a that . ''
`` She 's not so old-looking a I expect , '' say Felix .
`` If her hair be n't so white she would n't look much old than your mother . ''
`` You do n't have to be very old to be a great-aunt , '' say Cecily .
`` Kitty Marr have a great-aunt who be just the same age a her mother .
I expect it be bury so many husband turn her hair white .
But Aunt Eliza do n't look just a I expect she would either . ''
`` She 's dress more stylishly than I expect , '' say Felicity .
`` I think she 'd be real old-fashioned , but her clothes be n't too bad at all . ''

She 'll think we have no manner . ''
Accordingly we all file in rather reluctantly .
Great-aunt Eliza be toast her toe -- clad , a we note , in very smart and shapely shoe -- at the stove and look quite at her ease .

She do her brave best but she could not shout like Felicity , and half the time , a she confide to me later on , she felt that Great-aunt Eliza do not hear one word she say , because she do n't seem to take in who the people be , though , just like all deaf folk , she would n't let on .
Great-aunt Eliza certainly do n't talk much ; she look at the photograph in silence , but she smile now and then .
That smile bother me .
It be so twinkly and so very un-great-aunt-Elizaish .
But I felt indignant with her .
I think she might have show a little more appreciation of Cecily 's gallant effort to entertain .
It be very dull for the rest of u .
The Story Girl sit rather sulkily in her corner ; she be angry because Felicity would not let her make the rusk , and also , perhaps , a little vexed because she could not charm Great-aunt Eliza with her golden voice and story-telling gift .

In vain Cecily implore him to stop .
It be too good fun to give up .

CHAPTER VII .
WE VISIT COUSIN MATTIE 'S One Saturday in March we walk over to Baywater , for a long-talked-of visit to Cousin Mattie Dilke .
By the road , Baywater be six mile away , but there be a short cut across hill and field and wood which be scantly three .
We do not look forward to our visit with any particular delight , for there be nobody at Cousin Mattie 's except grown-ups who have be grow up so long that it be rather hard for them to remember they have ever be child .
But , a Felicity tell u , it be necessary to visit Cousin Mattie at least once a year , or else she would be `` huffed , '' so we conclude we might as well go and have it over .

`` Cousin Mattie 's a great cook and there 's nothing stingy about her . ''

He invariably meet her criticism with a good-natured grin and a flippant remark with some tender epithet tag on to it .
Poor Felicity use to get hopelessly furious over it .

The walking be good , for there have lately be a thaw and everything be frozen .
We go over field , cross by spidery trail of gray fence , where the withered grass stick forlornly up through the snow ; we linger for a time in a group of hill pine , great , majestic tree-creatures , friend of even star ; and finally strike into the belt of fir and maple which intervene between Carlisle and Baywater .
It be in this locality that Peg Bowen live , and our way lay near her house though not directly in sight of it .
We hop we would not meet her , for since the affair of the bewitchment of Paddy we do not know quite what to think of Peg ; the bold of u hold his breath a we pass her haunt , and draw it again with a sigh of relief when they be safely leave behind .
The wood be full of the brooding stillness that often precede a storm , and the wind crept along their white , cone-sprinkled floor with a low , wail cry .

`` I know a story about Cousin Mattie 's husband , '' say the Story Girl .
`` His name be Ebenezer , you know -- '' `` Is it any wonder he be thin and stunt look ? ''
say Dan .
`` Ebenezer be just a nice a name a Daniel , '' say Felicity .
`` Do you REALLY think so , my angel ? ''

One day Cousin Ebenezer come up the hill and into the kitchen where all the family be .

At last he get up and say in a desperate sort of way , ` Uncle Abraham , can I speak with you in private for a minute ? '

CHAPTER VIII .
WE VISIT PEG BOWEN We leave Cousin Mattie 's early , for it still look like a storm , though no more so than it have in the morning .
We intend to go home by a different path -- one lead through clear land overgrow with scrub maple , which have the advantage of be farther away from Peg Bowen 's house .
We hop to be home before it begin to storm , but we have hardly reach the hill above the village when a fine , drive snow begin to fall .
It would have be wise to have turn back even then ; but we have already come a mile and we think we would have ample time to reach home before it become really bad .
We be sadly mistake ; by the time we have go another half-mile we be in the thick of a bewildering , blind snowstorm .
But it be by now just a far back to Cousin Mattie 's a it be to Uncle Alec 's , so we struggle on , grow more frightened at every step .
We could hardly face the stinging snow , and we could not see ten foot ahead of u .
It have turn bitterly cold and the tempest howl all around u in white desolation under the fast-darkening night .
The narrow path we be try to follow soon become entirely obliterate and we stumble blindly on , hold to each other , and try to peer through the furious whirl that fill the air .
Our plight have come upon u so suddenly that we could not realize it .
Presently Peter , who be lead the van because he be suppose to know the path best , stop .
`` I ca n't see the road any long , '' he shout .
`` I do n't know where we be . ''
We all stop and huddle together in a miserable group .
Fear fill our heart .
It seem age ago that we have be snug and safe and warm at Cousin Mattie 's .
Cecily begin to cry with cold .
Dan , in spite of her protest , drag off his overcoat and make her put it on .

`` We 'll all freeze to death if we do .
Come on -- we 've get to keep moving .
The snow ai n't so deep yet .
Take hold of my hand , Cecily .
We must all hold together .
Come , now . ''
`` It wo n't be nice to be frozen to death , but if we get through alive think what a story we 'll have to tell , '' say the Story Girl between her chatter teeth .
In my heart I do not believe we would ever get through alive .
It be almost pitch dark now , and the snow grow deep every moment .
We be chill to the heart .
I think how nice it would be to lie down and rest ; but I remember hear that that be fatal , and I endeavour to stumble on with the others .
It be wonderful how the girl keep up , even Cecily .
It occur to me to be thankful that Sara Ray be not with u .
But we be wholly lose now .
All around u be a horror of great darkness .

shout Dan to Peter .

I have n't any idea where home be . ''
Home !
Would we ever see it again ?
We try to urge Felicity on , but she only repeat drowsily that she must lie down and rest .
Cecily , too , be reel against me .
The Story Girl still stand up staunchly and counsel struggle on , but she be numb with cold and her word be hardly distinguishable .

Suddenly Felix give a shout .
`` I see a light , '' he cry .
`` Where ?
Where ? ''
We all look but could see nothing .
`` I do n't see it now but I saw it a moment ago , '' shout Felix .
`` I 'm sure I do .
Come on -- over in this direction . ''
Inspired with fresh hope we hurry after him .

A few more step and , come into the shelter of the woodland on the further side , we realize where we be .
`` That 's Peg Bowen 's house , '' exclaim Peter , stop short in dismay .
`` I do n't care whose house it be , '' declare Dan .
`` We 've get to go to it . ''

`` I 'll be thankful to get in anywhere . ''
We reach the house , climb the flight of step that lead to that mysterious second story door , and Dan rap .
The door open promptly and Peg Bowen stand before u , in what seem exactly the same costume she have wear on the memorable day when we have come , bear gift , to propitiate her in the matter of Paddy .
`` Behind her be a dim room scantly illumine by the one small candle that have guide u through the storm ; but the old Waterloo stove be colour the gloom with tremulous , rose-red whorl of light , and warm and cosy indeed seem Peg 's retreat to u snow-covered , frost-chilled , benighted wanderer .
`` Gracious goodness , where do yez all come from ? ''

`` Did they turn yez out ? ''

`` We do n't know where we be till we saw your light .
I guess we 'll have to stay here till the storm be over -- if you do n't mind . ''
`` And if it wo n't inconvenience you , '' say Cecily timidly .
`` Oh , it 's no inconvenience to speak of .
Come in .
Well , yez HAVE get some snow on yez .
Let me get a broom .
You boys stomp your foot well and shake your coat .
You girls give me your thing and I 'll hang them up .
Guess yez be most froze .
Well , sit up to the stove and git het up . ''
Peg bustle away to gather up a dubious assortment of chair , with back and rung miss , and in a few minute we be in a circle around her roaring stove , get dry and thaw out .
In our wild flight of fancy we have never picture ourselves a guest at the witch 's hearth-stone .
Yet here we be ; and the witch herself be actually brew a jorum of ginger tea for Cecily , who continue to shiver long after the rest of u be roast to the marrow .
Poor Sis drink that scald draught , be in too great awe of Peg to do aught else .
`` That 'll soon fix your shiver , '' say our hostess kindly .
`` And now I 'll get yez all some tea . ''
`` Oh , please do n't trouble , '' say the Story Girl hastily . ''
` Tai n't any trouble , '' say Peg briskly ; then , with one of the sudden change to fierceness which make her such a terrifying personage , `` Do yez think my vittels ai n't clean ? ''
`` Oh , no , no , '' cry Felicity quickly , before the Story Girl could speak , `` none of u would ever think THAT .
Sara only mean she do n't want you to go to any bother on our account . ''
`` It ai n't any bother , '' say Peg , mollify .
`` I 'm spry a a cricket this winter , though I have the realagy sometimes .
Many a good bite I 've have in your ma 's kitchen .
I owe yez a meal . ''
No more protest be make .
We sit in awed silence , gaze with timid curiosity about the room , the stain , plaster wall of which be well-nigh cover with a motley assortment of picture , chromos , and advertisement , paste on without much regard for order or character .
We have hear much of Peg 's pet and now we saw them .
Six cat occupy various cosy corner ; one of them , the black goblin which have so terrified u in the summer , blink satirically at u from the centre of Peg 's bed .
Another , a dilapidated , strip beastie , with both ear and one eye go , glare at u from the sofa in the corner .
A dog , with only three leg , lay behind the stove ; a crow sit on a roost above our head , in company with a matronly old hen ; and on the clock shelf be a stuffed monkey and a grinning skull .
We have hear that a sailor have give Peg the monkey .
But where have she get the skull ?
And whose be it ?
I could not help puzzle over these gruesome question .
Presently tea be ready and we gather around the festal board -- a board literally as well a figuratively , for Peg 's table be the work of her own unskilled hand .
The le say about the viand of that meal , and the dish they be serve in , the good .
But we eat them -- bless you , yes !
-- a we would have eat any witch 's banquet set before u .
Peg might or might not be a witch -- common sense say not ; but we know she be quite capable of turn every one of u out of door in one of her sudden fierce fit if we offend her ; and we have no mind to trust ourselves again to that wild forest where we have fight a lose fight with the demon force of night and storm .
But it be not an agreeable meal in more way than one .
Peg be not at all careful of anybody 's feeling .
She hurt Felix 's cruelly a she pass him his cup of tea .
`` You 've go too much to flesh , boy .
So the magic seed do n't work , hey ? ''
How in the world have Peg find out about that magic seed ?
Felix look uncommonly foolish .
`` If you 'd come to me in the first place I 'd soon have tell you how to get thin , '' say Peg , nod wisely .
`` Wo n't you tell me now ? ''
ask Felix eagerly , his desire to melt his too solid flesh overcome his dread and shame .
`` No , I do n't like be second fiddle , '' answer Peg with a crafty smile .
`` Sara , you 're too scrawny and pale -- not much like your ma .
I know her well .
She be count a beauty , but she make no great thing of a match .
Your father have some money but he be a tramp like meself .
Where be he now ? ''
`` In Rome , '' say the Story Girl rather shortly .
`` People think your ma be crazy when she take him .
But she 'd a right to please herself .
Folks be too ready to call other folk crazy .
There 's people who say I 'M not in my right mind .
Did yez ever '' -- Peg fix Felicity with a piercing glance -- `` hear anything so ridiculous ? ''
`` Never , '' say Felicity , white to the lip .
`` I wish everybody be as sane a I be , '' say Peg scornfully .
Then she look poor Felicity over critically .
`` You 're good-looking but proud .
And your complexion wo n't wear .
It 'll be like your ma 's yet -- too much red in it . ''
`` Well , that 's good than be the colour of mud , '' mutter Peter , who be n't go to hear his lady traduce , even by a witch .
All the thanks he get be a furious look from Felicity , but Peg have not hear him and now she turn her attention to Cecily .
`` You look delicate .
I daresay you 'll never live to grow up . ''
Cecily 's lip tremble and Dan 's face turn crimson .
`` Shut up , '' he say to Peg .
`` You 've no business to say such thing to people . ''
I think my jaw drop .
I know Peter 's and Felix 's do .
Felicity break in wildly .
`` Oh , do n't mind him , Miss Bowen .
He 's get SUCH a temper -- that 's just the way he talk to u all at home .
PLEASE excuse him . ''
`` Bless you , I do n't mind him , '' say Peg , from whom the unexpected seem to be the thing to expect .
`` I like a lad of spurrit .
And so your father run away , do he , Peter ?
He use to be a beau of mine -- he see me home three time from sing school when we be young .
Some folk say he do it for a dare .
There 's such a lot of jealousy in the world , ai n't there ?
Do you know where he be now ? ''
`` No , '' say Peter .
`` Well , he 's come home before long , '' say Peg mysteriously .
`` Who tell you that ? ''
cry Peter in amazement .
`` Better not ask , '' respond Peg , look up at the skull .
If she mean to make the flesh creep on our bone she succeed .
But now , much to our relief , the meal be over and Peg invite u to draw our chair up to the stove again .
`` Make yourselves at home , '' she say , produce her pipe from her pocket .
`` I ai n't one of the kind who think their house too good to live in .
Guess I wo n't bother wash the dish .
They 'll do yez for breakfast if yez do n't forget your place .
I s ` pose none of yez smoke . ''
`` No , '' say Felicity , rather primly .
`` Then yez do n't know what 's good for yez , '' retort Peg , rather grumpily .
But a few whiff of her pipe placate her and , observe Cecily sigh , she ask her kindly what be the matter .
`` I 'm think how worried they 'll be at home about u , '' explain Cecily .
`` Bless you , dearie , do n't be worry over that .
I 'll send them word that yez be all snug and safe here . ''
`` But how can you ? ''
cry amazed Cecily .
`` Better not ask , '' say Peg again , with another glance at the skull .
An uncomfortable silence follow , finally break by Peg , who introduce her pet to u and tell how she have come by them .
The black cat be her favourite .
`` That cat know more than I do , if yez 'll believe it , '' she say proudly .
`` I 've get a rat too , but he 's a bit shy when stranger be round .
Your cat get all right again that time , do n't he ? ''
`` Yes , '' say the Story Girl .
`` Thought he would , '' say Peg , nod sagely .
`` I see to that .
Now , do n't yez all be star at the hole in my dress . ''
`` We be n't , '' be our chorus of protest .
`` Looked a if yez be .
I tear that yesterday but I do n't mend it .
I be bring up to believe that a hole be an accident but a patch be a disgrace .
And so your Aunt Olivia be go to be marry after all ? ''
This be news to u .
We felt and look daze .
`` I never hear anything of it , '' say the Story Girl .
`` Oh , it 's true enough .
She 's a great fool .
I 've no faith in husband .
But one good thing be she ai n't go to marry that Henry Jacobs of Markdale .
He want her bad enough .
Just like his presumption , -- think himself good enough for a King .
His father be the bad man alive .
He chase me off his place with his dog once .
But I 'll get even with him yet . ''
Peg look very savage , and vision of burn barn float through our mind .
`` He 'll be punish in hell , you know , '' say Peter timidly .
`` But I wo n't be there to see that , '' rejoin Peg .
`` Some folk say I 'll go there because I do n't go to church oftener .
But I do n't believe it . ''
`` Why do n't you go ? ''
ask Peter , with a temerity that border on rashness .
`` Well , I 've get so sunburned I 'm afraid folk might take me for an Injun , '' explain Peg , quite seriously .
`` Besides , your minister make such awful long prayer .
Why do he do it ? ''
`` I suppose he find it easy to talk to God than to people , '' suggest Peter reflectively .
`` Well , anyway , I belong to the round church , '' say Peg comfortably , `` and so the devil ca n't catch ME at the corner .
I have n't be to Carlisle church for over three year .
I think I 'd a-died laugh the last time I be there .
Old Elder Marr take up the collection that day .
He 'd on a pair of new boot and they squeak all the way up and down the aisle .
And every time the boot squeak the elder make a face , like he have toothache .
It be awful funny .
How 's your missionary quilt come on , Cecily ? ''
Was there anything Peg do n't know ?
`` Very well , '' say Cecily .
`` You can put my name on it , if you want to . ''
`` Oh , thank you .
Which section -- the five-cent one or the ten-cent one ? ''
ask Cecily timidly .
`` The ten-cent one , of course .
The best be none too good for me .
I 'll give you the ten cent another time .
I 'm short of change just now -- not be as rich a Queen Victory .
There 's her picture up there -- the one with the blue sash and diamint crown and the lace curting on her head .
Can any of yez tell me this -- be Queen Victory a married woman ? ''
`` Oh , yes , but her husband be dead , '' answer the Story Girl .
`` Well , I s ` pose they could n't have call her an old maid , see she be a queen , even if she 'd never get marry .
Sometimes I sez to myself , ` Peg , would you like to be Queen Victory ? '
But I never know what to answer .
In summer , when I can roam anywhere in the wood and the sunshine -- I would n't be Queen Victory for anything .
But when it 's winter and cold and I ca n't git nowhere -- I feel a if I would n't mind change place with her . ''
Peg put her pipe back in her mouth and begin to smoke fiercely .
The candle wick burn long , and be top by a little cap of fiery red that seem to wink at u like an impish gnome .
The most grotesque shadow of Peg flicker over the wall behind her .
The one-eyed cat remit his grim watch and go to sleep .
Outside the wind scream like a ravening beast at the window .
Suddenly Peg remove her pipe from her mouth , bent forward , grip my wrist with her sinewy finger until I almost cry out with pain , and gazed straight into my face .
I felt horribly frighten of her .
She seem an entirely different creature .
A wild light be in her eye , a furtive , animal-like expression be on her face .
When she speak it be in a different voice and in different language .
`` Do you hear the wind ? ''
she ask in a thrilling whisper .
`` What IS the wind ?
What IS the wind ? ''
`` I -- I -- do n't know , '' I stammer .
`` No more do I , '' say Peg , `` and nobody know .
Nobody know what the wind be .
I wish I could find out .
I might n't be so afraid of the wind if I know what it be .
I be afraid of it .
When the blast come like that I want to crouch down and hide me .
But I can tell you one thing about the wind -- it 's the only free thing in the world -- THE -- ONLY -- FREE -- THING .
Everything else be subject to some law , but the wind be FREE .
It bloweth where it listeth and no man can tame it .
It 's free -- that 's why I love it , though I 'm afraid of it .
It 's a grand thing to be free -- free free -- free ! ''
Peg 's voice rise almost to a shriek .
We be dreadfully frighten , for we know there be time when she be quite crazy and we fear one of her `` spell '' be come on her .
But with a swift movement she turn the man 's coat she wear up over her shoulder and head like a hood , completely hide her face .
Then she crouch forward , elbow on knee , and relapse into silence .
None of u dared speak or move .
We sit thus for half an hour .
Then Peg jump up and say briskly in her usual tone , `` Well , I guess yez be all sleepy and ready for bed .
You girls can sleep in my bed over there , and I 'll take the sofy .
Yez can put the cat off if yez like , though he wo n't hurt yez .
You boys can go downstairs .
There 's a big pile of straw there that 'll do yez for a bed , if yez put your coat on .
I 'll light yez down , but I ai n't go to leave yez a light for fear yez 'd set fire to the place . ''
Saying good-night to the girl , who look a if they think their last hour be come , we go to the low room .
It be quite empty , save for a pile of fire wood and another of clean straw .
Casting a stealthy glance around , ere Peg withdraw the light , I be relieve to see that there be no skull in sight .
We four boy snuggle down in the straw .
We do not expect to sleep , but we be very tired and before we know it our eye be shut , to open no more till morning .
The poor girl be not so fortunate .
They always aver they never close an eye .
Four thing prevent them from sleep .
In the first place Peg snore loudly ; in the second place the fitful gleam of firelight kept flicker over the skull for half the night and make gruesome effect on it ; in the third place Peg 's pillow and bedclothes smell rankly of tobacco smoke ; and in the fourth place they be afraid the rat Peg have speak of might come out to make their acquaintance .
Indeed , they be sure they hear him skirmish about several time .
When we waken in the morning the storm be over and a young morning be look through rosy eyelid across a white world .
The little clearing around Peg 's cabin be heap with dazzling drift , and we boys fell to and shovel out a road to her well .
She give u breakfast -- stiff oatmeal porridge without milk , and a boiled egg apiece .
Cecily could NOT eat her porridge ; she declare she have such a bad cold that she have no appetite ; a cold she certainly have ; the rest of u choke our mess down and after we have do so Peg ask u if we have notice a soapy taste .
`` The soap fell into the porridge while I be make it , '' she say .
`` But , '' -- smack her lip , -- `` I 'm go to make yez an Irish stew for dinner .
It 'll be fine . ''
An Irish stew concoct by Peg !
No wonder Dan say hastily , `` You be very kind but we 'll have to go right home . ''
`` Yez ca n't walk , '' say Peg .
`` Oh , yes , we can .
The drift be so hard they 'll carry , and the snow will be pretty well blow off the middle of the field .
It 's only three-quarters of a mile .
We boys will go home and get a pung and come back for you girls . ''
But the girl would n't listen to this .
They must go with u , even Cecily .
`` Seems to me yez be n't in such a hurry to leave last night , '' observe Peg sarcastically .
`` Oh , it 's only because they 'll be so anxious about u at home , and it 's Sunday and we do n't want to miss Sunday School , '' explain Felicity .
`` Well , I hope your Sunday School will do yez good , '' say Peg , rather grumpily .
But she relent again at the last and give Cecily a wishbone .
`` Whatever you wish on that will come true , '' she say .
`` But you only have the one wish , so do n't waste it . ''
`` We 're so much oblige to you for all your trouble , '' say the Story Girl politely .
`` Never mind the trouble .
The expense be the thing , '' retort Peg grimly .
`` Oh ! ''
Felicity hesitate .
`` If you would let u pay you -- give you something -- '' `` No , thank yez , '' respond Peg loftily .
`` There be people who take money for their hospitality , I 've heerd , but I 'm thankful to say I do n't associate with that class .
Yez be welcome to all yez have have here , if yez ARE in a big hurry to get away . ''
She shut the door behind u with something of a slam , and her black cat follow u so far , with stealthy , furtive footstep , that we be frighten of it .
Eventually it turn back ; then , and not till then , do we feel free to discuss our adventure .
`` Well , I 'm thankful we 're out of THAT , '' say Felicity , draw a long breath .
`` Has n't it just be an awful experience ? ''
`` We might all have be find frozen stark and stiff this morning , '' remark the Story Girl with apparent relish .
`` I tell you , it be a lucky thing we get to Peg Bowen 's , '' say Dan .
`` Miss Marwood say there be no such thing a luck , '' protest Cecily .
`` We ought to say it be Providence instead . ''
`` Well , Peg and Providence do n't seem to go together very well , somehow , '' retort Dan .
`` If Peg be a witch it must be the Other One she 's in co. .
with . ''
`` Dan , it 's get to be simply scandalous the way you talk , '' say Felicity .
`` I just wish ma could hear you . ''
`` Is soap in porridge any bad than tooth-powder in rusk , lovely creature ? ''
ask Dan .
`` Dan , Dan , '' admonish Cecily , between her cough , `` remember it 's Sunday . ''
`` It seem hard to remember that , '' say Peter .
`` It do n't seem a mite like Sunday and it seem awful long since yesterday . ''
`` Cecily , you 've get a dreadful cold , '' say the Story Girl anxiously .
`` In spite of Peg 's ginger tea , '' add Felix .
`` Oh , that ginger tea be AWFUL , '' exclaim poor Cecily .
`` I think I 'd never get it down -- it be so hot with ginger -- and there be so much of it !
But I be so frightened of offend Peg I 'd have try to drink it all if there have be a bucketful .
Oh , yes , it 's very easy for you all to laugh !
You do n't have to drink it . ''
`` We have to eat two meal , though , '' say Felicity with a shiver .
`` And I do n't know when those dish of hers be wash .
I just shut my eye and take gulp . ''
`` Did you notice the soapy taste in the porridge ? ''
ask the Story Girl .
`` Oh , there be so many queer taste about it I do n't notice one more than another , '' answer Felicity wearily .
`` What bother me , '' remark Peter absently , `` be that skull .
Do you suppose Peg really find thing out by it ? ''
`` Nonsense !
How could she ? ''
scoffed Felix , bold a a lion in daylight .
`` She do n't SAY she do , you know , '' I say cautiously .
`` Well , we 'll know in time if the thing she say be go to happen do , '' muse Peter .
`` Do you suppose your father be really come home ? ''
queried Felicity .
`` I hope not , '' answer Peter decidedly .
`` You ought to be ashamed of yourself , '' say Felicity severely .
`` No , I ought n't .
Father get drunk all the time he be home , and would n't work and be bad to mother , '' say Peter defiantly .
`` She have to support him as well a herself and me .
I do n't want to see any father come home , and you 'd better believe it .
Of course , if he be the right sort of a father it 'd be different . ''
`` What I would like to know be if Aunt Olivia be go to be marry , '' say the Story Girl absently .
`` I can hardly believe it .
But now that I think of it -- Uncle Roger have be tease her ever since she be in Halifax last summer . ''
`` If she do get marry you 'll have to come and live with u , '' say Cecily delightedly .
Felicity do not betray so much delight and the Story Girl remark with a weary little sigh that she hop Aunt Olivia would n't .
We all felt rather weary , somehow .
Peg 's prediction have be unsettling , and our nerve have all be more or less strain during our sojourn under her roof .
We be glad when we find ourselves at home .
The folk have not be at all troubled about u , but it be because they be sure the storm have come up before we would think of leave Cousin Mattie 's and not because they have receive any mysterious message from Peg 's skull .
We be relieve at this , but on the whole , our adventure have not do much towards clear up the vexed question of Peg 's witchcraft .
CHAPTER IX .
EXTRACTS FROM THE FEBRUARY AND MARCH NUMBERS OF `` OUR MAGAZINE '' RESOLUTION HONOUR ROLL Miss Felicity King .
HONOURABLE MENTION Mr. Felix King .
Mr. Peter Craig .
Miss Sara Ray .
EDITORIAL The editor wish to make a few remark about the Resolution Honour Roll .
As will be see , only one name figure on it .
Felicity say she have think a beautiful thought every morning before breakfast without miss one morning , not even the one we be at Peg Bowen 's .
Some of our number think it not fair that Felicity should be on the honour roll -LRB- FELICITY , ASIDE : `` That 's Dan , of course . '' -RRB-
when she only make one resolution and wo n't tell u what any of the thought be .
So we have decide to give honourable mention to everybody who have keep one resolution perfect .
Felix have work all his arithmetic problem by himself .
He complain that he never get more than a third of them right and the teacher have mark him away down ; but one can not keep resolution without some inconvenience .
Peter have never play tit-tat-x in church or get drunk and say it be n't as bad a he expect .
-LRB- PETER , INDIGNANTLY : `` I never say it . ''
CECILY , SOOTHINGLY : `` Now , Peter , Bev only mean that a a joke . '' -RRB-
Sara Ray have never talk any mean gossip , but do not find conversation as interesting a it use to be .
-LRB- SARA RAY , WONDERINGLY : `` I do n't remember of say that . '' -RRB-
Felix do not eat any apple until March , but forget and eat seven the day we be at Cousin Mattie 's .
-LRB- FELIX : `` I only eat five ! '' -RRB-
He soon give up try to say what he think always .
He get into too much trouble .
We think Felix ought to change to old Grandfather King 's rule .
It be , `` Hold your tongue when you can , and when you ca n't tell the truth . ''
Cecily feel she have not read all the good book she might , because some she try to read be very dull and the Pansy book be so much more interesting .
And it be no use try not to feel bad because her hair be n't curly and she have mark that resolution out .
The Story Girl come very near to keep her resolution to have all the good time possible , but she say she miss two , if not three , she might have have .
Dan refuse to say anything about his resolution and so do the editor .
PERSONALS We regret that Miss Cecily King be suffer from a severe cold .
Mr. Alexander Marr of Markdale die very suddenly last week .
We never hear of his death till he be dead .
Miss Cecily King wish to state that she do not ask the question about `` Holy Moses '' and the other word in the January number .
Dan put it in for a mean joke .
The weather have be cold and fine .
We have only have one bad storm .
The coasting on Uncle Roger 's hill continue good .
Aunt Eliza do not favour u with a visit after all .
She take cold and have to go home .
We be sorry that she have a cold but glad that she have to go home .
Cecily say she think it wicked of u to be glad .
But when we ask her `` cross her heart '' if she be n't glad herself she have to say she be .
Miss Cecily King have get three very distinguished name on her quilt square .
They be the Governor and his wife and a witch 's .
The King family have the honour of entertain the Governor 's wife to tea on February the seventeenth .
We be all invite to visit Government House but some of u think we wo n't go .
A tragic event occur last Tuesday .
Mrs. James Frewen come to tea and there be no pie in the house .
Felicity have not yet fully recover .
A new boy be come to school .
His name be Cyrus Brisk and his folk move up from Markdale .
He say he be go to punch Willy Fraser 's head if Willy keep on think he be Miss Cecily King 's beau .
-LRB- CECILY : `` I have n't ANY beau !
I do n't mean to think of such a thing for at least eight year yet ! '' -RRB-
Miss Alice Reade of Charlottetown Royalty have come to Carlisle to teach music .
She board at Mr. Peter Armstrong 's .
The girl be all go to take music lesson from her .
Two description of her will be find in another column .
Felix write one , but the girl think he do not do her justice , so Cecily write another one .
She admit she copy most of the description out of Valeria H. Montague 's story Lord Marmaduke 's First , Last , and Only Love ; or the Bride of the Castle by the Sea , but say they fit Miss Reade good than anything she could make up .
HOUSEHOLD DEPARTMENT Always keep the kitchen tidy and then you need n't mind if company come unexpectedly .
ANXIOUS INQUIRER : We do n't know anything that will take the stain out of a silk dress when a soft-boiled egg be drop on it .
Better not wear your silk dress so often , especially when boil egg .
Ginger tea be good for cold .
OLD HOUSEKEEPER : Yes , when the baking-powder give out you can use tooth-powder instead .
-LRB- FELICITY : `` I never write that !
I do n't care , I do n't think it 's fair for other people to be put thing in my department ! '' -RRB-
Our apple be not keep well this year .
They be rot ; and besides father say we eat an awful lot of them .
PERSEVERANCE : I will give you the recipe for dumpling you ask for .
But remember it be not everyone who can make dumpling , even from the recipe .
There 's a knack in it .
If the soap fall into the porridge do not tell your guest about it until they have finish eat it because it might take away their appetite .
FELICITY KING .
ETIQUETTE DEPARTMENT P-r C-g : -- Do not criticize people 's nose unless you be sure they ca n't hear you , and do n't criticize your best girl 's great-aunt 's nose in any case .

Ans .

F-x K-g : -- No , it be not polite to sleep with your mouth open .

DAN KING .
FASHION NOTES Crocheted watch pocket be all the rage now .
If you have n't a watch they do to carry your pencil in or a piece of gum .
It be stylish to have hair ribbon to match your dress .
But it be hard to match gray drugget .
I like scarlet for that .
It be stylish to pin a piece of ribbon on your coat the same colour a your chum wear in her hair .
Mary Martha Cowan saw them do it in town and start u do it here .
I always wear Kitty 's ribbon and Kitty wear mine , but the Story Girl think it be silly .
CECILY KING .
AN ACCOUNT OF OUR VISIT TO COUSIN MATTIE 'S We all walk over to Cousin Mattie 's last week .
They be all well there and we have a fine dinner .
On our way back a snow-storm come up and we get lose in the wood .
We do n't know where we be or nothing .
If we have n't see a light I guess we 'd all have be frozen and snow over , and they would never have find u till spring and that would be very sad .
But we saw a light and make for it and it be Peg Bowen 's .
Some people think she be a witch and it 's hard to tell , but she be real hospitable and take u all in .
Her house be very untidy but it be warm .
She have a skull .
I mean a loose skull , not her own .
She let on it tell her thing , but Uncle Alec say it could n't because it be only an Indian skull that old Dr. Beecham have and Peg steal it when he die , but Uncle Roger say he would n't trust himself with Peg 's skull for anything .
She give u supper .
It be a horrid meal .
The Story Girl say I must not tell what I find in the bread and butter because it would be too disgust to read in Our Magazine but it do n't matter because we be all there , except Sara Ray , and know what it be .
We stay all night and u boys slept in straw .
None of u have ever sleep on straw before .
We get home in the morning .
That be all I can write about our visit to Cousin Mattie 's .
FELIX KING .
MY WORST ADVENTURE It 's my turn to write it so I suppose I must .
I guess my bad adventure be two year ago when a whole lot of u be coast on Uncle Rogers hill .
Charlie Cowan and Fred Marr have start , but half-way down their sled get stuck and I run down to shove them off again .
Then I stand there just a moment to watch them with my back to the top of the hill .
While I be stand there Rob Marr start Kitty and Em Frewen off on his sled .
His sled have a wooden tongue in it and it slant back over the girl ' head .
I be right in the way and they yell to me to get out , but just a I hear them it strike me .
The sled take me between the leg and I be histed back over the tongue and drop in a heap behind before I know what have happen to me .
I think a tornado have strike me .
The girl could n't stop though they think I be kill , but Rob come tear down and help me up .
He be awful scared but I be n't kill nor my back be n't break but my nose bleed something awful and keep on bleeding for three day .
Not all the time but by spell .
DAN KING .
THE STORY OF HOW CARLISLE GOT ITS NAME This be a true story to .
Long ago there be a girl live in charlotte town .
I dont know her name so I cant right it and maybe it be just as well for Felicity might think it wasnt romantik like Miss Jemima Parrs .
She be awful pretty and a young englishman who have come out to make his fortune fell in love with her and they be engage to be marry the next spring .
His name be Mr. Carlisle .
In the winter he start off to hunt cariboo for a spell .
Cariboos live on the island then .
There aint any here now .
He get to where it be Carlisle now .
It be n't anything then only wood and a few indian .
He get awful sick and be sick for ever so long in a indian camp and only an old micmac squaw to wait on him .
Back in town they all think he be dead and his girl felt bad for a little while and then get over it and take up with another beau .
The girl say that wasnt romantik but I think it be sensible but if it have be me that die I 'd have felt bad if she forget me so soon .
But he hadnt die and when he get back to town he go right to her house and walk in and there she be stand up to be marry to the other fellow .
Poor Mr. Carlisle felt awful .
He be sick and week and it go to his head .
He just turn and run and run till he get back to the old micmac 's camp and fell in front of it .
But the indian have go because it be spring and it didnt matter because he really be dead this time and people come look for him from town and find him and bury him there and call the place after him .
They say the girl be never happy again and that be hard line on her but maybe she deserve it .
PETER CRAIG .
MISS ALICE READE Miss Alice Reade be a very pretty girl .
She have kind of curly blackish hair and big gray eye and a pale face .
She be tall and thin but her figure be pretty fair and she have a nice mouth and a sweet way of speaking .
The girl be crazy about her and talk about her all the time .
FELIX KING .
BEAUTIFUL ALICE That be what we girls call Miss Reade among ourselves .
She be divinely beautiful .
Her magnificent wealth of raven hair flow back in glisten wave from her sun-kissed brow .

Her hand be like a poet 's dream .

Her favourite colour be blue .
Some people think she be stiff and some say she be stuck-up , but she be n't a bit .
It 's just that she be different from them and they do n't like it .
She be just lovely and we adore her . -RRB-
CECILY KING .
CHAPTER X . DISAPPEARANCE OF PADDY As I remember , the spring come late that year in Carlisle .

CHAPTER XII .
FLOWERS O ' MAY Accordingly we go a-maying , follow the lure of dance wind to a certain westward slop hill lie under the spirit-like blue of spring sky , feather over with lisp young pine and fir , which cup little hollow and corner where the sunshine get in and never get out again , but stay there and grow mellow , coax dear thing to bloom long before they would dream of wake up elsewhere .

He be walk in his garden a we go by , look at his tulip bed .

And he say HE do n't do it -- it be all the work of the pixy who live in the wood across the brook .
There be more pixy baby than usual this spring , and the mother be in a hurry for the cradle .
The tulip be the pixy baby ' cradle , it seem .
The mother pixies come out of the wood at twilight and rock their tiny little brown baby to sleep in the tulip cup .
That be the reason why tulip bloom last so much long than other blossom .
The pixy baby must have a cradle until they be grow up .
They grow very fast , you see , and the Awkward Man say on a spring evening , when the tulip be out , you can hear the sweet , soft , clear , fairy music in his garden , and it be the pixy folk sing a they rock the pixy baby to sleep . ''
`` Then the Awkward Man say what be n't true , '' say Felicity severely .
CHAPTER XIII .
A SURPRISING ANNOUNCEMENT `` Nothing exciting have happen for ever so long , '' say the Story Girl discontentedly , one late May evening , a we linger under the wonderful white bloom of the cherry tree .
There be a long row of them in the orchard , with a Lombardy poplar at either end , and a hedge of lilac behind .
When the wind blew over them all the spicy breeze of Ceylon 's isle be never sweet .
It be a time of wonder and marvel , of the soft touch of silver rain on green field , of the incredible delicacy of young leaf , of blossom in field and garden and wood .
The whole world bloom in a flush and tremor of maiden loveliness , instinct with all the evasive , fleeting charm of spring and girlhood and young morning .
We felt and enjoy it all without understand or analyze it .
It be enough to be glad and young with spring on the golden road .
`` I do n't like excitement very much , '' say Cecily .
`` It make one so tired .
I 'm sure it be excite enough when Paddy be miss , but we do n't find that very pleasant . ''
`` No , but it be interest , '' return the Story Girl thoughtfully .
`` After all , I believe I 'd rather be miserable than dull . ''
`` I would n't then , '' say Felicity decidedly .
`` And you need never be dull when you have work to do .
` Satan find some mischief still for idle hand to do ! ' ''
`` Well , mischief be interesting , '' laugh the Story Girl .
`` And I think you do n't think it lady-like to speak of that person , Felicity ? ''
`` It 's all right if you call him by his polite name , '' say Felicity stiffly .
`` Why do the Lombardy poplar hold it branch straight up in the air like that , when all the other poplar hold theirs out or hang them down ? ''
interject Peter , who have be gaze intently at the slender spire show darkly against the fine blue eastern sky .
`` Because it grow that way , '' say Felicity .
`` Oh I know a story about that , '' cry the Story Girl .
`` Once upon a time an old man find the pot of gold at the rainbow 's end .
There IS a pot there , it be say , but it be very hard to find because you can never get to the rainbow 's end before it vanish from your sight .
But this old man find it , just at sunset , when Iris , the guardian of the rainbow gold , happen to be absent .
As he be a long way from home , and the pot be very big and heavy , he decide to hide it until morning and then get one of his son to go with him and help him carry it .
So he hide it under the bough of the sleep poplar tree .
`` When Iris come back she miss the pot of gold and of course she be in a sad way about it .
She send Mercury , the messenger of the god , to look for it , for she do n't dare leave the rainbow again , l somebody should run off with that too .
Mercury ask all the tree if they have see the pot of gold , and the elm , oak and pine point to the poplar and say , '' ` The poplar can tell you where it be . ' ''
` How can I tell you where it be ? '
cry the poplar , and she hold up all her branch in surprise , just a we hold up our hand -- and down tumble the pot of gold .
The poplar be amaze and indignant , for she be a very honest tree .
She stretch her boughs high above her head and declare that she would always hold them like that , so that nobody could hide steal gold under them again .
And she teach all the little poplar she know to stand the same way , and that be why Lombardy poplar always do .
But the aspen poplar leaf be always shake , even on the very calm day .
And do you know why ? ''
And then she tell u the old legend that the cross on which the Saviour of the world suffer be make of aspen poplar wood and so never again could it poor , shake , shiver leaf know rest or peace .
There be an aspen in the orchard , the very embodiment of youth and spring in it litheness and symmetry .
Its little leaf be hang tremulously , not yet so fully blow a to hide it development of bough and twig , make poetry against the spiritual tint of a spring sunset .
`` It do look sad , '' say Peter , `` but it be a pretty tree , and it be n't it fault . ''
`` There 's a heavy dew and it 's time we stop talk nonsense and go in , '' decreed Felicity .
`` If we do n't we 'll all have a cold , and then we 'll be miserable enough , but it wo n't be very exciting . ''
`` All the same , I wish something excite would happen , '' finish the Story Girl , a we walk up through the orchard , people with it nun-like shadow .
`` There 's a new moon tonight , so may be you 'll get your wish , '' say Peter .
`` My Aunt Jane do n't believe there be anything in the moon business , but you never can tell . ''
The Story Girl do get her wish .
Something happen the very next day .
She join u in the afternoon with a quite indescribable expression on her face , compound of triumph , anticipation , and regret .
Her eye betray that she have be cry , but in them shine a chastened exultation .
Whatever the Story Girl mourn over it be evident she be not without hope .
`` I have some news to tell you , '' she say importantly .
`` Can you guess what it be ? ''
We could n't and would n't try .
`` Tell u right off , '' implore Felix .
`` You look a if it be something tremendous . ''
`` So it be .
Listen -- Aunt Olivia be go to be marry . ''
We star in blank amazement .
Peg Bowen 's hint have fade from our mind and we have never put much faith in it .
`` Aunt Olivia !
I do n't believe it , '' cry Felicity flatly .
`` Who tell you ? ''
`` Aunt Olivia herself .
So it be perfectly true .
I 'm awfully sorry in one way -- but oh , wo n't it be splendid to have a real wedding in the family ?
She 's go to have a big wedding -- and I be to be bridesmaid . ''
`` I should n't think you be old enough to be a bridesmaid , '' say Felicity sharply .
`` I 'm nearly fifteen .
Anyway , Aunt Olivia say I have to be . ''
`` Who 's she go to marry ? ''
ask Cecily , gather herself together after the shock , and find that the world be go on just the same .
`` His name be Dr. Seton and he be a Halifax man .
She meet him when she be at Uncle Edward 's last summer .
They 've be engage ever since .

`` Why do thing always come together like that ?

`` I 'm come to live at your house , '' answer the Story Girl rather timidly .
She do not know how Felicity might like that .
But Felicity take it rather well .
`` You 've be here most of the time anyhow , so it 'll just be that you 'll sleep and eat here , too .

`` Aunt Olivia say he 'll have to get married , too .
But Uncle Roger say he 'd rather hire a housekeeper than marry one , because in the first case he could turn her off if he do n't like her , but in the second case he could n't . ''
`` There 'll be a lot of cook to do for the wedding , '' reflect Felicity in a tone of satisfaction .
`` I s ` pose Aunt Olivia will want some rusk make .
I hope she have plenty of tooth-powder laid in , '' say Dan .
`` It 's a pity you do n't use some of that tooth-powder you 're so fond of talk about yourself , '' retort Felicity .
`` When anyone have a mouth the size of yours the teeth show so plain . ''
`` I brush my teeth every Sunday , '' asseverate Dan .
`` Every Sunday !
You ought to brush them every DAY . ''

demand Dan sincerely .
`` Well , you know , it really do say so in the Family Guide , '' say Cecily quietly .
`` Then the Family Guide people must have lot more spare time than I have , '' retort Dan contemptuously .

What be his first name ? ''
`` Robert . ''

`` Not until he 's married to her .
Then we will , of course . ''

`` I hope Dr. Seton wo n't fail to show up , like your cousin Rachel Ward 's beau , '' say Peter .
`` That make me think of another story I read the other day about Great-uncle Andrew King and Aunt Georgina , '' laugh the Story Girl .
`` It happen eighty year ago .
It be a very stormy winter and the road be bad .
Uncle Andrew live in Carlisle , and Aunt Georgina -- she be Miss Georgina Matheson then -- live away up west , so he could n't get to see her very often .
They agree to be marry that winter , but Georgina could n't set the day exactly because her brother , who live in Ontario , be come home for a visit , and she want to be marry while he be home .
So it be arrange that she be to write Uncle Andrew and tell him what day to come .
She do , and she tell him to come on a Tuesday .
But her writing be n't very good and poor Uncle Andrew think she write Thursday .
So on Thursday he drive all the way to Georgina 's home to be marry .
It be forty mile and a bitter cold day .
But it be n't any cold than the reception he get from Georgina .
She be out in the porch , with her head tie up in a towel , pick goose .
She have be all ready Tuesday , and her friend and the minister be there , and the wedding supper prepare .
But there be no bridegroom and Georgina be furious .
Nothing Uncle Andrew could say would appease her .
She would n't listen to a word of explanation , but tell him to go , and never show his nose there again .
So poor Uncle Andrew have to go ruefully home , hop that she would relent later on , because he be really very much in love with her . ''
`` And do she ? ''
queried Felicity .
`` She do .
Thirteen year exactly from that day they be marry .
It take her just that long to forgive him . ''
`` It take her just that long to find out she could n't get anybody else , '' say Dan , cynically .
CHAPTER XIV .
A PRODIGAL RETURNS Aunt Olivia and the Story Girl live in a whirlwind of dressmaking after that , and enjoy it hugely .

It 's too short , but ma say it 's plenty good for this summer .
I 'll be so mortified if I have to wear it . ''

`` I 've never be to anything .
I would n't miss it for the world . ''

Felicity be very hard on him that spring , but his loyalty never waver .
Everything she say or do be right in Peter 's eye .

The wedding be a perennial source of conversation among u in those day ; but presently it interest pal for a time in the light of another quite tremendous happen .
One Saturday night Peter 's mother call to take him home with her for Sunday .
She have be work at Mr. James Frewen 's , and Mr. Frewen be drive her home .
We have never see Peter 's mother before , and we look at her with discreet curiosity .
She be a plump , black-eyed little woman , neat a a pin , but with a rather tired and care-worn face that look a if it should have be rosy and jolly .

Peter go home with her and return Sunday evening .

Paddy , grown sleek and handsome again , be sit on the stone itself , wash his jowl .

demand the Story Girl .

The announcement produce all the sensation he could have wish .

`` Peter !
When do he come back ? ''
`` Saturday night .
He be there when ma and I get home .
It give her an awful turn .
I do n't know him at first , of course . ''
`` Peter Craig , I believe you be glad your father have come back , '' cry the Story Girl . ''
` Course I 'm glad , '' retort Peter .

You have n't hear my story yet .
I would n't have be glad to see father if he 'd come back the same a he go away .
But he be a changed man .
He happen to go into a revival meeting one night this spring and he get convert .
And he 's come home to stay , and he say he 's never go to drink another drop , but he 's go to look after his family .
Ma be n't to do any more washing for nobody but him and me , and I 'm not to be a hired boy any long .
He say I can stay with your Uncle Roger till the fall 'cause I promise I would , but after that I 'm to stay home and go to school right along and learn to be whatever I 'd like to be .
I tell you it make me feel queer .
Everything seem to be upset .
But he give ma forty dollar -- every cent he have -- so I guess he really be convert . ''

She do not say it nastily , however .

Do n't you tell me she be n't a witch after that . ''

Grown up folk talk thing over long before they tell them to child , '' say Cecily .

She tell me father be come home and he come ! ''

Felicity sniffed .

Perhaps Peter 's father have too , if we but realize it -- imprison in the dungeon of his own evil appetite and habit , than which none could be more loathsome .
But a Power , mighty than the force of evil , have strike off his fetter and lead him back to his long-forfeited liberty and light .
And no countess or lady of high degree could have welcome a long-lost earl home more joyfully than the tired little washerwoman have welcome the err husband of her youth .
But in Peter 's ointment of joy there be a fly or two .
So very , very few thing be flawless in this world , even on the golden road .
`` Of course I 'm awful glad that father have come back and that ma wo n't have to wash any more , '' he say with a sigh , `` but there be two thing that kind of worry me .
My Aunt Jane always say that it do n't do any good to worry , and I s ` pose it do n't , but it 's kind of a relief . ''

I 'll miss you just dreadful , and I wo n't even be able to go to the same school .
I 'll have to go to Markdale school . ''
`` But you must come and see u often , '' say Felicity graciously .
`` Markdale be n't so far away , and you could spend every other Saturday afternoon with u anyway . ''
Peter 's black eye fill with adore gratitude .

He be n't anything before .
He use to say he be a Nothingarian and live up to it -- kind of brag like .
But he 's a strong Methodist now , and be go to go to Markdale Methodist church and pay to the salary .
Now what 'll he say when I tell him I 'm a Presbyterian ? ''

I be scar he 'd say I 'd have to be a Methodist . ''

I 've get to be a Presbyterian , 'cause I stick to a thing when I once decide it .

`` Well , lot o ' people do .

But I expect it will make thing unpleasant . ''

`` Just keep quiet and go to the Methodist church until you get big , and then you can go where you please . ''

So I 'll tell father right out , but I 'll wait a few week so a not to spoil thing for ma too soon if he act up . ''
Peter be not the only one who have secret care .
Sara Ray be begin to feel worried over her look .

`` I 'm so afraid , Cecily , that I 'm go to be homely all my life , '' say poor Sara with a tremble in her voice .
`` You can stand be ugly when you be young if you have any hope of be well look when you grow up .
But I 'm get bad .
Aunt Mary say I 'm go to be the very image of Aunt Matilda .
And Aunt Matilda be as homely a she can be .
It be n't '' -- and poor Sara sigh -- `` a very cheerful prospect .

`` Besides , you be real nice look at time , Sara .

Crying spoil your eye and make the end of your nose red . ''

`` Goodness ! ''

`` Just think , Cecily , you 've have a proposal already , '' say Sara Ray in an awe-struck tone .

`` No , indeed !
I guess not ! ''

`` I could n't do that .
I have n't enough spunk , '' confess Cecily with a blush .
`` But I 'll tell you what I do do once .
He write me a long letter last week .
It be just awfully SOFT , and every other word be spell wrong .
He even spell bake soda , ` bacon soda ! ' ''
`` What on earth have he to say about bake soda in a love-letter ? ''
ask Felicity .
`` Oh , he say his mother send him to the store for some and he forget it because he be think about me .

I think maybe he 'd feel insulted and stop writing to me . ''
`` And do he ? ''
`` No , he do n't .
It be my opinion you ca n't insult Cyrus Brisk .
He be too thick-skinned .
He write another letter , and thank me for correct his mistake , and say it make him feel glad because it show I be begin to take an interest in him when I want him to spell good .
Did you ever ?
