`` Mrs. Cyrus Brisk WOULD be an awful name , '' giggle Felicity .
`` Flossie Brisk say Cyrus be ruin all the tree on his father 's place cut your name on them , '' say Sara Ray .
`` His father tell him he would whip him if he do n't stop , but Cyrus keep right on .
He tell Flossie it relieve his feeling .
Flossie say he cut yours and his together on the birch tree in front of the parlour window , and a row of heart around them . ''
`` Just where every visitor can see them , I suppose , '' lament Cecily .
`` He just worry my life out .
And what I mind most of all be , he sit and look at me in school with such melancholy , reproachful eye when he ought to be work sum .
I wo n't look at him , but I FEEL him star at me , and it make me so nervous . ''
`` They say his mother be out of her mind at one time , '' say Felicity .
I do not think Felicity be quite well pleased that Cyrus should have pass over her rose-red prettiness to set his affection on that demure elf of a Cecily .
She do not want the allegiance of Cyrus in the least , but it be something of a slight that he have not want her to want it .
`` And he send me piece of poetry he cut out of the paper , '' Cecily go on , `` with lot of the line mark with a lead pencil .
Yesterday he put one in his letter , and this be what he mark : '' ` If you will not relent to me Then must I learn to know Darkness alone till life be fly .
Here -- I have the piece in my sewing-bag -- I 'll read it all to you . ''
Those three graceless girl read the sentimental rhyme and giggle over it .
Poor Cyrus !
His young affection be sadly misplace .
But after all , though Cecily never relent towards him , he do not condemn himself to darkness alone till life be fly .
Quite early in life he wed a stout , rosy , buxom lass , the very antithesis of his first love ; he prosper in his undertaking , raise a large and respectable family , and be eventually appoint a Justice of the Peace .
Which be all very sensible of Cyrus .
CHAPTER XV .
THE RAPE OF THE LOCK June be crowd full of interest that year .
We gather in with it sheaf of fragrant day the choice harvest of childhood .
Things happen right along .
Cecily declare she hat to go to sleep for fear she might miss something .
There be so many dear delight along the golden road to give u pleasure -- the earth dapple with new blossom , the dance of shadow in the field , the rustling , rain-wet way of the wood , the faint fragrance in meadow lane , liltings of bird and croon of bee in the old orchard , windy piping on the hill , sunset behind the pine , limpid dew fill primrose cup , crescent moon through darklings bough , soft night alight with blink star .
We enjoy all these boon , unthinkingly and light-heartedly , a child do .
And besides these , there be the absorb little drama of human life which be be enact all around u , and in which each of u play a satisfying part -- the gay preparation for Aunt Olivia 's mid-June wedding , the excitement of practise for the concert with which our school-teacher , Mr. Perkins , have elect to close the school year , and Cecily 's trouble with Cyrus Brisk , which furnish unholy mirth for the rest of u , though Cecily could not see the funny side of it at all .
Matters go from bad to worse in the case of the irrepressible Cyrus .
He continue to shower Cecily with note , the spelling of which show no improvement ; he worry the life out of her by constantly threaten to fight Willy Fraser -- although , a Felicity sarcastically point out , he never do it .
`` But I 'm always afraid he will , '' say Cecily , `` and it would be such a DISGRACE to have two boy fight over me in school . ''
`` You must have encourage Cyrus a little in the beginning or he 'd never have be so persevering , '' say Felicity unjustly .
`` I never do ! ''
cry outrage Cecily .
`` You know very well , Felicity King , that I hat Cyrus Brisk ever since the very first time I saw his big , fat , red face .
So there ! ''
`` Felicity be just jealous because Cyrus do n't take a notion to her instead of you , Sis , '' say Dan .
`` Talk sense ! ''
snap Felicity .
`` If I do you would n't understand me , sweet little sister , '' rejoin aggravate Dan .
Finally Cyrus crown his iniquity by steal the denied lock of Cecily 's hair .
One sunny afternoon in school , Cecily and Kitty Marr ask and receive permission to sit out on the side bench before the open window , where the cool breeze sweep in from the green field beyond .
To sit on this bench be always consider a treat , and be only allow a a reward of merit ; but Cecily and Kitty have another reason for wish to sit there .
Kitty have read in a magazine that sun-baths be good for the hair ; so both she and Cecily toss their long braid over the window-sill and let them hang there in the broiling sun-shine .
And while Cecily sit thus , diligently work a fraction sum on her slate , that base Cyrus ask permission to go out , have previously borrow a pair of scissors from one of the big girl who do fancy work at the noon recess .
Outside , Cyrus sneak up close to the window and cut off a piece of Cecily 's hair .
This rape of the lock do not produce quite such terrible consequence a the more famous one in Pope 's poem , but Cecily 's soul be no less agitate than Belinda 's .
She cry all the way home from school about it , and only check her tear when Dan declare he 'd fight Cyrus and make him give it up .
`` Oh , no , You must n't . ''
say Cecily , struggle with her sob .
`` I wo n't have you fight on my account for anything .
And besides , he 'd likely lick you -- he 's so big and rough .
And the folk at home might find out all about it , and Uncle Roger would never give me any peace , and mother would be cross , for she 'd never believe it be n't my fault .
It would n't be so bad if he 'd only take a little , but he cut a great big chunk right off the end of one of the braid .
Just look at it .
I 'll have to cut the other to make them fair -- and they 'll look so awful stubby . ''
But Cyrus ' acquirement of the chunk of hair be his last triumph .
His downfall be near ; and , although it involve Cecily in a most humiliating experience , over which she cry half the following night , in the end she confess it be worth undergoing just to get rid of Cyrus .
Mr. Perkins be an exceedingly strict disciplinarian .
No communication of any sort be permit between his pupil during school hour .
Anyone catch violate this rule be promptly punish by the infliction of one of the weird penance for which Mr. Perkins be famous , and which be generally far bad than ordinary whipping .
One day in school Cyrus send a letter across to Cecily .
Usually he leave his effusion in her desk , or between the leaf of her book ; but this time it be pass over to her under cover of the desk through the hand of two or three scholar .
Just a Em Frewen hold it over the aisle Mr. Perkins wheel around from his station before the blackboard and catch her in the act .
`` Bring that here , Emmeline , '' he command .
Cyrus turn quite pale .
Em carry the note to Mr. Perkins .
He take it , hold it up , and scrutinize the address .
`` Did you write this to Cecily , Emmeline ? ''
he ask .
`` No , sir . ''
`` Who write it then ? ''
Em say quite shamelessly that she do n't know -- it have just be pass over from the next row .
`` And I suppose you have no idea where it come from ? ''
say Mr. Perkins , with his frightful , sardonic grin .
`` Well , perhaps Cecily can tell u .
You may take your seat , Emmeline , and you will remain at the foot of your spell class for a week a punishment for pass the note .
Cecily , come here . ''
Indignant Em sit down and poor , innocent Cecily be hale forth to public ignominy .
She go with a crimson face .
`` Cecily , '' say her tormentor , `` do you know who write this letter to you ? ''
Cecily , like a certain renowned personage , could not tell a lie .
`` I -- I think so , sir , '' she murmur faintly .
`` Who be it ? ''
`` I ca n't tell you that , '' stammer Cecily , on the verge of tear .
`` Ah ! ''
say Mr. Perkins politely .
`` Well , I suppose I could easily find out by open it .
But it be very impolite to open other people 's letter .
I think I have a good plan .
Since you refuse to tell me who write it , open it yourself , take this chalk , and copy the content on the blackboard that we may all enjoy them .
And sign the writer 's name at the bottom . ''
`` Oh , '' gasp Cecily , choose the less of two evil , `` I 'll tell you who write it -- it be -- `` Hush ! ''
Mr. Perkins check her with a gentle motion of his hand .
He be always most gentle when most inexorable .
`` You do not obey me when I first order you to tell me the writer .
You can not have the privilege of do so now .
Open the note , take the chalk , and do a I command you . ''
Worms will turn , and even meek , mild , obedient little soul like Cecily may be goad to the point of wild , sheer rebellion .
`` I -- I wo n't ! ''
she cry passionately .
Mr. Perkins , martinet though he be , would hardly , I think , have inflict such a punishment on Cecily , who be a favourite of his , have he know the real nature of that luckless missive .
But , a he afterwards admit , he think it be merely a note from some other girl , of such trifle sort a school-girls be wont to write ; and moreover , he have already commit himself to the decree , which , like those of Mede and Persian , must not alter .
To let Cecily off , after her mad defiance , would be to establish a revolutionary precedent .
`` So you really think you wo n't ? ''
he query smilingly .
`` Well , on second thought , you may take your choice .
Either you will do a I have bid you , or you will sit for three day with '' -- Mr. Perkins ' eye skim over the school-room to find a boy who be sit alone -- `` with Cyrus Brisk . ''
This choice of Mr. Perkins , who know nothing of the little drama of emotion that go on under the routine of lesson and exercise in his domain , be purely accidental , but we take it at the time a a stroke of diabolical genius .
It leave Cecily no choice .
She would have do almost anything before she would have sit with Cyrus Brisk .
With flashing eye she tear open the letter , snatch up the chalk , and dash at the blackboard .
In a few minute the content of that letter grace the expanse usually sacred to more prosaic composition .
I can not reproduce it verbatim , for I have no after opportunity of refresh my memory .
But I remember that it be exceedingly sentimental and exceedingly ill-spelled -- for Cecily mercilessly copy down poor Cyrus ' mistake .
He write her that he wear her hare over his hart -- `` and he steal it , '' Cecily throw passionately over her shoulder at Mr. Perkins -- that her eye be so sweet and lovely that he could n't find word nice enuf to describ them , that he could never forget how butiful she have look in prar meeting the evening before , and that some meels he could n't eat for thinking of her , with more to the same effect and he sign it `` yours till deth u do part , Cyrus Brisk . ''
As the writing proceed we scholar explode into smothered laughter , despite our awe of Mr. Perkins .
Mr. Perkins himself could not keep a straight face .
He turn abruptly away and look out of the window , but we could see his shoulder shake .
When Cecily have finish and have throw down the chalk with bitter vehemence , he turn around with a very red face .
`` That will do .
You may sit down .
Cyrus , since it seem you be the guilty person , take the eraser and wipe that off the board .
Then go stand in the corner , face the room , and hold your arm straight above your head until I tell you to take them down . ''
Cyrus obey and Cecily flee to her seat and wept , nor do Mr. Perkins meddle with her more that day .
She bore her burden of humiliation bitterly for several day , until she be suddenly comfort by a realization that Cyrus have cease to persecute her .
He write no more letter , he gaze no longer in rapt adoration , he bring no more votive offering of gum and pencil to her shrine .
At first we think he have be cure by the unmerciful chaffing he have to undergo from his mate , but eventually his sister tell Cecily the true reason .
Cyrus have at last be drive to believe that Cecily 's aversion to him be real , and not merely the defence of maiden coyness .
If she hat him so intensely that she would rather write that note on the blackboard than sit with him , what use be it to sigh like a furnace longer for her ?
Mr. Perkins have blight love 's young dream for Cyrus with a kill frost .
Thenceforth sweet Cecily keep the noiseless tenor of her way unvexed by the attention of enamoured swain .
CHAPTER XVI .
AUNT UNA 'S STORY Felicity , and Cecily , Dan , Felix , Sara Ray and I be sit one evening on the mossy stone in Uncle Roger 's hill pasture , where we have sit the morning the Story Girl tell u the tale of the Wedding Veil of the Proud Princess .

Peter have go to Markdale after dinner to spend the afternoon with his reunited parent because it be his birthday .
He have leave u grimly determine to confess to his father the dark secret of his Presbyterianism , and we be anxious to know what the result have be .

yell Dan , as soon a Peter be within earshot .

`` I be anxious to have it over with .

I 'm sorry I ca n't be a Methodist , like you and mother and Aunt Jane , but I ca n't and that 's all there be to it , ' I say .

I 'm not care , ' he say .
` The main thing be that you must be good and do what 's right . '
I tell you , '' conclude Peter emphatically , `` father be a Christian all right . ''
`` Well , I suppose your mind will be at rest now , '' say Felicity .
`` What 's that you have in your buttonhole ? ''
`` That 's a four-leaved clover , '' answer Peter exultantly .
`` That mean good luck for the summer .
I find it in Markdale .
There ai n't much clover in Carlisle this year of any kind of leaf .
The crop be go to be a failure .

There 's lot of them in Markdale , and that 's the reason , he say , why they always have such good clover crop there . ''
`` What on earth have old maid to do with it ? ''

`` I do n't believe they 've a single thing to do with it , but Mr. Roger say they have , and he say a man call Darwin prove it .

But mice eat bumble-bees and cat eat mouse and old maid keep cat .
So your Uncle Roger say the more old maids the more cat , and the more cat the few field-mice , and the few field-mice the more bumble-bees , and the more bumble-bees the good clover crop . ''
`` So do n't worry if you do get to be old maid , girl , '' say Dan .
`` Remember , you 'll be help the clover crop . ''

`` There come the Story Girl , '' cry Cecily eagerly .
`` Now we 'll hear all about Beautiful Alice 's home . ''
The Story Girl be bombard with eager question as soon a she arrive .
Miss Reade 's home be a dream of a place , it appear .

And I saw the hero of the story too . ''
`` Where be the heroine ? ''
query Cecily .
`` She be dead . ''
`` Oh , of course she 'd have to die , '' exclaim Dan in disgust .
`` I 'd like a story where somebody live once in awhile . ''

`` If this heroine have n't die there would n't have be any story .

Miss Reade tell me all about her .

I say .
`` Beautiful Alice laugh and say it be forty year since he have be her Aunt Una 's lover .
He have be a tall , handsome young man then , and her Aunt Una be a beautiful girl of nineteen .
`` We go over and sit down and Miss Reade tell me all about her .
She say that when she be a child she have hear much of her Aunt Una -- that she seem to have be one of those people who be not soon forgotten , whose personality seem to linger about the scene of their life long after they have pass away . ''
`` What be a personality ?
Is it another word for ghost ? ''
ask Peter .
`` No , '' say the Story Girl shortly .
`` I ca n't stop in a story to explain word . ''
`` I do n't believe you know what it be yourself , '' say Felicity .
The Story Girl pick up her hat , which she have throw down on the grass , and place it defiantly on her brown curl .
`` I 'm go in , '' she announce .

`` Dan and Felix and Sara Ray and Cecily and I have never say a word .

`` I only want to know , '' mutter Peter sulkily .
`` I DO know what personality be , but it 's hard to explain , '' say the Story Girl , relent .
`` It 's what make you different from Dan , Peter , and me different from Felicity or Cecily .

And she be beautiful , too , with white skin and night-black eye and hair -- a ` moonlight beauty , ' Miss Reade call it .
She use to keep a kind of a diary , and Miss Reade 's mother use to read part of it to her .
She write verse in it and they be lovely ; and she write description of the old garden which she love very much .
Miss Reade say that everything in the garden , plot or shrub or tree , recall to her mind some phrase or verse of her Aunt Una 's , so that the whole place seem full of her , and her memory haunt the walk like a faint , sweet perfume .
`` Una have , a I 've tell you , a lover ; and they be to have be marry on her twentieth birthday .
Her wedding dress be to have be a gown of white brocade with purple violet in it .
But a little while before it she take ill with fever and die ; and she be bury on her birthday instead of be marry .
It be just in the time of open rose .

Miss Reade say she always love to see him sit there because it give her such a deep and lasting sense of the beauty and strength of love which can thus outlive time and death .
And sometimes , she say , it give her a little eerie feeling , too , a if her Aunt Una be really sit there beside him , keep tryst , although she have be in her grave for forty year . ''
`` It would be real romantic to die young and have your lover make a pilgrimage to your garden every year , '' reflect Sara Ray .

`` There 's nobody in Carlisle half good enough for her , '' cry the Story Girl , `` except -- ex-cept -- '' `` Except who ? ''
ask Felix .
`` Never mind , '' say the Story Girl mysteriously .
CHAPTER XVII .
AUNT OLIVIA 'S WEDDING What a delightful , old-fashioned , wholesome excitement there be about Aunt Olivia 's wedding !

Monday evening shroud itself in cloud , and all night long the voice of the wind answer to the voice of the rain .
Tuesday the downpour continue .
We be quite frantic about it .
Suppose it keep on raining over Wednesday !
Aunt Olivia could n't be marry in the orchard then .
That would be too bad , especially when the late apple tree have most obligingly keep it store of blossom until after all the other tree have fade and then burst lavishly into bloom for Aunt Olivia 's wedding .
That apple tree be always very late in blooming , and this year it be a week later than usual .
It be a sight to see -- a great tree-pyramid with high , far-spreading bough , over which a wealth of rosy snow seem to have be fling .

SHE can take a joke . ''

`` Judy Pineau bring it up when she bring Mrs. Ray 's spoon .

Last night I go with Judy to water the cow and in the spruce bush we find a WASPS ' NEST and Judy think it be AN OLD ONE and she POKED IT WITH A STICK .

`` Why do n't you get marry yourself , Peg ? ''

`` Wasps , '' stammer Sara Ray , laconic from terror .
`` Humph !
And your hand ? ''
`` Warts . ''
`` I 'll tell you what 'll take them away .
You get a pertater and go out under the full moon , cut the pertater in two , rub your wart with one half and say , ` One , two , three , wart , go away from me . '
Then rub them with the other half and say , ` One , two , three , four , wart , never trouble me more . '
Then bury the pertater and never tell a living soul where you bury it .
You wo n't have no more wart .
Mind you bury the pertater , though .
If you do n't , and anyone pick it up , she 'll get your wart . ''
CHAPTER XVIII .
SARA RAY HELPS OUT We all miss Aunt Olivia greatly ; she have be so merry and companionable , and have possess such a knack of understand small fry .
But youth quickly adapt itself to change condition ; in a few week it seem a if the Story Girl have always be live at Uncle Alec 's , and a if Uncle Roger have always have a fat , jolly housekeeper with a double chin and little , twinkle blue eye .
I do n't think Aunt Janet ever quite get over miss Aunt Olivia , or look upon Mrs. Hawkins a anything but a necessary evil ; but life resume it even tenor on the King farm , break only by the ripple of excitement over the school concert and letter from Aunt Olivia describe her trip through the land of Evangeline .
We incorporate the letter in Our Magazine under the head `` From Our Special Correspondent '' and be very proud of them .
At the end of June our school concert come off and be a great event in our young life .
It be the first appearance of most of u on any platform , and some of u be very nervous .
We all have recitation , except Dan , who have refuse flatly to take any part and be consequently care-free .
`` I 'm sure I shall die when I find myself up on that platform , face people , '' sigh Sara Ray , a we talk the affair over in Uncle Stephen 's Walk the night before the concert .
`` I 'm afraid I 'll faint , '' be Cecily 's more moderate foreboding .
`` I 'm not one single bit nervous , '' say Felicity complacently .
`` I 'm not nervous this time , '' say the Story Girl , `` but the first time I recite I be . ''
`` My Aunt Jane , '' remark Peter , `` use to say that an old teacher of hers tell her that when she be go to recite or speak in public she must just get it firmly into her mind that it be only a lot of cabbage head she have before her , and she would n't be nervous . ''
`` One might n't be nervous , but I do n't think there would be much inspiration in recite to cabbage head , '' say the Story Girl decidedly .
`` I want to recite to PEOPLE , and see them look interested and thrill . ''
`` If I can only get through my piece without break down I do n't care whether I thrill people or not , '' say Sara Ray .
`` I 'm afraid I 'll forget mine and get stick , '' forebode Felix .
`` Some of you fellows be sure and prompt me if I do -- and do it quick , so 's I wo n't get bad rattle . ''
`` I know one thing , '' say Cecily resolutely , `` and that be , I 'm go to curl my hair for to-morrow night .
I 've never curl it since Peter almost die , but I simply must tomorrow night , for all the other girl be go to have theirs in curl . ''
`` The dew and heat will take all the curl out of yours and then you 'll look like a scarecrow , '' warn Felicity .
`` No , I wo n't .
I 'm go to put my hair up in paper tonight and wet it with a curling-fluid that Judy Pineau use .
Sara bring me up a bottle of it .
Judy say it be great stuff -- your hair will keep in curl for day , no matter how damp the weather be .
I 'll leave my hair in the paper till tomorrow evening , and then I 'll have beautiful curl . ''
`` You 'd better leave your hair alone , '' say Dan gruffly .
`` Smooth hair be good than a lot of fly-away curl . ''
But Cecily be not to be persuade .
Curls she crave and curl she mean to have .
`` I 'm thankful my wart have all go , any-way , '' say Sara Ray .
`` So they have , '' exclaim Felicity .
`` Did you try Peg 's recipe ? ''
`` Yes .
I do n't believe in it but I try it .
For the first few day afterwards I keep watch my wart , but they do n't go away , and then I give up and forget them .
But one day last week I just happen to look at my hand and there be n't a wart to be see .
It be the most amazing thing . ''
`` And yet you 'll say Peg Bowen be n't a witch , '' say Peter .
`` Pshaw , it be just the potato juice , '' scoff Dan .
`` It be a dry old potato I have , and there be n't much juice in it , '' say Sara Ray .
`` One hardly know what to believe .
But one thing be certain -- my wart be go . ''
Cecily put her hair up in curl-papers that night , thoroughly soak in Judy Pineau 's curling-fluid .
It be a nasty job , for the fluid be very sticky , but Cecily persevere and get it do .
Then she go to bed with a towel tie over her head to protect the pillow .
She do not sleep well and have uncanny dream , but she come down to breakfast with an expression of triumph .
The Story Girl examine her head critically and say , `` Cecily , if I be you I 'd take those paper out this morning . ''
`` Oh , no ; if I do my hair will be straight again by night .
I mean to leave them in till the last minute . ''
`` I would n't do that -- I really would n't , '' persist the Story Girl .
`` If you do your hair will be too curly and all bushy and fuzzy . ''
Cecily finally yield and go upstairs with the Story Girl .
Presently we hear a little shriek -- then two little shriek -- then three .
Then Felicity come fly down and call her mother .
Aunt Janet go up and presently come down again with a grim mouth .
She fill a large pan with warm water and carry it upstairs .
We dare ask her no question , but when Felicity come down to wash the dish we bombard her .
`` What on earth be the matter with Cecily ? ''
demand Dan .
`` Is she sick ? ''
`` No , she be n't .
I warn her not to put her hair in curl but she would n't listen to me .
I guess she wish she have now .
When people have n't natural curly hair they should n't try to make it curly .
They get punish if they do . ''
`` Look here , Felicity , never mind all that .
Just tell u what have happen Sis . ''
`` Well , this be what have happen her .
That ninny of a Sara Ray bring up a bottle of mucilage instead of Judy 's curling-fluid , and Cecily put her hair up with THAT .
It 's in an awful state . ''
`` Good gracious ! ''
exclaim Dan .
`` Look here , will she ever get it out ? ''
`` Goodness know .
She 's get her head in soak now .
Her hair be just mat together hard a a board .
That 's what come of vanity , '' say Felicity , than whom no vainer girl exist .
Poor Cecily pay dearly enough for HER vanity .
She spend a bad forenoon , make no easier by her mother 's severe rebuke .
For an hour she `` soaked '' her head ; that be , she stand over a panful of warm water and keep dip her head in with tightly shut eye .
Finally her hair soften sufficiently to be disentangle from the curl paper ; and then Aunt Janet subject it to a merciless shampoo .
Eventually they get all the mucilage wash out of it and Cecily spend the remainder of the forenoon sit before the open oven door in the hot kitchen dry her ill-used tress .
She felt very down-hearted ; her hair be of that order which , glossy and smooth normally , be dry and harsh and lustreless for several day after be shampooed .
`` I 'll look like a fright tonight , '' say the poor child to me with tremble voice .
`` The end will be stick out all over my head . ''
`` Sara Ray be a perfect idiot , '' I say wrathfully `` Oh , do n't be hard on poor Sara .
She do n't mean to bring me mucilage .
It 's really all my own fault , I know .
I make a solemn vow when Peter be die that I would never curl my hair again , and I should have keep it .
It be n't right to break solemn vow .
But my hair will look like dried hay tonight . ''
Poor Sara Ray be quite overwhelmed when she come up and find what she have do .
Felicity be very hard on her , and Aunt Janet be coldly disapproving , but sweet Cecily forgive her unreservedly , and they walk to the school that night with their arm about each other 's waist a usual .
The school-room be crowd with friend and neighbour .
Mr. Perkins be fly about , get thing into readiness , and Miss Reade , who be the organist of the evening , be sit on the platform , look her sweetest and prettiest .
She wear a delightful white lace hat with a fetching little wreath of tiny forget-me-not around the brim , a white muslin dress with spray of blue violet scatter over it , and a black lace scarf .
`` Does n't she look angelic ? ''
say Cecily rapturously .
`` Mind you , '' say Sara Ray , `` the Awkward Man be here -- in the corner behind the door .
I never remember see him at a concert before . ''
`` I suppose he come to hear the Story Girl recite , '' say Felicity .
`` He be such a friend of hers . ''
The concert go off very well .
Dialogues , chorus and recitation follow each other in rapid succession .
Felix get through his without `` get stuck , '' and Peter do excellently , though he stuff his hand in his trouser pocket -- a habit of which Mr. Perkins have vainly try to break him .
Peter 's recitation be one greatly in vogue at that time , begin , `` My name be Norval ; on the Grampian hill My father feed his flock . ''
At our first practice Peter have start gaily in , rush through the first line with no thought whatever of punctuation -- `` My name be Norval on the Grampian Hills . ''
`` Stop , stop , Peter , '' quoth Mr. Perkins , sarcastically , `` your name might be Norval if you be never on the Grampian Hills .
There 's a semi-colon in that line , I wish you to remember . ''
Peter do remember it .
Cecily neither faint nor fail when it come her turn .
She recite her little piece very well , though somewhat mechanically .
I think she really do much good than if she have have her desired curl .
The miserable conviction that her hair , alone among that glossy-tressed bevy , be look badly , quite blot out all nervousness and self-consciousness from her mind .
Her hair apart , she look very pretty .
The prevailing excitement have make bright her eye and flush her cheeks rosily -- too rosily , perhaps .
I hear a Carlisle woman behind me whisper that Cecily King look consumptive , just like her Aunt Felicity ; and I hat her fiercely for it .
Sara Ray also manage to get through respectably , although she be pitiably nervous .
Her bow be naught but a short nod -- `` a if her head work on wire , '' whisper Felicity uncharitably -- and the wave of her lily-white hand more nearly resemble an agonized jerk than a wave .
We all felt relieve when she finish .
She be , in a sense , one of `` our crowd , '' and we have be afraid she would disgrace u by break down .
Felicity follow her and recite her selection without haste , without rest , and absolutely without any expression whatever .
But what matter it how she recite ?
To look at her be sufficient .
What with her splendid fleece of golden curl , her great , brilliant blue eye , her exquisitely tinted face , her dimpled hand and arm , every member of the audience must have felt it be worth the ten cent he have pay merely to see her .
The Story Girl follow .
An expectant silence fell over the room , and Mr. Perkins ' face lose the look of tense anxiety it have wear all the evening .
Here be a performer who could be depend on .
No need to fear stage fright or forgetfulness on her part .
The Story Girl be not look her best that night .
White never become her , and her face be pale , though her eye be splendid .
But nobody think about her appearance when the power and magic of her voice caught and hold her listener spellbound .
Her recitation be an old one , figure in one of the School Readers , and we scholars all know it off by heart .
Sara Ray alone have not hear the Story Girl recite it .
The latter have not be drill at practice a have the other pupil , Mr. Perkins choose not to waste time teach her what she already know far good than he do .
The only time she have recite it have be at the `` dress rehearsal '' two night before , at which Sara Ray have not be present .
In the poem a Florentine lady of old time , wed to a cold and cruel husband , have die , or be suppose to have die , and have be carry to `` the rich , the beautiful , the dreadful tomb '' of her proud family .
In the night she waken from her trance and make her escape .
Chilled and terrify , she have make her way to her husband 's door , only to be drive away brutally a a restless ghost by the horror-stricken inmate .
A similar reception await her at her father 's .
Then she have wander blindly through the street of Florence until she have fall exhaust at the door of the lover of her girlhood .
He , unafraid , have take her in and care for her .
On the morrow , the husband and father , have discover the empty tomb , come to claim her .
She refuse to return to them and the case be carry to the court of law .
The verdict give be that a woman who have be `` to burial borne '' and leave for dead , who have be driven from her husband 's door and from her childhood home , `` must be adjudge a dead in law and fact , '' be no more daughter or wife , but be set free to form what new tie she would .
The climax of the whole selection come in the line , `` The court pronounce the defendant -- DEAD ! ''
and the Story Girl be wont to render it with such dramatic intensity and power that the veriest dullard among her listener could not have miss it force and significance .
She sweep along through the poem royally , play on the emotion of her audience a she have so often play on ours in the old orchard .
Pity , terror , indignation , suspense , possess her hearer in turn .
In the court scene she surpass herself .
She be , in very truth , the Florentine judge , stern , stately , impassive .
Her voice drop into the solemnity of the all-important line , '' ` The court pronounce the defendant -- ' '' She pause for a breathless moment , the good to bring out the tragic import of the last word .
`` DEAD , '' pip up Sara Ray in her shrill , plaintive little voice .
The effect , to use a hackneyed but convenient phrase , can well be imagine than described .
Instead of the sigh of relieved tension that should have sweep over the audience at the conclusion of the line , a burst of laughter greet it .
The Story Girl 's performance be completely spoil .
She deal the luckless Sara a glance that would have slay her on the spot could glance kill , stumble lamely and impotently through the few remain line of her recitation , and flee with crimson cheek to hide her mortification in the little corner that have be curtain off for a dressing-room .
Mr. Perkins look thing not lawful to be utter , and the audience titter at interval for the rest of the performance .
Sara Ray alone remain serenely satisfy until the close of the concert , when we surround her with a whirlwind of reproach .
`` Why , '' she stammer aghast , `` what do I do ?
I -- I think she be stick and that I ought to prompt her quick . ''
`` You little fool , she just pause for effect , '' cry Felicity angrily .
Felicity might be rather jealous of the Story Girl 's gift , but she be furious at behold `` one of our family '' make ridiculous in such a fashion .
`` You have less sense than anyone I ever heard of , Sara Ray . ''
Poor Sara dissolve in tear .
`` I do n't know .
I think she be stick , '' she wail again .
She cry all the way home , but we do not try to comfort her .
We felt quite out of patience with her .
Even Cecily be seriously annoy .
This second blunder of Sara 's be too much even for her loyalty .
We saw her turn in at her own gate and go sob up her lane with no relenting .
The Story Girl be home before u , have flee from the schoolhouse as soon a the programme be over .
We try to sympathize with her but she would not be sympathize with .
`` Please do n't ever mention it to me again , '' she say , with compress lip .
`` I never want to be remind of it .
Oh , that little IDIOT ! ''
`` She spoil Peter 's sermon last summer and now she 's spoil your recitation , '' say Felicity .
`` I think it 's time we give up associate with Sara Ray . ''
`` Oh , do n't be quite so hard on her , '' plead Cecily .
`` Think of the life the poor child have to live at home .
I know she 'll cry all night . ''
`` Oh , let 's go to bed , '' growl Dan .
`` I 'm good and ready for it .
I 've have enough of school concert . ''
CHAPTER XIX .
BY WAY OF THE STARS But for two of u the adventure of the night be not yet over .
Silence settle down over the old house -- the eerie , whisperful , creep silence of night .
Felix and Dan be already sound asleep ; I be drift near the coast o ' dream when I be arouse by a light tap on the door .
`` Bev , be you asleep ? ''
come in the Story Girl 's whisper .
`` No , what be it ? ''
`` S-s-h .
Get up and dress and come out .
I want you . ''
With a good deal of curiosity and some misgiving I obey .
What be in the wind now ?
Outside in the hall I find the Story Girl , with a candle in her hand , and her hat and jacket .
`` Where be you go ? ''
I whisper in amazement .
`` Hush .
I 've get to go to the school and you must come with me .
I leave my coral necklace there .
The clasp come loose and I be so afraid I 'd lose it that I take it off and put it in the bookcase .
I be feel so upset when the concert be over that I forget all about it . ''
The coral necklace be a very handsome one which have belong to the Story Girl 's mother .
She have never be permit to wear it before , and it have only be by dint of much coaxing that she have induce Aunt Janet to let her wear it to the concert .
`` But there 's no sense in go for it in the dead of night , '' I object .
`` It will be quite safe .
You can go for it in the morning . ''
`` Lizzie Paxton and her daughter be go to clean the school tomorrow , and I hear Lizzie say tonight she mean to be at it by five o'clock to get through before the heat of the day .
You know perfectly well what Liz Paxton 's reputation be .
If she find that necklace I 'll never see it again .
Besides , if I wait till the morning , Aunt Janet may find out that I leave it there and she 'd never let me wear it again .
No , I 'm go for it now .
If you 're afraid , '' add the Story Girl with delicate scorn , `` of course you need n't come . ''
Afraid !
I 'd show her !
`` Come on , '' I say .
We slip out of the house noiselessly and find ourselves in the unutterable solemnity and strangeness of a dark night .
It be a new experience , and our heart thrill and our nerve tingle to the charm of it .
Never have we be abroad before at such an hour .
The world around u be not the world of daylight .
'T be an alien place , full of weird , evasive enchantment and magicry .
Only in the country can one become truly acquainted with the night .
There it have the solemn calm of the infinite .
The dim wide field lie in silence , wrap in the holy mystery of darkness .
A wind , loosen from wild place far away , steal out to blow over dewy , star-lit , immemorial hill .
The air in the pasture be sweet with the hush of dream , and one may rest here like a child on it mother 's breast .
`` Is n't it wonderful ? ''
breathe the Story Girl a we go down the long hill .
`` Do you know , I can forgive Sara Ray now .
I think tonight I never could -- but now it do n't matter any more .
I can even see how funny it be .
Oh , be n't it funny ?
` DEAD ' in that squeaky little voice of Sara 's !
I 'll just behave to her tomorrow a if nothing have happen .
It seem so long ago now , here in the night . ''
Neither of u ever forget the subtle delight of that steal walk .
A spell of glamour be over u .
The breeze whisper strange secret of elf-haunted glen , and the hollow where the fern grow be brim with mystery and romance .
Ghostlike scent creep out of the meadow to meet u , and the fir wood before we come to the church be a living sweetness of Junebells grow in abundance .
Junebells have another and more scientific name , of course .
But who could desire a good name than Junebells ?
They be so perfect in their way that they seem to epitomize the very scent and charm of the forest , a if the old wood 's dainty thought have materialize in blossom ; and not all the rose by Bendameer 's stream be as fragrant a a shallow sheet of Junebells under the bough of fir .
There be firefly abroad that night , too , increase the gramarye of it .
There be certainly something a little supernatural about firefly .
Nobody pretend to understand them .
They be akin to the tribe of fairy , survival of the elder time when the wood and hill swarm with the little green folk .
It be still very easy to believe in fairy when you see those goblin lantern glimmer among the fir tassel .
`` Is n't it beautiful ? ''
say the Story Girl in rapture .
`` I would n't have miss it for anything .
I 'm glad I leave my necklace .
And I be glad you be with me , Bev .
The others would n't understand so well .
I like you because I do n't have to talk to you all the time .
It 's so nice to walk with someone you do n't have to talk to .
Here be the graveyard .
Are you frighten to pass it , Bev ? ''
`` No , I do n't think I 'm frightened , '' I answer slowly , `` but I have a queer feeling . ''
`` So have I .
But it be n't fear .
I do n't know what it be .
I feel a if something be reach out of the graveyard to hold me -- something that want life -- I do n't like it -- let 's hurry .
But be n't it strange to think of all the dead people in there who be once alive like you and me .
I do n't feel a if I could EVER die .
Do you ? ''
`` No , but everybody must .
Of course we go on living afterwards , just the same .
Do n't let 's talk of such thing here , '' I say hurriedly .
When we reach the school I contrive to open a window .
We scramble in , light a lamp and find the miss necklace .
The Story Girl stand on the platform and give an imitation of the catastrophe of the evening that make me shout with laughter .
We prowl around for sheer delight over be there at an unearthly hour when everybody suppose we be sound asleep in our bed .
It be with regret that we leave , and we walk home as slowly a we could to prolong the adventure .
`` Let 's never tell anyone , '' say the Story Girl , a we reach home .
`` Let 's just have it a a secret between u for ever and ever -- something that nobody else know a thing about but you and me . ''
`` We 'd well keep it a secret from Aunt Janet anyhow , '' I whisper , laugh .
`` She 'd think we be both crazy . ''
`` It 's real jolly to be crazy once in a while , '' say the Story Girl .
CHAPTER XX .

THE STORY OF THE LOCKET THAT WAS BAKED This be a story my Aunt Jane tell me about her granma when she be a little girl .
Its funny to think of bake a locket , but it be n't to eat .
She be my great granma but Ill call her granma for short .
It happen when she be ten year old .
Of course she wasent anybodys granma then .
Her father and mother and her be live in a new settlement call Brinsley .
Their near naybor be a mile away .
One day her Aunt Hannah from Charlottetown come and want her ma to go visit with her .
At first granma 's ma think she couldent go because it be bake day and granma 's pa be away .
But granma wasent afraid to stay alone and she know how to bake the bread so she make her ma go and her Aunt Hannah take off the handsome gold locket and chain she be war round her neck and hung it on granmas and tell her she could ware it all day .
Granma be awful pleased for she have never have any jewelry .
She do all the chore and then be need the loaf when she look up and saw a tramp come in and he be an awful villenus look tramp .
He dident even pass the time of day but just set down on a chair .
Poor granma be awful fritened and she turn her back on him and go on need the loaf cold and trembling -- that be , granma be tremble not the loaf .
She be worry about the locket .
She do n't know how she could hide it for to get anywhere she would have to turn round and pas him .
All of a suddent she think she would hide it in the bread .
She put her hand up and pull it hard and quick and break the fastening and need it right into the loaf .
Then she put the loaf in the pan and set it in the oven .
The tramp hadent see her do it and then he ask for something to eat .
Granma get him up a meal and when hed et it he begin prowl about the kitchen look into everything and open the cubbord door .
Then he go into granma 's ma room and turn the buro drawer and trunk inside out and throw the thing in them all about .
All he find be a purse with a dollar in it and he swore about it and take it and go away .
When granma be sure he be really go she break down and cry .
She forget all about the bread and it burn as black a coal .
When she smell it burn granma run and pull it out .
She be awful scar the locket be spoil but she saw open the loaf and it be there safe and sound .
When her Aunt Hannah come back she say granma deserve the locket because she have save it so clever and she give it to her and grandma always wear it and be very proud of it .
And granma use to say that be the only loaf of bread she ever spoil in her life .

MY MOST EXCITING ADVENTURE It 's my turn to write it but I 'm SO NERVOUS .
My bad adventure happen TWO YEARS AGO .
It be an awful one .
I have a striped ribbon , strip brown and yellow and I LOST IT .
I be very sorry for it be a handsome ribbon and all the girl in school be jealous of it .

I would rather DIE than have SUCH AN EXPERIENCE again .

HOUSEHOLD DEPARTMENT Aunt Olivia 's wed cake be say to be the best one of it kind ever taste in Carlisle .
Me and mother make it .
ANXIOUS INQUIRER : -- It be not advisable to curl your hair with mucilage if you can get anything else .
Quince juice be well .
-LRB- CECILY , BITTERLY : `` I suppose I 'll never hear the last of that mucilage . ''
DAN : `` Ask her who use tooth-powder to raise biscuit ? '' -RRB-
We have rhubarb pie for the first time this spring last week .
They be fine but hard on the cream .
FELICITY KING .
ETIQUETTE DEPARTMENT PATIENT SUFFERER : -- What will I do when a young man steal a lock of my hair ?
Ans . : -- Grow some more .
No , F-l-x , a little caterpillar be not call a kittenpillar .
-LRB- FELIX , ENRAGED : `` I never ask that !
Dan just make that etiquette column up from begin to end ! ''
FELICITY : `` I do n't see what that kind of a question have to do with etiquette anyhow . '' -RRB-
Yes , P-t-r , it be quite proper to treat a lady friend to ice cream twice if you can afford it .
No , F-l-c-t-y , it be not ladylike to chew tobacco .

DAN KING .
FASHION NOTES Frilled muslin apron will be much worn this summer .
It be no longer fashionable to trim them with knit lace .
One pocket be consider smart .
Clam-shells be fashionable keepsake .
You write your name and the date inside one and your friend write hers in the other and you exchange .
CECILY KING .
FUNNY PARAGRAPHS MR. PERKINS : -- `` Peter , name the large island of the world . ''
PETER : -- `` The Island , the British Isles and Australia . ''
-LRB- PETER , DEFIANTLY : `` Well , Mr. Perkins say he guess I be right , so you need n't laugh . '' -RRB-
This be a true joke and really happen .
It 's about Mr. Samuel Clask again .
He be once lead a prayer meeting and he look through the window and saw the constable driving up and guess he be after him because he be always in debt .
So in a great hurry he call on Brother Casey to lead in prayer and while Brother Casey be pray with his eye shut and everybody else have their head bow Mr. Clask get out of the window and get away before the constable got in because he do n't like to come in till the prayer be finish .
Uncle Roger say it be a smart trick on Mr. Clask 's part , but I do n't think there be much religion about it .
FELIX KING .
CHAPTER XXI .
PEG BOWEN COMES TO CHURCH When those of u who be still leave of that band of child who play long year ago in the old orchard and walk the golden road together in joyous companionship , foregather now and again in our busy life and talk over the event of those many merry moon -- there be some of our adventure that gleam out more vividly in memory than the others , and be oftener discuss .
The time we buy God 's picture from Jerry Cowan -- the time Dan eat the poison berry -- the time we hear the ghostly bell ring -- the bewitchment of Paddy -- the visit of the Governor 's wife -- and the night we be lose in the storm -- all awaken reminiscent jest and laughter ; but none more than the recollection of the Sunday Peg Bowen come to church and sat in our pew .
Though goodness know , a Felicity would say , we do not think it any matter for laughter at the time -- far from it .
It be one Sunday evening in July .
Uncle Alec and Aunt Janet , have be out to the morning service , do not attend in the evening , and we small fry walk together down the long hill road , wear Sunday attire and try , more or less successfully , to wear Sunday face also .
Those walk to church , through the golden completeness of the summer evening , be always very pleasant to u , and we never hurry , though , on the other hand , we be very careful not to be late .
This particular evening be particularly beautiful .
It be cool after a hot day , and wheat field all about u be ripen to their harvestry .
The wind gossip with the grass along our way , and over them the buttercup dance , goldenly-glad .
Waves of sinuous shadow go over the ripe hayfield , and plunder bee sing a freebooting lilt in wayside garden .
`` The world be so lovely tonight , '' say the Story Girl .
`` I just hate the thought of go into the church and shut all the sunlight and music outside .
I wish we could have the service outside in summer . ''
`` I do n't think that would be very religious , '' say Felicity .
`` I 'd feel ever so much more religious outside than in , '' retort the Story Girl .
`` If the service be outside we 'd have to sit in the graveyard and that would n't be very cheerful , '' say Felix .
`` Besides , the music be n't shut out , '' add Felicity .
`` The choir be inside . '' ''
` Music have charm to soothe a savage breast , ' '' quote Peter , who be get into the habit of adorn his conversation with similar gem .
`` That 's in one of Shakespeare 's play .
I 'm read them now , since I get through with the Bible .
They 're great . ''
`` I do n't see when you get time to read them , '' say Felicity .
`` Oh , I read them Sunday afternoon when I 'm home . ''
`` I do n't believe they 're fit to read on Sundays , '' exclaim Felicity .
`` Mother say Valeria Montague 's story ai n't . ''
`` But Shakespeare 's different from Valeria , '' protest Peter .
`` I do n't see in what way .
He write a lot of thing that be n't true , just like Valeria , and he write swear word too .
Valeria never do that .
Her character all talk in a very refined fashion . ''
`` Well , I always skip the swear word , '' say Peter .
`` And Mr. Marwood say once that the Bible and Shakespeare would furnish any library well .
So you see he put them together , but I 'm sure that he would never say that the Bible and Valeria would make a library . ''
`` Well , all I know be , I shall never read Shakespeare on Sunday , '' say Felicity loftily .
`` I wonder what kind of a preacher young Mr. Davidson be , '' speculate Cecily .
`` Well , we 'll know when we hear him tonight , '' say the Story Girl .
`` He ought to be good , for his uncle before him be a fine preacher , though a very absent-minded man .
But Uncle Roger say the supply in Mr. Marwood 's vacation never amount to much .
I know an awfully funny story about old Mr. Davidson .
He use to be the minister in Baywater , you know , and he have a large family and his child be very mischievous .
One day his wife be iron and she iron a great big nightcap with a frill round it .
One of the child take it when she be n't look and hide it in his father 's best beaver hat -- the one he wear on Sundays .
When Mr. Davidson go to church next Sunday he put the hat on without ever look into the crown .
He walk to church in a brown study and at the door he take off his hat .
The nightcap just slip down on his head , a if it have be put on , and the frill stand out around his face and the string hang down his back .
But he never notice it , because his thought be far away , and he walk up the church aisle and into the pulpit , like that .
One of his elder have to tiptoe up and tell him what he have on his head .
He pluck it off in a dazed fashion , hold it up , and look at it .
` Bless me , it be Sally 's nightcap ! '
he exclaim mildly . '
I do not know how I could have get it on . '
Then he just stuff it into his pocket calmly and go on with the service , and the long string of the nightcap hang down out of his pocket all the time . ''
`` It seem to me , '' say Peter , amid the laughter with which we greet the tale , `` that a funny story be funny when it be about a minister than it be about any other man .
I wonder why . ''
`` Sometimes I do n't think it be right to tell funny story about minister , '' say Felicity .
`` It certainly be n't respectful . ''
`` A good story be a good story -- no matter who it 's about , '' say the Story Girl with ungrammatical relish .
There be a yet no one in the church when we reach it , so we take our accustomed ramble through the graveyard surround it .
The Story Girl have bring flower for her mother 's grave a usual , and while she arrange them on it the rest of u read for the hundredth time the epitaph on Great-Grandfather King 's tombstone , which have be compose by Great-Grandmother King .
That epitaph be quite famous among the little family tradition that entwine every household with mingled mirth and sorrow , smile and tear .
It have a perennial fascination for u and we read it over every Sunday .
Cut deeply in the upright slab of red Island sandstone , the epitaph run a follow : -- SWEET DEPARTED SPIRIT Do receive the vow a grateful widow pay , Each future day and night shall hear her speak her Isaac 's praise .
Though thy beloved form must in the grave decay Yet from her heart thy memory no time , no change shall steal away .
Do thou from mansion of eternal bliss Remember thy distress relict .
Look on her with an angel 's love -- Soothe her sad life and cheer her end Through this world 's danger and it grief .
Then meet her with thy well-known smile and welcome At the last great day .
`` Well , I ca n't make out what the old lady be drive at , '' say Dan .
`` That 's a nice way to speak of your great-grandmother , '' say Felicity severely .
`` How do The Family Guide say you ought to speak of your great-grandma , sweet one ? ''
ask Dan .
`` There be one thing about it that puzzle me , '' remark Cecily .
`` She call herself a GRATEFUL widow .
Now , what be she grateful for ? ''
`` Because she be rid of him at last , '' say graceless Dan .
`` Oh , it could n't have be that , '' protest Cecily seriously .
`` I 've always hear that Great-Grandfather and Great-Grandmother be very much attach to each other . ''
`` Maybe , then , it mean she be grateful that she 'd have him as long a she do , '' suggest Peter .
`` She be grateful to him because he have be so kind to her in life , I think , '' say Felicity .
`` What be a ` distressed relict ' ? ''
ask Felix . ''
` Relict ' be a word I hate , '' say the Story Girl .
`` It sound so much like relic .
Relict mean just the same a widow , only a man can be a relict , too . ''
`` Great-Grandmother seem to run short of rhyme at the last of the epitaph , '' comment Dan .
`` Finding rhyme be n't as easy a you might think , '' avow Peter , out of his own experience .
`` I think Grandmother King intend the last of the epitaph to be in blank verse , '' say Felicity with dignity .
There be still only a sprinkling of people in the church when we go in and take our place in the old-fashioned , square King pew .
We have just get comfortably settle when Felicity say in an agitated whisper , `` Here be Peg Bowen ! ''
We all star at Peg , who be pace composedly up the aisle .
We might be excuse for so do , for seldom be the decorous aisle of Carlisle church invade by such a figure .
Peg be dress in her usual short drugget skirt , rather worn and fray around the bottom , and a waist of brilliant turkey red calico .
She wear no hat , and her grizzled black hair stream in elf lock over her shoulder .
Face , arm and foot be bare -- and face , arm and foot be liberally powder with FLOUR .
Certainly no one who saw Peg that night could ever forget the apparition .
Peg 's black eye , in which shine a more than usually wild and fitful light , rove scrutinizingly over the church , then settle on our pew .
`` She 's come here , '' whisper Felicity in horror .
`` Ca n't we spread out and make her think the pew be full ? ''
But the manoeuvre be too late .
The only result be that Felicity and the Story Girl in move over leave a vacant space between them and Peg promptly plump down in it .
`` Well , I 'm here , '' she remark aloud .
`` I do say once I 'd never darken the door of Carlisle church again , but what that boy there '' -- nod at Peter -- `` say last winter set me thinking , and I conclude maybe I 'd well come once in a while , to be on the safe side . ''
Those poor girl be in an agony .
Everybody in the church be look at our pew and smiling .
We all felt that we be terribly disgrace ; but we could do nothing .
Peg be enjoy herself hugely , beyond all doubt .
From where she sit she could see the whole church , include pulpit and gallery , and her black eye dart over it with restless glance .
`` Bless me , there 's Sam Kinnaird , '' she exclaim , still aloud .
`` He 's the man that dun Jacob Marr for four cent on the church step one Sunday .
I hear him . '
I think , Jacob , you owe me four cent on that cow you buy last fall .
Rec ` llect you could n't make the change ? '
Well , you know , ` twould a-made a cat laugh .
The Kinnairds be all mighty close , I can tell you .
That 's how they get rich . ''
What Sam Kinnaird felt or think during this speech , which everyone in the church must have hear , I know not .
Gossip have it that he change colour .
We wretched occupant of the King pew be concern only with our own outraged feeling .
